I, i¹
/aɪ ||; aɪ/noun [C,U] (plural I's;i's /aɪz ||; aɪz/) the ninth letter of the English alphabet 英语字母表的第九个字母: ‘Island’ begins with (an) ‘I’. island以字母Ｉ开头。

*I²
/aɪ ||; aɪ/pronoun (the subject of a verb) the person who is speaking or writing （作动词的主语）我: I phoned and said that I was busy. 我打过电话说我没有空。 I'm not going to fall, am I? 我不会掉下去的，对吗？

iambic
/aɪˈæmbɪk ||; aɪˈæmbɪk/adj (technical术语) (used about rhythm in poetry) having one short or weak syllable followed by one long or strong syllable （指诗歌的韵律）抑扬格的,短长格的: a poem written in iambic pentameters (= in lines of ten syllables, five short and five long) 一首以抑扬格写的五音步诗

*ice¹
/aɪs ||; aɪs/noun [U] water that has frozen and become solid 冰: Do you want ice in your orange juice? 你的橙汁里要不要搁点冰？ I slipped on a patch of ice. 我踩在冰块上，滑倒了。 black ice (= ice on roads, that cannot be seen easily) 黑冰（结在马路上不易被察觉的冰） break the ice to say or do sth that makes people feel more relaxed, especially at the beginning of a party or meeting 使气氛活跃宽松（尤指聚会、会议开始时）: She smiled to break the ice. 她一笑就使气氛活跃起来。 cut no ice (with sb) to have no influence or effect on sb 没有影响；不起作用: His excuses cut no ice with me. 他的借口说服不了我。 on ice
1 (used about wine, etc) kept cold by being surrounded by ice （指酒等）冰镇的
2 (used about a plan, etc) waiting to be dealt with later; delayed （指计划等）暂搁着，以后再处理: We've had to put our plans to go to Australia on ice for the time being. 我们暂且得把澳大利亚之行的计划搁一搁。
ice²
/aɪs ||; aɪs/ (especially US 尤为美 frost) verb [T] to decorate a cake by covering it with a mixture of sugar, butter, chocolate, etc 往糕饼上撒（用糖、黄油、巧克力等混合而成的）糖霜 ☞Look at icing. 参看icing。 ice (sth) over/up to cover sth or become covered with ice 以冰覆盖…；被冰覆盖: The windscreen of the car had iced over in the night. 一夜之间，汽车的挡风玻璃上结满了冰。

/ˈaɪkɒn ||; ˈaɪkɑn/noun[C]

*idea
/aɪˈdɪə ||; aɪˈdɪə/noun
1 [C] an idea (for sth);an idea (of sth/of doing sth) a plan, thought or suggestion, especially about what to do in a particular situation 想法；主意；构想: That's a good idea! 好主意！ He's got an idea for a new play. 他构思了一出新戏。 I had the bright idea of getting Jane to help me with my homework. 我想出一个好主意，就是让简帮我做作业。 Has anyone got any ideas of how to tackle this problem? 有谁知道怎么解决这个问题？ It was your idea to invite so many people to the party. 邀请这么多人来聚会是你的主意。
2 [sing] an idea (of sth) a picture or impression in your mind 想法；印象: You have no idea (= you can't imagine) how difficult it was to find a time that suited everybody. 你有所不知，找一个适合大家的时间可不容易呀。 The programme gave a good idea of what life was like before the war. 这个节目使你对战前生活有清楚的了解。 Staying in to watch the football on TV is not my idea of a good time. 我觉得呆在家里看电视上转播的足球比赛没劲儿。
3 [C] an idea (about sth) an opinion or belief 意见；看法: She has her own ideas about how to bring up children. 在管教儿女方面，她有自己的主张。
4 the idea [sing] the idea (of sth/of doing sth) the aim or purpose of sth 目的: The idea of the course is to teach the basics of car maintenance. 这个课程的目的，就是让同学掌握汽车维修的基本知识。
get the idea to understand the aim or purpose of sth 明了（某事的目标或目的）: Right! I think I've got the idea now. 是啊！我想我如今明白了。 get the idea that... to get the feeling or impression that... 形成或得到…感觉或印象: Where did you get the idea that I was paying for this meal? 你怎么会以为这顿饭是由我来付钱的？ have an idea that... to have a feeling or think that... 觉得；认为: I'm not sure but I have an idea that they've gone on holiday. 我觉得他们度假去了，可是拿不准。 not have the faintest/foggiest (idea)→FAINT¹

*ideal¹
/aɪˈdi:əl ||; aɪˈdiəl/adj ideal (for sb/sth) the best possible; perfect 理想的；完美的: She's the ideal candidate for the job. 她是这份工作的理想人选。 In an ideal world there would be no poverty. 理想的世界里没有贫困。 It would be an ideal opportunity for you to practise your Spanish. 这将是你练习西班牙语的极好机会。
ideal²
/aɪˈdi:əl ||; aɪˈdiəl/noun[C]
1 an idea or principle that seems perfect to you and that you want to achieve 理想: She finds it hard to live up to her parents' high ideals. 她发觉很难实现她爸妈对她的期望。 political/moral/social ideals 政治╱道德╱社会理想
2 [usu.sing] an ideal (of sth) a perfect example of a person or thing 典范；完美的境地: It's my ideal of what a family home should be. 这就是我理想中的家。

idealism
/aɪˈdi:əlɪzəm ||; aɪˈdiəlˌɪzəm/noun [U] the belief that a perfect life, situation, etc can be achieved, even when this is not very likely 理想主义（认为完美的生活、境地等终可达到，即使不大可能）: Young people are usually full of idealism. 年轻人一般都充满理想主义。 ☞ Look at realism. 参看realism。 ➔idealist noun [C]: Most people are idealists when they are young. 人们年轻时大都是理想主义者。 ➔idealistic /ˌaɪdɪəˈlɪstɪk ||; aɪˌdɪəlˈɪstɪk/ adj

idealize
/aɪˈdi:əlaɪz ||; aɪˈdɪəlˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to imagine or show sb/sth as being better than he/she/it really is 理想化；美化: Old people often idealize the past. 老年人常常美化他们的过去。

ideally
/aɪˈdi:əli ||; aɪˈdiəlɪ/adv
1 perfectly 完美地: They are ideally suited to each other. 他们俩十分相配。
2 in an ideal situation 理想地: Ideally, no class should be larger than 25. 理想的安排是，每班不多于25人。

identical
/aɪˈdentɪkl ||; aɪˈdɛntɪkḷ/adj
1 identical (to/with sb/sth) exactly the same as; similar in every detail 完全相同的；一模一样的: I can't see any difference between these two pens -- they look identical to me. 这两支笔我看不出有什么分别，看上去完全一样。 That watch is identical to the one I lost yesterday. 这块表跟我昨天丢失的那块一模一样。
2 the identical (only before a noun 只用于名词前) the same 同一的；相同的: This is the identical room we stayed in last year. 这是我们去年住过的同一个房间。 ➔identically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

iˌdentical ˈtwin
noun [C] one of two children born at the same time from the same mother, and who are of the same sex and look very similar 全等双生（之一）；同卵双生（之一）

*identification
/aɪˌdentɪfɪˈkeɪʃn ||; aɪˌdɛntəfəˈkeʃən/noun[U] [C]
1 the process of showing, recognizing or giving proof of who or what sb/sth is 辨认；验明: The identification of the bodies of those killed in the explosion was very difficult. 爆炸事件死难者的尸体难以辨认。
2 (abbr ID) [U] an official paper, document, etc that is proof of who you are 身分证明文件: Do you have any identification? 你有没有身分证明文件？
3 identification (with sb/sth) a strong feeling of understanding or sharing the same feelings as sb/sth 对…怀有的同感；认同: children's identification with TV heroes 儿童对电视片英雄角色的认同

*identify
/aɪˈdentɪfaɪ ||; aɪˈdɛntəˌfaɪ/verb [T] (present participle identifying third person singular present identifies;past tense past participle identified)identify sb/sth (as sb/sth) to recognize or be able to say who or what sb/sth is 认出: The police need someone to identify the body. 警察须要有人出来辨认这具尸体。 We must identify the cause of the problem before we look for solutions. 我们必须先弄清问题的起因，然后再寻求解决的方法。 identify sth with sth to think or say that sth is the same as sth else 把…等同于…: You can't identify nationalism with fascism. 可不能把民族主义跟法西斯主义混为一谈。 identify with sb to feel that you understand and share what sb else is feeling 认同某人的感情: I found it hard to identify with the woman in the film. 电影里的那个妇人无法引起我的共鸣。 identify (yourself) with sb/sth to support or be closely connected with sb/sth 支持；与…有密切关系: She became identified with the new political party. 她支持那个新成立的政党。

*identity
/aɪˈdentəti ||; aɪˈdɛntətɪ/noun [C,U] (plural identities) who or what a person or a thing is 身分；特性: There are few clues to the identity of the killer. 关于杀人凶手的身分，线索并不多。 The region has its own cultural identity. 这个地区有自己的文化特色。 The arrest was a case of mistaken identity (= the wrong person was arrested). 这次逮捕行动抓错了人。

iˈdentity card
(also IˈD card) noun [C] a card with your name, photograph, etc that is proof of who you are 身分证

ideology
/ˌaɪdiˈɒlədʒi ||; ˌaɪdɪˈɑlədʒɪ/noun [C,U] (plural ideologies) a set of ideas which form the basis for a political or economic system （政治或经济制度赖以建立的）意识形态，思想体系: Marxist ideology 马克思主义思想体系 ➔ideological /ˌaɪdiəˈlɒdʒɪkl ||; ˌaɪdɪəˈlɑdʒɪkḷ/ adj

idiom
/ˈɪdiəm ||; ˈɪdɪəm/noun [C] an expression whose meaning is different from the meanings of the individual words in it 习语；惯用语；成语: The idiom ‘bring sth home to sb’ means ‘make sb understand sth’. bring sth home to sb这个习语的意思是“使人明白某事物”。

idiomatic
/ˌɪdiəˈmætɪk ||; ˌɪdɪəˈmætɪk/adj
1 using language that contains expressions that are natural to sb who learned the language as a child 合乎语言习惯的；用法地道的: He speaks good idiomatic English. 他的英语说得很地道。
2 containing an idiom 含有习语的: an idiomatic expression 惯用语

idiosyncrasy
/ˌɪdiəˈsɪŋkrəsi ||; ˌɪdɪəˈsɪŋkrəsɪ/noun [C,U] (plural idiosyncrasies) a person's particular way of behaving, thinking, etc, especially when it is unusual; an unusual characteristic 习性，癖好（尤指不寻常的）；不平常的特点 [SYN] eccentricity 同义词为eccentricity Eating garlic every morning is one of his idiosyncrasies. 他的癖好之一是每天早上吃蒜。 The car has its little idiosyncrasies. 这辆车有几个小特点。 ➔idiosyncratic /ˌɪdiəsɪŋˈkrætɪk ||; ˌɪdɪosɪŋˈkrætɪk/ His teaching methods are idiosyncratic but successful. 他的教学方法别树一帜，但很成功。

idiot
/ˈɪdiət ||; ˈɪdɪət/noun [C] (informal 非正式) a very stupid person 笨蛋；白痴: I was an idiot to forget my passport. 我真胡涂，竟忘了带护照。 ➔idiotic /ˌɪdiˈɒtɪk ||; ˌɪdɪˈɑtɪk/ adj ➔ idiotically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

idle
/ˈaɪdl ||; ˈaɪdḷ/adj
1 not wanting to work hard; lazy 懒散的: He has the ability to succeed but he is just bone (= very) idle. 他有能力做得到，可就是懒骨头，不肯做。
2 not doing anything; not being used 闲散的；闲置的: She can't bear to be idle. 她这个人闲不下来。 The factory stood idle while the machines were being repaired. 机器进行维修时，工厂停工。
3 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) not to be taken seriously because it will not have any result 不必认真对待的: an idle promise/threat 信口许下的诺言；随便说说吓唬人的话 idle chatter/curiosity 随便说说；随便打听 ➔idleness noun [U] ➔idly /ˈaɪdli ||; ˈaɪdlɪ/ adv

idol
/ˈaɪdl ||; ˈaɪdḷ/noun[C]
1 a person (such as a film star or pop musician) who is admired or loved 崇拜对象，偶像（如电影明星、流行乐手）: a pop/football/teen/screen idol 流行音乐╱足球╱青少年╱银幕偶像
2 a statue that people treat as a god 神像；偶像

idolize
/ˈaɪdəlaɪz ||; ˈaɪdḷˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to love or admire sb very much or too much 崇拜；极度喜爱或仰慕: He is an only child and his parents idolize him. 他是独子，父母对他十分溺爱。

idyllic
/ɪˈdɪlɪk; US aɪˈd- ||; aɪˈdɪlɪk/adj very pleasant and peaceful; perfect 怡人的；平和的: an idyllic holiday 诗情画意的假期

i.e.
/ˌaɪ ˈi: ||; ˌaɪ ˈi/abbr that is; in other words 即是；换言之: deciduous trees, i.e. those which lose their leaves in autumn 落叶树，即在秋天落叶的树木

*if
/ɪf ||; ɪf/ conj
1 used in sentences in which one thing only happens or is true when another thing happens or is true 如果；假如；要是: If you see him, give him this letter. 你看到他的话，把这封信交给他。 We won't go to the beach if it rains. 要是下雨，我们就不去海滩了。 If I had more time, I would learn another language. 如果有时间，我会再学一种语言。 I might see her tomorrow. If not, I'll see her at the weekend. 我明天或许会见到她，要不就会在周末见到。
2 when; every time 当；每次: If I try to phone her she just hangs up. 每次我给她打电话，她都把电话挂断。 If metal gets hot it expands. 金属遇热就膨胀。
3 used after verbs such as ‘ask’, ‘know’, ‘remember’ （用于ask、know、remember等动词之后）是否: They asked if we would like to go too. 他们问我们是不是也想去。 I can't remember if I posted the letter or not. 这封信我记不清寄了没有。 ☞Look at the note at whether. 参看whether的注释。
4 used when you are asking sb to do sth or suggesting sth politely （用于礼貌的请求或建议）: If you could just come this way, sir. 先生，请跟我来。 If I might suggest something... 我想提个建议…
as if→AS even if→EVEN² if I were you used when you are giving sb advice （用于提出忠告）: If I were you, I'd leave now. 我要是你，现在就走。 if it wasn't/weren't for sb/sth if a particular person or situation did not exist or was not there; without sb/sth 要不是；若非: If it wasn't for him, I wouldn't stay in this country. 要不是因为他，我不会待在这个国家。 if only used for expressing a strong wish （用于表达殷切的愿望）: If only I could drive. 我会开车就好了。 If only he'd write. 要是他写信给我就好了。

igloo
/ˈɪglu: ||; ˈɪglu/noun [C] (plural igloos) a small house that is built from blocks of hard snow 伊格鲁（用坚硬雪块盖的小屋）；圆顶冰屋

igneous
/ˈɪgniəs ||; ˈɪgnɪəs/adj (technical术语) (used about rocks 指岩石) formed when MAGMA (= melted or liquid material from below the earth's surface) comes out of a VOLCANO and becomes solid 火成的 ☞Compare metamorphic and sedimentary. 与metamorphic及sedimentary比较。 ☞picture at rock 见rock插图

ignite
/ɪgˈnaɪt ||; ɪgˈnaɪt/verb [I,T] (formal 正式) to start burning or to make sth start burning 点燃；（使）着火 · A spark from the engine ignited the petrol. 引擎的火花点燃了汽油。

ignition
/ɪgˈnɪʃn ||; ɪgˈnɪʃən/noun
1 [C] the electrical system that starts the engine of a car （启动汽车引擎的）点火装置: to turn the ignition on/off 开╱关点火装置 First of all, put the key in the ignition. 首先把钥匙插进点火装置。 ☞picture at car 见car插图
2 [U] the action of starting to burn or making sth start to burn 着火；点火

ignominious
/ˌɪgnəˈmɪniəs ||; ˌɪgnəˈmɪnɪəs/adj (formal 正式) making you feel embarrassed 令人丢脸的: The team suffered an ignominious defeat. 这支球队打了一场不光彩的败仗。 ➔ignominiously adv

ignorance
/ˈɪgnərəns ||; ˈɪgnərəns/noun [U]: ignorance (of/about sth) a lack of information or knowledge （对某事）缺乏认识，无知: The workers were in complete ignoranceof the management's plans. 工人对资方的计划一无所知。

ignorant
/ˈɪgnərənt ||; ˈɪgnərənt/adj
1 ignorant (of/about sth) not knowing about sth 不知道的；无知的: Many people are ignorant of their rights. 很多人不知道自己的权利。
2 (informal 非正式) having or showing bad manners 莽撞的；无礼的: an ignorant person/remark 鲁莽的人；无礼的话

*ignore
/ɪgˈnɔ:(r) ||; ɪgˈnɔr/verb [T] to pay no attention to sb/sth 不理；忽视: I said hello to Debbie but she totally ignored me (= acted as though she hadn't seen me). 我跟戴比打招呼，可她理也不理。 Alison ignored her doctor's advice about drinking and smoking less. 医生叫艾莉森少喝酒，少抽烟，她就是不听。 Be careful. Ignore and be ignorant are different in meaning. 注意：ignore和be ignorant的意思不同。

*ill¹
/ɪl ||; ɪl/adj
1 (US 美 sick) (not before a noun 不用于名词前) not in good health; not well 生病；身体不适: I can't drink milk because it makes me feel ill. 我不能喝牛奶，一喝就觉得难受。 My mother was taken ill suddenly last week. 妈妈上个礼拜突然病了。 My grandfather is seriously ill in hospital. 爷爷躺在医院里，病得很厉害。 ☞Look at the note at sick. 参看sick的注释。
2 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) bad or harmful 坏的；有害的: He resigned because of ill health. 他因为身体不好，辞职了。 I'm glad to say I suffered no ill effects from all that rich food. 虽然我吃了那么油腻的东西，可庆幸什么事也没有。 ☞noun illness 名词为illness

I'll
/aɪl ||; aɪl/ short forI WILL, I SHALL
ill²
/ɪl ||; ɪl/adv
1 (often in compounds 常用于构成复合词) badly or wrongly 恶劣地；错误地: You would be ill-advised to drive until you have fully recovered. 除非你完全康复，否则不该开车。
2 only with difficulty; not easily 困难地: They could ill afford the extra money for better heating. 好一点的暖气设备要额外开支，他们负担不起。
augur well/ill for sb/sth→AUGUR bode well/ill (for sb/sth)→BODE

*illegal
/ɪˈli:gl ||; ɪˈligḷ/adj not allowed by the law 非法的: It is illegal to own a gun without a special licence. 没有特别的执照拥有枪械是非法的。 illegal drugs/immigrants/activities 非法毒品╱移民╱活动 [OPP] legal 反义词为legal [SYN]a more formal word is unlawful. 较正式的用语为unlawful。 ➔illegally /-gəli ||; -gḷɪ/ adv

illegality
/ˌɪliˈgæləti ||; ˌɪliˈgælətɪ/noun (plural illegalities)
1 [U] the state of being illegal 违法；非法；不合法: No illegality is suspected. 没有非法的嫌疑。
2 [C] an illegal act 非法行为 ☞Compare legality. 与legality比较。

illegible
/ɪˈledʒəbl ||; ɪˈlɛdʒəbḷ/adj difficult or impossible to read 难以辨认的: Your handwriting is quite illegible. 你的字迹相当潦草。 [OPP] legible 反义词为legible ➔illegibly /-əblɪ ||; -əblɪ/ adv

illegitimate
/ˌɪləˈdʒɪtəmət ||; ˌɪlɪˈdʒɪtəmɪt/adj

2 not allowed by law; against the rules 非法的；违规的: the illegitimate use of company money 挪用公司款项 [OPP] legitimate 反义词为legitimate ➔illegitimacy /ˌɪləˈdʒɪtəməsi ||; ˌɪlɪˈdʒɪtəməsɪ/ noun [U]

ˌill-ˈfated

illicit
/ɪˈlɪsɪt ||; ɪˈlɪsɪt/adj (used about an activity or substance) not allowed by law or by the rules of society （指活动或物质）违法的，违禁的: the illicit trade in ivory 非法的象牙贸易 They were having an illicit affair. 他们俩有奸情。

illiterate
/ɪˈlɪtərət ||; ɪˈlɪtərɪt/adj

*illness
/ˈɪlnəs ||; ˈɪlnɪs/noun
1 [U] the state of being physically or mentally ill （身体或精神）有病: He's missed a lot of school through illness. 他因为生病缺了好多课。 There is a history of mental illness in the family. 这个家族有精神病史。
2 [C] a type or period of physical or mental ill health （身体或精神方面的）疾病，患病期间: minor/serious/childhood illnesses 小病；重病；小儿疾病 My dad is just getting over his illness. 我的爸爸病后刚刚痊愈。 ☞adjective ill 形容词为ill ☞ Look at the note at disease. 参看disease的注释。

illogical
/ɪˈlɒdʒɪkl ||; ɪˈlɑdʒɪkḷ/adj not sensible or reasonable 不理智的；不合理的；不合逻辑的: It seems illogical to me to pay somebody to do work that you could do yourself. 自己做得来的事情还要花钱叫别人做，我以为似乎没有道理。 [OPP] logical 反义词为logical ➔illogicality /ɪˌlɒdʒɪˈkæləti ||; ɪˌlɑdʒɪˈkælətɪ/ noun [C,U] (plural illogicalities) ➔illogically /-kli/ adv

ˌill-ˈtreat
verb [T] to treat sb/sth badly or in an unkind way 虐待；折磨: This cat has been ill-treated. 这只猫受到虐待。 ➔ˌill-ˈtreatment noun [U]

illuminate
/ɪˈlu:mɪneɪt ||; ɪˈluməˌnet/verb [T] (formal 正式)
1 to shine light on sth or to decorate sth with lights 照亮；用灯装饰: The palace was illuminated by spotlights. 聚光灯把皇宫照得通亮。

/ɪˈlu:mɪneɪtɪŋ ||; ɪˈluməˌnetɪŋ/adj helping to explain sth or make sth clear 有助阐释的；有启发作用的: an illuminating discussion 使人大开眼界的讨论

illumination
/ɪˌlu:mɪˈneɪʃn ||; ɪˌluməˈneʃən/noun
1 [U] [C] light or the place where a light comes from 光线；采光: These big windows give good illumination. 有了这些大窗户，光线真不错。

illusion
/ɪˈlu:ʒn ||; ɪˈluʒən/noun
1 [C,U] a false idea, belief or impression 虚幻的观念；幻想；幻觉: I have no illusions about the situation -- I know it's serious. 我知道形势严峻，对它不存幻想。 I think Peter's under the illusion that he will be the new director. 我想彼得误以为自己是下一任的董事长。
2 [C] something that your eyes tell you is there or is true but in fact is not 错觉: That line looks longer, but in fact they're the same length. It's an optical illusion. 那条线看上去长一点，其实两条线都一样长，这是视错觉使然。

illusory
/ɪˈlu:səri ||; ɪˈlusərɪ/adj (formal 正式) not real, although seeming to be 虚假的；幻觉的: The profits they had hoped for proved to be illusory. 他们指望实现的利润证明是不切实际的。

*illustrate

1 to explain or make sth clear by using examples, pictures or diagrams 用例子、图片或图表说明: These statistics illustrate the point that I was making very well. 这些统计资料把我要说的都说清楚了。
2 to add pictures, diagrams, etc to a book or magazine （为书或杂志）加插图: Most cookery books are illustrated. 大部份烹饪书籍都附有插图。

illustration
/ˌɪləˈstreɪʃn ||; ˌɪləsˈtreʃən/noun

3 [C] an example that makes a point or an idea clear 例证: Can you give me an illustration of what you mean? 可不可以举例说明你的意思？

*image
/ˈɪmɪdʒ ||; ˈɪmɪdʒ/noun[C]
1 the general impression that a person or organization gives to the public （某人或组织给公众留下的）总体印象，形象: When you meet him, he's very different from his public image. 你当面见他的时候，会发现他跟在公众场合的形象有很大不同。
2 a mental picture or idea of sb/sth 脑海里的形象；印象: I have an image of my childhood as always sunny and happy. 我脑海中的童年总是快乐无忧的。
3 a picture or description that appears in a book, film or painting （书本、电影或图画里的）图像，描述: horrific images of war 触目惊心的战争图片
4 a copy or picture of sb/sth seen in a mirror, through a camera, on television, computer, etc 副本；影像；映像: A perfect image of the building was reflected in the lake. 湖水映着这座楼房的清晰倒影。 (figurative 比喻) He's the (spitting) image of his father (= he looks exactly like him). 他长得跟他爸爸一个模样。

imagery
/ˈɪmɪdʒəri ||; ˈɪmɪdʒərɪ/noun [U] language that produces pictures in the minds of the people reading or listening 形象化描述；意象: poetic imagery 诗歌的意象

imaginable
/ɪˈmædʒɪnəbl ||; ɪˈmædʒɪnəbḷ/adj that you can imagine 想象得出的；可以想象的: Sophie made all the excuses imaginable when she was caught stealing. 索菲行窃当场被捉，她找出各种各样的借口来辩解。 His house was equipped with every imaginable luxury. 他这座房子极尽奢华之能事。

*imaginary
/ɪˈmædʒɪnəri; US -ənerɪ ||; ɪˈmædʒəˌnɛrɪ/adj existing only in the mind; not real 假想的；虚构的: Many children have imaginary friends. 很多孩子心里都有假想的朋友。

*imagination
/ɪˌmædʒɪˈneɪʃn ||; ɪˌmædʒəˈneʃən/noun
1 [U] [C] the ability to create mental pictures or new ideas 想象力: He has a lively imagination. 他有丰富的想象力。 She's very clever but she doesn't have much imagination. 她这个人虽然很聪明，可是没什么想象力。
Imagination is a creative quality that a person has. Fantasy refers to thoughts, stories, etc that are not related to reality. 想象叫imagination。幻想叫fantasy。
2 [C] the part of the mind that uses this ability 想象: If you use your imagination, you should be able to guess the answer. 只要动动脑筋，你就能猜出答案。 ➔imaginatively adv

imaginative
/ɪˈmædʒɪnətɪv ||; ɪˈmædʒəˌnetɪv/adj having or showing imagination 富有╱表现出想象力: She's always full of imaginative ideas. 她总是充满新奇的念头。

*imagine
/ɪˈmædʒɪn ||; ɪˈmædʒɪn/verb[T]
1 imagine that...;imagine sb/sth (doing/as sth) to form a picture or idea in your mind of what sth/sb might be like 想象: Imagine that you're lying on a beach. 想象一下你躺在海滩上。 It's not easy to imagine your brother as a doctor. 很难想象你哥哥是当医生的。 I can't imagine myself cycling 20 miles a day. 我无法想象自己会每天骑自行车跑20英里。
2 to see, hear or think sth that is not true or does not exist 幻想: She's always imagining that she's ill but she's fine really. 她老以为自己有病，其实她身体挺不错。 I thought I heard someone downstairs, but I must have been imagining things. 我好像听到楼下有人，不过准是幻觉罢了。
3 to think that sth is probably true; to suppose 认为；以为: I imagine he'll be coming by car. 我想他会开车来的。

2 to copy the speech or actions of sb/sth, often in order to make people laugh 模仿别人的言谈举止（常为了逗人发笑）: She could imitate her mother perfectly. 她学起她妈妈来倒是维妙维肖。

immature
/ˌɪməˈtjʊə(r); US -tʊər ||; ˌɪməˈtυr/adj
1 not fully grown or developed 发育未全的；不成熟的: an immature body 发育未全的身躯
2 (used about a person) behaving in a way that is not sensible and is typical of people who are much younger （指人）幼稚的（头脑简单，处事方法欠成熟）: I think he's too immature to take his work seriously. 我认为他还很幼稚，不会认真对待工作。 [OPP] mature 反义词为mature

immeasurable
/ɪˈmeʒərəbl ||; ɪˈmɛʒərəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) too large, great, etc to be measured （大得）不可计量的；无限的: to cause immeasurable harm 造成巨大的伤害 Her contribution was of immeasurable importance. 他的贡献极其重要。 ➔immeasurably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv Housing standards have improved immeasurably since the war. 战后住房标准已经大大提高。

immediacy
/ɪˈmi:diəsi ||; ɪˈmidɪəsɪ/noun [U] the quality of being available or seeming to happen close to you and without delay 实时性；直接性: Letters do not have the same immediacy as email. 书信不如电子邮件那样快捷。

*immediate
/ɪˈmi:diət ||; ɪˈmidɪɪt/adj
1 happening or done without delay 立即的；实时的: I'd like an immediate answer to my proposal. 关于我的建议，我想尽快得到答复。 The government responded with immediate action. 政府马上采取行动。
2 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) existing now and needing urgent attention 当前的；紧迫的: Tell me what your immediate needs are. 你急需什么可以告诉我。
3 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) nearest in time, position or relationship （时间、位置或关系上）最接近的: They won't make any changes in the immediate future. 他们在短期内不会作出任何变动。 He has left most of his money to his immediate family (= parents, children, brothers and sisters). 他把大部份钱都留给了直系亲属。

immediately
/ɪˈmi:diətli ||; ɪˈmidɪɪtlɪ/adv conj
1 at once; without delay 马上；立刻: Can you come home immediately after work? 你下班后可以马上回家吗？ I couldn't immediately see what he meant. 我一时摸不清楚他的意思。
2 very closely; directly 很密切；直接: He wasn't immediately involved in the crime. 他跟这项罪行没有直接牵连。
3 nearest in time or position （时间或位置上）最接近: Who's the girl immediately in front of Simon? 紧邻在西蒙前面的那个女孩子是谁？ What did you do immediately after the war? 战事刚刚结束的时候，你做什么来着？
4 (Brit 英) as soon as 一…就…: I opened the letter immediately I got home. 我一回到家就把信拆开。

immense
/ɪˈmens ||; ɪˈmɛns/adj very big or great 重大的；巨大的: immense difficulties/importance/power 重大的困难；无比的重要性；巨大的权力 She gets immense pleasure from her garden. 她的花园带给她莫大的乐趣。

immensely
/ɪˈmensli ||; ɪˈmɛnslɪ/adv extremely; very much 极度；非常: immensely enjoyable 趣味无穷 ‘Did you enjoy the party?’ ‘Yes, immensely.’ “这个舞会你玩得开心吗？”“开心极了。”

immensity
/ɪˈmensəti ||; ɪˈmɛnsətɪ/noun [U] an extremely large size 巨大；广大: the immensity of the universe 宇宙的浩瀚

immerse
/ɪˈmɜ:s ||; ɪˈmɝs/verb[T]
1 immerse sth (in sth) to put sth into a liquid so that it is covered 浸，泡（在液体中）: Make sure the spaghetti is fully immersed in the boiling water. 意大利面条要全部泡在沸水里煮。
2 immerse yourself (in sth) to involve yourself completely in sth so that you give it all your attention 醉心于，沉浸于，沉迷于（某事物）: Rachel's usually immersed in a book. 雷切尔常常手不释卷。

immersion
/ɪˈmɜ:ʃn ||; ɪˈmɝʒən/noun [U]:
1 immersion (in sth) the act of putting sb/sth into a liquid so that he/she/it is completely covered; the state of being completely covered by a liquid 沉浸；浸没: Immersion in cold water resulted in rapid loss of heat. 浸入冷水就很快冷却。
2 immersion (in sth) the state of being completely involved in sth 陷入；专心: a two-week immersion course in French (= in which the student hears and uses only French) 两星期的法语强化课程

*immigrant
/ˈɪmɪgrənt ||; ˈɪməgrənt/noun [C] a person who has come into a foreign country to live there permanently （外来）移民: The government plans to tighten controls to prevent illegal immigrants. 政府打算加强控制，防止非法移民进入。 London has a high immigrant population. 伦敦住了大量移民。 Great Britain has many immigrant communities which make it a multicultural society. Groups of immigrants or children of immigrants who share a common cultural tradition form an ethnic minority. 英国有很多移民族群，使其成为一个多元文化社会(multicultural society)。有共同文化传统的移民及其子女构成一个少数族裔(ethnic minority)。

*immigration
/ˌɪmɪˈgreɪʃn ||; ˌɪməˈgreʃən/noun [U]:
1 the process of coming to live permanently in a country that is not your own; the number of people who do this 移民: There are greater controls on immigration than there used to be. 现在对外来移民的管制比过去严格。
2 (also immiˈgration control) the control point at an airport, port, etc where the official documents of people who want to come into a country are checked 入境检查站: When you leave the plane you have to go through customs and immigration. 下机后得办理过关及入境手续。
There is a verb ‘immigrate’ but it is very rarely used. We normally use the expression ‘be an immigrant’ or the verb ‘emigrate’ which is used in connection with the place that somebody has come from My parents emigrated to this country from Jamaica. immigrate这个动词很少用。一般用be an immigrant，也可以说从某地emigrate：My parents emigrated to this country from Jamaica. 我父母从牙买加移居这个国家。 Look at emigrate, emigrant and emigration. 参看emigrate、emigrant及emigration。
imminent
/ˈɪmɪnənt ||; ˈɪmənənt/adj (usually used about sth unpleasant) almost certain to happen very soon （通常指令人不快的事情）即将发生的: Heavy rainfall means that flooding is imminent. 连场暴雨预示着马上要发洪水。 ➔imminently adv

immiscible
/ɪˈmɪsəbl ||; ɪˈmɪsəbḷ/adj (technical术语) (used about liquids) that cannot be mixed together （指液体）不能混合的 [OPP] miscible 反义词为miscible

immobile
/ɪˈməʊbaɪl; US -bl ||; ɪˈmobḷ/adj not moving or not able to move 静止不动的；不能移动的: The hunter stood immobile until the lion had passed. 猎人一动不动地站着，直到狮子走过去。 [OPP] mobile 反义词为mobile ➔immobility /ˌɪməˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪmoˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

immobilize
/ɪˈməʊbəlaɪz ||; ɪˈmobḷˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to prevent sb/sth from moving or working normally 使不能正常活动或运作: The railways have been completely immobilized by the strike. 这次工潮使铁路完全瘫痪。 This device immobilizes the car to prevent it being stolen. 这种装置使汽车无法动弹，免被人偷走。 [OPP] mobilize 反义词为mobilize

immobilizer
/ɪˈməʊbəlaɪzə ||; ɪˈmobḷˌaɪzɚ/ (also -iser) a device in a vehicle that prevents thieves from starting the engine when the vehicle is parked 汽车防盗装置

immoral
/ɪˈmɒrəl; US ɪˈmɔ:rəl ||; ɪˈmɔrəl/ (used about people or their behaviour) considered wrong or not honest by most people （指人或其行为）不道德的: It's immoral to steal. 偷窃是不道德行为。 [OPP] moral 反义词为moral ☞Compare amoral. 与amoral比较。 ➔immorality /ˌɪməˈræləti ||; ˌɪməˈrælətɪ/ noun [U] [OPP] morality 反义词为morality ➔immorally /-rəli ||; -rəlɪ/ adv

immortal
/ɪˈmɔ:tl ||; ɪˈmɔrtḷ/adj living or lasting for ever 永生的；不朽的: Nobody is immortal -- we all have to die some time. 人的生命有限，总免不了一死。 [OPP] mortal 反义词为mortal ➔immortality /ˌɪmɔ:ˈtæləti ||; ˌɪmɔrˈtælətɪ/ noun [U]

immortalize
/ɪˈmɔ:təlaɪz ||; ɪˈmɔrtḷˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to give lasting fame to sb/sth 使不朽；使流芳百世: He immortalized their relationship in a poem. 他把他们的关系写进诗篇，使其永垂千古。

immune
/ɪˈmju:n ||; ɪˈmjun/adj
1 immune (to sth) having natural protection against a certain disease or illness 有免疫力: You should be immune to measles if you've had it already. 如果你得过痲疹，对这种病就有免疫力。
2 immune (to sth) not affected by sth 不受（某事物）影响: You can say what you like -- I'm immune to criticism! 你有什么话只管说，批评伤不了我。
3 immune (from sth) protected from a danger or punishment 免受（危险或惩罚）: Young children are immune from prosecution. 幼童免受检控。

immunity
/ɪˈmju:nəti ||; ɪˈmjunətɪ/noun [U] the ability to avoid or not be affected by disease, criticism, punishment by law, etc 免疫力；豁免权: In many countries people have no immunity to diseases like measles. 许多国家的人对痲疹这类疾病没有免疫力。 Ambassadors to other countries receive diplomatic immunity (= protection from prosecution, etc). 驻外大使享有外交豁免权（免受司法起诉等）。

immunize
/ˈɪmjʊnaɪz ||; ˈɪmjυˌnaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to make sb immune to a disease, usually by putting a substance (vaccine) into his/her body 使免疫: Before visiting certain countries you will need to be immunized against cholera. 到某些国家之前，需要注射霍乱疫苗。 [SYN] Inoculate and vaccinate have similar meanings. inoculate和vaccinate意思相近。 ➔immunization(also -isation) /ˌɪmjʊnaɪˈzeɪʃn; US -nɪˈz- ||; ˌɪmjυnəˈzeʃən/ noun [C,U]

*impact
/ˈɪmpækt ||; ˈɪmpækt/noun
1 [C] [usu.sing] an impact (on/upon sb/sth) an effect or impression 影响；印象: I hope this anti-smoking campaign will make/have an impact on young people. 我希望这场反吸烟运动能对年轻人产生影响。
2 [U] the action or force of one object hitting another 撞击: The impact of the crash threw the passengers out of their seats. 这下撞击的冲力把乘客抛离了座位。 The bomb exploded on impact. 炸弹受到碰撞就马上爆炸了。

impair
/ɪmˈpeə(r) ||; ɪmˈpɛr/verb [T] to damage sth or make it weaker 损害；使减弱: Ear infections can result in impaired hearing. 耳朵感染可能导致听觉受损。

impaired
/ɪmˈpeəd ||; ɪmˈpɛrd/adj
1 damaged or not functioning normally 受损的；损坏的: impaired vision/memory 受损的视力/记忆
2 -impaired having the type of physical or mental problem mentioned 有缺陷的；有…障碍的: hearing-impaired children 听力受损的儿童 Nowadays we say someone is ‘hearing-impaired’, not deaf. 现在我们说某个人“有听力障碍”，而不说聋子。

impairment

impart
/ɪmˈpɑ:t ||; ɪmˈpɑrt/verb [T] (formal 正式)
1 impart sth (to sb) to pass information, knowledge, etc to other people （把信息、知识等）传给别人: He rushed home eager to impart the good news. 他赶回家里宣布好消息。
2 impart sth (to sth) to give a certain quality to sth 使（某事物）具有某种特性: The low lighting imparted a romantic atmosphere to the room. 昏暗的灯光给房间添上浪漫气氛。

*impatient

1 impatient (at sth/with sb) not able to stay calm and wait for sb/sth; easily annoyed by sb/sth that seems slow 不耐烦的: The passengers are getting impatient at the delay. 乘客对这次延误越来越不耐烦。 It's no good being impatient with small children. 对小孩子光着急没有用。 [OPP] patient 反义词为patient
2 impatient for/to do sth wanting sth to happen soon 迫不及待: By the time they are sixteen many young people are impatient to leave school. 很多年轻人满十六岁时都迫不及待要离开学校。 ➔impatience noun [U]: He began to explain for the third time with growing impatience. 他开始作第三次解释的时候，就越来越不耐烦了。 ➔impatiently adv

implication
/ˌɪmplɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ˌɪmplɪˈkeʃən/noun
1 [C] [usu.pl] implications (for/of sth) the effect that sth will have on sth else in the future 对另一事物将会产生的影响: The new law will have serious implicationsfor our work. 新法例将对我们的工作有重大影响。
2 [C,U] something that is suggested or said indirectly 暗示: The implication of what she said was that we had made a bad mistake. 她言下之意是我们犯了大错误。 ☞verb imply 动词为imply
3 [U] implication (in sth) the fact of being involved, or of involving sb, in sth unpleasant, especially a crime 牵连或卷入（尤指罪行）: The player's implication in this scandal could affect his career. 该选手跟这宗丑闻有牵连，他的前程可能因此受到影响。 ☞verb implicate 动词为implicate

/ɪmˈplɪsɪt ||; ɪmˈplɪsɪt/adj

*important
/ɪmˈpɔ:tnt ||; ɪmˈpɔrtṇt/adj
1 important (to sb);important (for sb/sth) (to do sth);important that... having great value or influence; very necessary 重要的；必要的: an important meeting/decision/factor 重要会议╱决定╱因素 This job is very important to me. 这份工作对我很重要。 It's important not to be late. 千万不可迟到。 It's important for people to see the results of what they do. 每个人都必须清楚自己所作所为的后果。 It was important to me that you were there. 你当时在场对我来说很重要。
2 (used about a person) having great influence or authority （指人）有影响的，有权力的: He was one of the most important writers of his time. 他是他那个年代最重要的作家之一。 ➔importantly adv

impose
/ɪmˈpəʊz ||; ɪmˈpoz/verb
1 [T] impose sth (on/upon sb/sth) to make a law, rule, opinion, etc be accepted by using your power or authority 将（法律、规定、意见等）强加于某人: A new tax will be imposed on cigarettes. 当局将对香烟征收新税。 Parents should try not to impose their own ideas on their children. 父母应避免把自己的想法强加给孩子。
2 [I] impose (on/upon sb/sth) to ask or expect sb to do sth that may cause extra work or trouble 要求或指望某人（做可能带来额外负担或麻烦的事）: I hate to impose on you, but can you lend me some money? 我实在不想麻烦你，可是你借点钱给我好吗？ ➔imposition /ˌɪmpəˈzɪʃn ||; ˌɪmpəˈzɪʃən/ noun [U] [C]: the imposition of military rule 强制实行军人统治

imposing
/ɪmˈpəʊzɪŋ ||; ɪmˈpozɪŋ/adj big and important; impressive 壮观的；给人深刻印象的: They lived in a large, imposing house near the park. 他们住在公园附近一座宏伟的房子里。

*impossible
/ɪmˈpɒsəbl ||; ɪmˈpɑsəbḷ/adj
1 not able to be done or to happen 不可能的: It's impossible for me to be there before 12. 12点之前我可赶不到那儿。 I find it almost impossible to get up in the morning! 我早上差点起不了床！ That's impossible! (= I don't believe it!) 不可能！
2 very difficult to deal with or control 难以应付的；无法控制的: This is an impossible situation! 这真是个无法对付的局面！ He's always been an impossible child. 他一直是个无可救药的顽童。 [OPP] possible 反义词为possible ➔the impossible noun [sing] Don't attempt the impossible! 别做办不到的事情！ ➔impossibility /ɪmˌpɒsəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪmpɑsəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [C,U] (plural impossibilities) What you are suggesting is a complete impossibility! 你这个建议完全行不通！

impossibly
/ɪmˈpɒsəbli ||; ɪmˈpɑsəblɪ/adv extremely 极度: impossibly complicated 极为复杂

impostor
/ɪmˈpɒstə(r) ||; ɪmˈpɑstɚ/noun [C] a person who pretends to be sb else in order to trick other people 冒充他人行骗者；骗子

impotent
/ˈɪmpətənt ||; ˈɪmpətənt/adj
1 without enough power to influence a situation or to change things 无能为力的
2 (medical医学) (used about men) not capable of having sex （指男性）阳痿的，性无能的 ➔impotence noun [U]

impound
/ɪmˈpaʊnd ||; ɪmˈpaund/verb [T] to take sth and lock it up so that it cannot be used, or so that it can be kept for its owner 暂时没收；扣押；收押: Illegally parked cars will be impounded. 违章停放的车将被扣押。 Animals that have been impounded can be reclaimed by their owners between 9 a.m. and 5 p.m. 被收押的动物可由其主人在上午 9 点至下午 5 点间前来领取。

impoverish
/ɪmˈpɒvərɪʃ ||; ɪmˈpɑvərɪʃ/verb [T] (formal 正式) to make sb/sth poor or lower in quality 使贫困；使降低质量 [OPP] enrich 反义词为enrich

impractical
/ɪmˈpræktɪkl ||; ɪmˈpræktɪkḷ/adj
1 not sensible or realistic 不切实际的: It would be impractical to take our bikes on the train. 把我们的自行车搬上火车是行不通的。
2 (used about a person) not good at doing ordinary things that involve using your hands; not good at organizing or planning things （指人）做不了事情的，无办事能力的: He's clever but completely impractical. 他虽然聪明，但无办事能力。 [OPP] practical 反义词为practical

imprecise
/ˌɪmprɪˈsaɪs ||; ˌɪmprɪˈsaɪs/adj not clear or exact 不清楚的；不精确的: imprecise instructions 不明确的指示 [OPP] precise 反义词为precise

*impress
/ɪmˈpres ||; ɪmˈprɛs/verb[T]
1 impress sb (with sth);impress sb that... to make sb feel admiration and respect 令人称羡；令人尊重: She's always trying to impress people with her new clothes. 她老是想以新衣服引人注意。 It impressed me that he understood immediately what I meant. 我一说他就明白了，真叫我佩服。
2 (formal 正式)impress sth on/upon sb to make the importance of sth very clear to sb 使某人清楚某事的重要性: I wish you could impress on John that he must pass these exams. 我希望你能让约翰明白，这些考试他必须通过。

*impression
/ɪmˈpreʃn ||; ɪmˈprɛʃən/noun[C]
1 an idea, a feeling or an opinion that you get about sb/sth 想法；感觉；看法: What's your first impression of the new director? 你对新董事长的第一个感觉如何？ I'm not sure but I have/get the impression that Jane's rather unhappy. 我感觉到珍不大高兴，可是我也拿不准。 I was under the impression (= I believed, but I was wrong) that you were married. 我以为你已经结婚。
2 the effect that a person or thing produces on sb else 印象: She gives the impression of being older than she really is. 她看起来比实际年龄大。 Do you think I made a good impression on your parents? 你认为我有没有给你父母留下好印象？
3 an amusing copy of the way a person acts or speaks; an imitation 滑稽模仿；模仿: My brother can do a good impression of the Prime Minister. 我哥哥学起首相来倒学得维妙维肖。 [SYN] imitation 同义词为imitation
4 a mark that is left when an object has been pressed hard into a surface （挤压留下的）印记

impressionable
/ɪmˈpreʃənəbl ||; ɪmˈprɛʃənəbḷ/adj easy to influence 易受影响的: Sixteen is a very impressionable age. 十六岁的年轻人易受熏染。

*impressive
/ɪmˈpresɪv ||; ɪmˈprɛsɪv/adj causing a feeling of admiration and respect because of the importance, size, quality, etc of sth 给人深刻印象的: an impressive building/speech 宏伟的建筑；令人难忘的演说 The way he handled the situation was most impressive. 他处理当时局面的手法令人赞叹。

imprint
/ɪmˈprɪnt ||; ɪmˈprɪnt/noun [C] a mark made by pressing an object on a surface （挤压留下的）印记: the imprint of a foot in the sand 沙地里的脚印

imprison
/ɪmˈprɪzn ||; ɪmˈprɪzṇ/verb [T] (often passive 常用于被动语态) to put or keep in prison 监禁: He was imprisoned for armed robbery. 他因犯了持械抢劫罪而给关进监牢。 [SYN] Incarcerate is a more formal word. 较正式的场合用incarcerate。 ➔imprisonment noun [U]: She was sentenced to five years' imprisonment. 她被判处五年徒刑。

improbable
/ɪmˈprɒbəbl ||; ɪmˈprɑbəbḷ/adj not likely to be true or to happen 不大可能的: an improbable explanation 说不通的解释 It is highly improbable that she will arrive tonight. 她今晚准来不了。 [SYN] unlikely 同义词为unlikely [OPP] probable 反义词为probable ➔improbability /ɪmˌprɒbəˈbɪləti ||; ɪmˌprɑbəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U] ➔improbably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

impromptu
/ɪmˈprɒmptju:; US -tu: ||; ɪmˈprɑmptu/adj (done) without being prepared or organized 即席的；即兴的: an impromptu party 即兴酒会

improper
/ɪmˈprɒpə(r) ||; ɪmˈprɑpɚ/adj
1 illegal or dishonest 非法的；不诚实的: It seems that she had been involved in improper business deals. 看来她卷入了一些不正当的交易。
2 not suitable for the situation; rude in a sexual way 不适当的；不得体的；下流的: It would be improper to say anything else at this stage. 在这个阶段说任何别的话都是不合适的。 He lost his job for making improper suggestions to several of the women. 他因为向好几位女性说了些下流话而失去工作。 [OPP] proper 反义词为proper ➔improperly adv [OPP] properly 反义词为properly

impropriety
/ˌɪmprəˈpraɪəti ||; ˌɪmprəˈpraɪətɪ/noun [U] [C] (plural improprieties) (formal 正式) behaviour or actions that are morally wrong or not appropriate 下流或不适当的行为: She was unaware of the impropriety of her remark. 她不知道自己说话造次了。

*improve
/ɪmˈpru:v ||; ɪmˈpruv/verb [I,T] to become or to make sth better 改进；改善: Your work has greatly improved. 你的工作大有改进。 I hope the weather will improve later on. 我希望天气会好转。 Your vocabulary is excellent but you could improve your pronunciation. 你掌握了大量的词汇，但发音可以改进一下。 improve on/upon sth to produce sth that is better than sth else 生产出比某物更好的东西: Nobody will be able to improve on that score (= nobody will be able to make a higher score). 没有人能超过那个成绩。

*improvement
/ɪmˈpru:vmənt ||; ɪmˈpruvmənt/noun [C,U] (an) improvement (on/in sth) (a) change which makes the quality or condition of sb/sth better 改进；改善: Your written work is in need of some improvement. 你的笔头作业须要改进一下。 We use improvement in to talk about something that has got better than it was before There's been a considerable improvement in your mother's condition. Improvement on is used when we are comparing two things and one is better than the other These marks are an improvement on your previous ones. 说某事物比过去有改进，要用improvement in：There's been a considerable improvement in your mother's condition.你妈妈的情况好多了。比较两个事物，一个比另一个好，就要用improvement on：These marks are an improvement on your previous ones.你这次分数比上次高。
improvise
/ˈɪmprəvaɪz; US ˌɪmprəˈvaɪz ||; ˌɪmprəˈvaɪz/verb[I,T]
1 to make, do, or manage sth without preparation, using what you have 临时凑合: If you're short of teachers today you'll just have to improvise (= manage somehow with the people that you've got). 今天老师不够的话，你要将就一下了。
2 to play music, speak or act using your imagination instead of written or remembered material 即兴演奏、讲演或行动；临时创作: It was obvious that the actor had forgotten his lines and was trying to improvise. 那个演员显然忘了台词，在当场发挥呢。 ➔improvisation /ˌɪmprəvaɪˈzeɪʃn; US ɪmˌprɒvəˈzeɪʃn ||; ɪmˌprɑvəˈzeʃən/ noun [C,U]

impudent
/ˈɪmpjədənt ||; ˈɪmpjədənt/adj (formal 正式) very rude; lacking respect and not polite 粗鲁的；无礼的 [SYN]A more informal word is cheeky. 非正式场合用cheeky。 ➔impudently adv ➔impudence noun [U]

impulse
/ˈɪmpʌls ||; ˈɪmpʌls/noun[C]
1 [usu.sing] an impulse (to do sth) a sudden desire to do sth without thinking about the results 冲动；突如其来的念头: She felt a terrible impulse to rush out of the house and never come back. 突然间她心里有个冲动，恨不得冲出屋去，再也不回来。
2 (technical术语) a force or movement of energy that causes a reaction 电路脉冲；神经冲动: nerve/electrical impulses 神经冲动；脉冲
on (an) impulse without thinking or planning and not considering the results 一时冲动: When I saw the child fall in the water, I just acted on impulse and jumped in after her. 看到那个孩子掉进水里，我就凭冲动行事，跟着跳进去。

impulsive
/ɪmˈpʌlsɪv ||; ɪmˈpʌlsɪv/adj likely to act suddenly and without thinking; done without careful thought 鲁莽的；冲动的: an impulsive character 容易冲动的个性 ➔impulsively adv ➔impulsiveness noun [U]

impure
/ɪmˈpjʊə(r) ||; ɪmˈpjυr/adj
1 not pure or clean; consisting of more than one substance mixed together (and therefore not of good quality) 不纯净的；有杂质的: impure metals 不纯的金属
2 (old-fashioned 旧) (used about thoughts and actions connected with sex) not moral; bad （指跟性有关的言行思想）下流的，淫猥的 [OPP] pure 反义词为pure

impurity
/ɪmˈpjʊərəti ||; ɪmˈpjυrətɪ/noun (plural impurities)
1 [C] [usu.pl] a substance that is present in small amounts in another substance, making it dirty or of poor quality 杂质: People are being advised to boil their water because certain impurities have been found in it. 水里发现了一些杂质，当局建议大家把水煮开。
2 [U] (old-fashioned 旧) the state of being morally bad 淫秽 ☞Look at purity. 参看purity。

*in¹
/ɪn ||; ɪn/adv prep For special uses with many nouns, for example in time, look at the noun entries. For special uses with many verbs, for example give in, look at the verb entries. 介词in可与许多名词连用，如in time，其用法参看有关名词词条。副词in可与许多动词连用，如give in，其用法参看有关动词词条。
1 (used to show place) inside or to a position inside a particular area or object （表示地方）在某范围内: a country in Africa 一个非洲国家 an island in the Pacific 太平洋上的一个岛屿 in a box 在箱子里 I read about it in the newspaper. 我在报纸上看到这个消息。 He lay in bed. 他躺在床上。 She put the keys in her pocket. 她把钥匙放在口袋里。 His wife's in hospital. 他妻子进医院了。 She opened the door and went in. 她把门打开进去了。 My suitcase is full. I can't get any more in. 我的提箱满了，再也装不下什么东西。 When does the train get in (= to the station)? 火车什么时候到站？
2 at home or at work 在家里或工作的地方: I phoned him last night but he wasn't in. 我昨晚给他挂电话，可是他不在家。 She won't be in till late today. 她今天要很晚才回家。
3 (showing time) during a period of time （表示时间）在某段时间内: My birthday is in August. 我的生日在八月。 in spring/summer/autumn/winter 在春天╱夏天╱秋天╱冬天 He was born in 1980. 他生于1980年。 You could walk there in about an hour (= it would take that long to walk there). 走一个钟头左右就到那儿。
4 (showing time) after a period of time （表示时间）某段时间后: I'll be finished in ten minutes. 我十分钟后可以做完。
5 wearing sth 穿着…: They were all dressed in black for the funeral. 葬礼上人人都穿着黑色衣服。 I've never seen you in a suit before. 以前我从没见过你穿西装。 a woman in a yellow dress 一个穿黄色连衣裙的女人
6 showing the condition or state of sb/sth （表示状况或状态）: My father is in poor health. 我父亲身体不好。 This room is in a mess ! 这个房间乱七八糟的！ Richard's in love. 理查德德在恋爱了。 He's in his mid-thirties. 他大约三十五六岁。
7 showing sb's job or the activity sb is involved in （表示所从事的工作或活动）: He's got a good job in advertising. 他有一份理想的广告界工作。 All her family are in politics (= they are politicians). 她全家都从政。 He's in the army. 他在当兵。
8 contained in; forming the whole or part of sth 包括在…内；构成整体或部份: There are 31 days in January. 一月份有31天。 What's in this casserole? 这砂锅里有什么？
9 used for saying how things are arranged （用于事物的编排）: We sat in a circle. 我们围成一个圈子坐着。 She had her hair in plaits. 她把头发编成辫子。
10 used for saying how sth is written or expressed （表示书写或表达方式）: Please write in pen. 请用墨水笔写。 They were talking in Italian/French/Polish. 他们在用意大利语╱法语╱波兰语交谈。 to work in groups/teams 分组╱小组工作
11 used with feelings （用于表示感觉）: I watched in horror as the plane crashed to the ground. 我看见飞机坠落地面，吓得魂飞魄散。 He was in such a rageI didn't dare to go near him. 他在大发雷霆，我根本不敢接近。
12 used for giving the rate of sth and for talking about numbers （用于比率或数字）: One family in tenowns a dishwasher. 每十个家庭就有一个拥有洗碗机。
13 received by sb official 正式收到: Entries should be in by 20 March. 报名期限为3月20日。 All applications must be in by Friday. 所有申请书最晚必须在星期五交来。
14 (used about the sea) at the highest point, when the water is closest to the land （指潮水）涨，升高: The tide's coming in. 现在开始涨潮了。
be in for it/sth to be going to experience sth unpleasant 将要经历令人不快的事情: He'll be in for a shock when he gets the bill. 他收到账单准会大吃一惊。 You'll be in for it when Mum sees what you've done. 妈妈发现你做了的事，一定会罚你。 be/get in on sth to be included or involved in sth 参与: I'd like to be in on the new project. 我想参与这项新计划。 have (got) it in for sb(informal 非正式) to be unpleasant to sb because he/she has done sth to upset you 对某人怀有恶意: The boss has had it in for me ever since I asked to be considered for the new post. 自从我要求老板考虑让我出任新职位，他就一直跟我过不去。
in²
/ɪn ||; ɪn/noun the ins and outs (of sth) the details and difficulties (involved in sth) 详情；细节；始末: Will somebody explain the ins and outs of the situation to me? 谁能向我解释一下当前局势的来龙去脉？
in³
/ɪn ||; ɪn/adj (informal 非正式) fashionable at the moment 时髦的；流行的: the in place to go 时髦的去处 The colour grey is very in this season. 这个季节很流行灰色。

in.
abbr inch(es) 英寸；吋

in-
/ɪn ||; ɪn/prefix
1 (also il- /ɪl ||; ɪl/im- /ɪm ||; ɪm/ir- /ɪr ||; ɪr/) (in adjectives, adverbs and nouns) not; the opposite of （用于构成形容词、副词及名词）不，非，相反: infinite 无限的 illogical 不合逻辑的 immorally 不道德 irrelevance 不相干
2 (also im- /ɪm ||; ɪm/) (in verbs 用于构成动词) to put into the condition mentioned 放在…里；使陷于…: inflame 使燃烧 imperil 使陷于危险

inability
/ˌɪnəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪnəˈbɪlətɪ/noun [sing] inability (to do sth) lack of ability, power or skill 无能；不能: He has a complete inability to listen to other people's opinions. 别人的意见他完全听不进去。 ☞adjective unable 形容词为unable

inaccessible
/ˌɪnækˈsesəbl ||; ˌɪnəkˈsɛsəbḷ/adj very difficult or impossible to reach or contact 难以达到的；不可及的: That beach is inaccessible by car. 那个海滩汽车去不了。 [OPP] accessible 反义词为accessible ➔inaccessibility /ˌɪnækˌsesəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪnəkˌsɛsəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

inaccurate
/ɪnˈækjərət ||; ɪnˈækjərɪt/adj not correct or accurate; with mistakes 不正确的；不准确的；有错误的: an inaccurate report/description/statement 不准确的报告╱描绘╱陈述 [OPP] accurate 反义词为accurate ➔inaccuracy /ɪnˈækjərəsi ||; ɪnˈækjərəsɪ/ noun [C,U] (plural inaccuracies): There are always some inaccuracies in newspaper reports. 报纸上的报道总有不准确的地方。 [OPP] accuracy 反义词为accuracy ➔inaccurately adv

inaction
/ɪnˈækʃn ||; ɪnˈækʃən/noun [U] doing nothing; lack of action 无行动；无作为: The crisis was blamed on the government's earlier inaction. 有人把这次危机归咎于政府早先没有采取行动。 [OPP] action 反义词为action

inactive
/ɪnˈæktɪv ||; ɪnˈæktɪv/adj doing nothing; not active 无行动的；不活跃的: The virus remains inactive in the body. 病毒依然潜伏在体内。 [OPP] active 反义词为active ➔inactivity /ˌɪnækˈtɪvəti ||; ˌɪnækˈtɪvətɪ/ noun [U] [OPP] activity 反义词为activity

inadequate
/ɪnˈædɪkwət ||; ɪnˈædəkwɪt/adj
1 inadequate (for sth/to do sth) not enough; not good enough 不足的；不够好的: the problem of inadequate housing 住房不足的问题
2 (used about a person) not able to deal with a problem or situation; not confident （指人）不能胜任的，信心不足的: There was so much to learn in the new job that for a while I felt totally inadequate. 新工作有太多东西要学，我一时感到力不从心。 [OPP] adequate 反义词为adequate ➔inadequately adv ➔inadequacy /ɪnˈædɪkwəsi ||; ɪnˈædəkwəsɪ/ noun [C,U] (plural inadequacies) his inadequacy as a parent 他这个不称职的家长

inadmissible
/ˌɪnədˈmɪsəbl ||; ˌɪnədˈmɪsəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) that cannot be allowed or accepted, especially in a court of law 不允许的，不能接受的（尤指在法庭上）: inadmissible evidence 不能接纳的证据

inadvertent
/ˌɪnədˈvɜ:tənt ||; ˌɪnədˈvɝtṇt/adj (used about actions) done without thinking, not on purpose （指行动）漫不经心的，非故意的 [OPP] intentional or deliberate 反义词为intentional或deliberate ➔inadvertently adv She had inadvertently left the letter where he could find it. 她一时大意，竟把那封信放在他找得到的地方。

inadvisable
/ˌɪnədˈvaɪzəbl ||; ˌɪnədˈvaɪzəbḷ/adj not sensible; not showing good judgement 不明智的；失策的: It is inadvisable to go swimming when you have a cold. 得了感冒最好不要去游泳。 [OPP] advisable 反义词为advisable

inalienable
/ɪnˈeɪliənəbl ||; ɪnˈelɪənəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) that cannot be taken away from you 不可剥夺的

inane
/ɪˈneɪn ||; ɪnˈen/adj without any meaning; silly 无聊的；愚蠢的: an inane remark 无聊话 ➔inanely adv

inanimate
/ɪnˈænɪmət ||; ɪnˈænəmɪt/adj not alive in the way that people, animals and plants are 无生命的: A rock is an inanimate object. 岩石是无生命物体。 [OPP] animate ² 反义词为animate^2

inappropriate
/ˌɪnəˈprəʊpriət ||; ˌɪnəˈproprɪɪt/adj not suitable 不合适的；不恰当的: Isn't that dress rather inappropriate for the occasion? 你不觉得那条裙子不大适合那种场合吗？ [OPP] appropriate 反义词为appropriate

inarticulate
/ˌɪnɑ:ˈtɪkjələt ||; ˌɪnɑrˈtɪkjəlɪt/adj
1 (used about a person) not able to express ideas and feelings clearly （指人）不善表达思想感情的
2 (used about speech) not clear or well expressed （指言语）含糊不清的 [OPP] articulate 反义词为articulate ➔inarticulately adv

inasmuch as
/ˌɪnəzˈmʌtʃ əz ||; ˌɪnəzˈmʌtʃ əz/ conj (formal 正式) because of the fact that 因为；鉴于: We felt sorry for the boys inasmuch as they had not realized that what they were doing was wrong. 这些男孩做了错事自己还不知道，我们因此感到很难过。

inaugurate
/ɪˈnɔ:gjəreɪt ||; ɪnˈɔgjəˌret/verb[T]
1 to introduce a new official, leader, etc at a special formal ceremony 为（官员、领袖等）举行就职典礼: He will be inaugurated as President next month. 他将于下个月就任总统。

incapable
/ɪnˈkeɪpəbl ||; ɪnˈkepəbḷ/adj
1 incapable of sth/doing sth not able to do sth 没有能力或不能做某事的: She is incapable of hard work/working hard. 她不能辛勤工作。 He's quite incapable of unkindness (= too nice to be unkind). 他这个人硬不起心肠。
2 not able to do, manage or organize anything well 无能的；不能胜任的: As a doctor, she's totally incapable. 作为医生，她是完全不能胜任的。 [OPP] capable 反义词为capable

incarnation
/ˌɪnkɑ:ˈneɪʃn ||; ˌɪnkɑrˈneʃən/noun[C]

incest

1 involving illegal sex between members of the same family 涉及乱伦的: an incestuous relationship 乱伦的关系
2 (used about a group of people and their relationships with each other) too close; not open to anyone outside the group （指一群人及他们之间的关系）过分亲密的，排外的，小圈子的: Life in a small community can be very incestuous. 小小区的生活有时是非常排外的。

*inch¹
/ɪntʃ ||; ɪntʃ/noun [C] (abbr in.) a measure of length; 2.54 centimetres. There are 12 inches in a foot. 英寸，吋（长度单位，相当于2.54厘米；一英尺等于12英寸）: He's 5 foot 10 inches tall. 他身高5英尺10英寸。 Three inches of rain fell last night. 昨晚下了三英寸的雨。
inch²
/ɪntʃ ||; ɪntʃ/verb [I,T] inch forward, past, through, etc to move slowly and carefully in the direction mentioned 小心翼翼地向某个方向移动: He inched (his way) forward along the cliff edge. 他沿着悬崖边缘小心翼翼地向前移动。

incidence
/ˈɪnsɪdəns ||; ˈɪnsədəns/noun
1 [sing] (formal 正式)an incidence of sth the number of times sth (usually sth unpleasant) happens; the rate of sth 发生率（一般指不好的事情）: a high incidence of crime/disease/unemployment 高犯罪率╱发病率╱失业率
2 [U] (technical术语) the way in which a ray of light meets a surface （光线的）射入: the angle of incidence 入射角 ➔incident adj the incident ray (= the one that meets a surface) 入射线 the incident angle (= at which a ray of light meets a surface) 入射角 ☞picture at reflection 见reflection插图

*incident

incidentally
/ˌɪnsɪˈdentli ||; ˌɪnsəˈdɛntḷɪ/adv used to introduce extra news, information, etc that the speaker has just thought of （用于带出临时想到的额外消息、信息等）顺便提一句: Incidentally, that new restaurant you told me about is excellent. 顺便说一句，你跟我提起的那家餐馆很不错。 ☞ Another way of saying ‘incidentally’ is by the way. 也可以说by the way。

/ˌɪnklɪˈneɪʃn ||; ˌɪnkləˈneʃən/noun [C,U] inclination (to do sth);inclination (towards/for sth) a feeling that makes sb want to behave in a particular way 意向；倾向: He did not show the slightest inclination to help. 他毫无帮忙之意。 She had no inclination for a career in teaching. 她无意以教书为职业。

incline¹
/ɪnˈklaɪn ||; ɪnˈklaɪn/verb
1 [I] (formal 正式)incline to/towards sth to want to behave in a particular way or make a particular choice 有意于；倾向于: I don't know what to choose, but I'm inclining towards the fish. 我不知道点什么菜好，不过我倾向于吃鱼。
2 [T] (formal 正式) to bend (your head) forward 弯腰；低头: They sat round the table, heads inclined, deep in discussion. 他们围桌而坐，弯身向前，专注地讨论问题。
3 [I] incline towards sth to be at an angle in a particular direction （向某方向）倾斜: The land inclines towards the shore. 陆地向岸边倾斜。
incline²
/ˈɪnklaɪn ||; ˈɪnklaɪn/noun [C] (formal 正式) a slight hill 斜坡: a steep/slight incline 陡峭的╱微斜的坡面 [SYN] slope 同义词为slope

inclined
/ɪnˈklaɪnd ||; ɪnˈklaɪnd/adj
1 inclined (to do sth) (not before a noun 不用于名词前) wanting to behave in a particular way 倾向；偏向于: I know Amir well so I'm inclined to believe what he says. 我跟埃米尔很熟，他说的我多半相信。
2 inclined to do sth likely to do sth 很可能（做某事）: She's inclined to change her mind very easily. 她这个人很容易改变主意。
3 having a natural ability in the subject mentioned 在某方面有天分: to be musically inclined 有音乐天分

*include
/ɪnˈklu:d ||; ɪnˈklud/verb [T] (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时)
1 to have as one part; to contain (among other things) 包括；含有: The price of the holiday includes the flight, the hotel and car hire. 旅费包括机票、住宿和租车费。 The crew included one woman. 工作人员里面有一位女性。 ☞ Look at the note at contain. 参看contain的注释。 [OPP] exclude 反义词为exclude
2 include sb/sth (as/in/on sth) to make sb/sth part (of another group, etc) （使）成为其中一分子或一部份: The children immediately included the new girl in their games. 孩子们马上接受这个新来的小女孩一起玩耍。 Everyone was disappointed, myself included. 谁都感到失望，我也是。 ➔inclusion /ɪnˈklu:ʒn ||; ɪnˈkluʒən/ noun [U]: The inclusion of all that violence in the film was unnecessary. 那部电影根本没有必要加插那么多的暴力镜头。

including
/ɪnˈklu:dɪŋ ||; ɪnˈkludɪŋ/prep having as a part 包括: It costs $17.99, including postage and packing. 一共要17.99元，邮费和包装费包括在内。 [OPP] excluding 反义词为excluding

inclusive
/ɪnˈklu:sɪv ||; ɪnˈklusɪv/adj
1 inclusive (of sth) (used about a price, etc) including or containing everything; including the thing mentioned （指价格等）包括所有项目的，连…算在内的: Is that an inclusive price or are there some extras? 这个价格是不是什么都包括了？有没有额外收费？ The rent is inclusive of electricity. 房租已包括电费在内。
2 (only after a noun 只用于名词后) including the dates, numbers, etc mentioned 包括所说的日期、数目等在内: You are booked at the hotel from Monday to Friday inclusive (= including Monday and Friday). 你订了星期一到星期五的旅馆房间，首尾两天包括在内。
When talking about time through is often used in American English instead of inclusive We'll be away from Friday through Sunday. 指日期时，美国英语一般说through，不说inclusive：We'll be away from Friday through Sunday.星期五到星期日我们都不在家。

incoherent
/ˌɪnkəʊˈhɪərənt ||; ˌɪnkoˈhɪrənt/adj not clear or easy to understand; not saying sth clearly 不清楚的；不合逻辑的 [OPP] coherent 反义词为coherent ➔incoherence noun [U] ➔incoherently adv

*income
/ˈɪnkʌm;-kəm ||; ˈɪnˌkʌm; -kəm/noun [C,U] the money you receive regularly as payment for your work or as interest on money you have saved, etc 收入（包括薪俸、存款利息等）: It's often difficult for a family to live on one income. 一个家庭往往难以靠一份收入过活。 We talk about a monthly or an annual income. An income may be high or low. Your gross income is the amount you earn before paying tax. Your net income is your income after tax. Look at the note at pay ². 收入可以按月(monthly)或者按年(annual)计算。收入高可用high形容，收入低用low。未扣除应缴税款前的总收入叫做gross income，扣税后的净收入叫做net income。参看pay^2的注释。

ˈincome tax
noun [U] the amount of money you pay to the government according to how much you earn 所得税

2 new; recently elected 新来的；新选的: the incoming government 新政府

inconceivable
/ˌɪnkənˈsi:vəbl ||; ˌɪnkənˈsivəbḷ/adj impossible or very difficult to believe or imagine 难以置信的；不可想象的: It's inconceivable that he would have stolen anything. 他竟然还会偷东西，真难以置信。 [OPP] conceivable 反义词为conceivable

inconclusive
/ˌɪnkənˈklu:sɪv ||; ˌɪnkənˈklusɪv/adj not leading to a definite decision or result 非决定性的；无结果的: an inconclusive discussion 毫无结果的讨论 inconclusive evidence (= that doesn't prove anything) 不确切的证据 [OPP] conclusive 反义词为conclusive ➔inconclusively adv

incongruous

inconsiderate
/ˌɪnkənˈsɪdərət ||; ˌɪnkənˈsɪdərɪt/adj (used about a person) not thinking or caring about the feelings, or needs of other people （指人）不替别人着想的，不体贴的: It was inconsiderate of you not to offer her a lift. 你真不体贴，没有开车送她一程。 [SYN] synonym thoughtless 同义词为thoughtless [OPP] considerate 反义词为considerate ➔inconsiderately adv ➔inconsiderateness noun [U]

inconsistent
/ˌɪnkənˈsɪstənt ||; ˌɪnkənˈsɪstənt/adj
1 inconsistent (with sth) (used about statements, facts, etc) not the same as sth else; not matching, so that one thing must be wrong or not true （指陈述、事实等）不一致，不协调: The witnesses' accounts of the event are inconsistent. 目击者对这宗事件的陈述互相矛盾。 These new facts are inconsistent with the earlier information. 新近掌握的事实跟先前的资料不吻合。
2 (used about a person) likely to change (in attitude, behaviour, etc) so that you cannot depend on him/her （指人）（态度、行为等）不一贯的，反复无常的: She's so inconsistent -- sometimes her work is good and sometimes it's really awful. 她这个人不大稳，有时做得好，有时做得很糟糕。 [OPP] consistent 反义词为consistent ➔inconsistency /-ənsi ||; -ənsɪ/ noun [C] [U] (plural inconsistencies) There were a few inconsistencies in her argument. 她的论点里有一些前后矛盾的地方。 [OPP] consistency 反义词为consistency ➔inconsistently adv

inconspicuous
/ˌɪnkənˈspɪkjuəs ||; ˌɪnkənˈspɪkjυəs/adv not easily noticed 不显眼的；不引人注目的: I tried to make myself as inconspicuousas possible so that no one would ask me a question. 我尽量不惹人注意，以免有人向我提问题。 [OPP] conspicuous 反义词为conspicuous ➔inconspicuously adv

incontinent
/ɪnˈkɒntɪnənt ||; ɪnˈkɑntənənt/adj unable to control the passing of waste (urine) and (faeces) from the body 大小便失禁的 ➔incontinence noun [U]

inconvenience
/ˌɪnkənˈvi:niəns ||; ˌɪnkənˈvinjəns/noun [U] [C] trouble or difficulty, especially when it affects sth that you need to do; a person or thing that causes this 麻烦；困难；不便；引起不便的人或事物: We apologize for any inconvenience caused by the delays. 若因延误引致不便，我们谨致歉意。 ➔inconvenience verb [T]

inconvenient
/ˌɪnkənˈvi:niənt ||; ˌɪnkənˈvinjənt/adj causing trouble or difficulty, especially when it affects sth that you need to do 引起麻烦或困难的；不方便的: It's a bit inconvenient at the moment -- could you phone again later? 现在不太方便，等会儿再来电话，好不好？ [OPP] convenient 反义词为convenient ➔inconveniently adv

incorporate
/ɪnˈkɔ:pəreɪt ||; ɪnˈkɔrpəˌret/verb [T] incorporate sth (in/into/within sth) to make sth a part of sth else; to have sth as a part 将…并入或包括进去: I'd like you to incorporate this information into your report. 希望你把这个内容写进你的报告。 [SYN] include 同义词为include ➔incorporation /ɪnˌkɔ:pəˈreɪʃn ||; ɪnˌkɔrpəˈreʃən/ noun [U]

/ɪnˈkɔ:pəreɪtɪd ||; ɪnˈkɔrpəˌretɪd/adj (abbr Inc.) (following the name of a company) formed into a legal organization (corporation) （放在公司的名称后面）组成法人团体或公司的，有限责任公司的

/ˌɪnkəˈrekt ||; ˌɪnkəˈrɛkt/adj not right or true 不正确的；不真实的: Incorrect answers should be marked with a cross. 不对的答案应该打叉。 [OPP] correct 反义词为correct ➔incorrectly adv

incorrigible
/ɪnˈkɒrɪdʒəbl; US -ˈkɔ:r- ||; ɪnˈkɔrɪdʒəbḷ/adj (used about a person or his/her behaviour) very bad; too bad to be corrected or improved （指人或其行为）不可救药的，积习难改的: an incorrigible liar 说谎成性的人

*increase¹
/ɪnˈkri:s ||; ɪnˈkris/verb [I,T] increase (sth) (from A) (to B);increase (sth) (by sth) to become or to make sth larger in number or amount 增加: The rate of inflation has increased by 1% to 7%. 通胀率已上升一个百分点，达到7%。 My employer would like me to increase my hours of work from 25 to 30. 老板要我把工作时间从25小时增加到30小时。 She increased her speed to overtake the lorry. 她加快速度追过那辆卡车。 [OPP] decrease or reduce 反义词为decrease或reduce
*increase²
/ˈɪŋkri:s/noun [C,U] (an) increase (in sth) a rise in the number, amount or level of sth 增加: There has been a sharp increase of nearly 50% on last year's figures. 今年的数字比去年激增了将近五成。 Doctors expect some further increase in the spread of the disease. 医生预测，这种疾病蔓延的范围仍会有所扩大。 They are demanding a large wage increase. 他们要求把工资大幅度调高。 [OPP] decrease or reduction 反义词为decrease或reduction on the increase becoming larger or more frequent; increasing 正在增加: Attacks by dogs on children are on the increase. 恶犬袭击儿童的事件越来越多。

increasingly
/ɪnˈkri:sɪŋli ||; ɪnˈkrisɪŋlɪ/adv more and more 越来越…；愈加: It's becoming increasingly difficult/important/dangerous to stay here. 留在这儿变得越来越困难╱重要╱危险。

incredible
/ɪnˈkredəbl ||; ɪnˈkrɛdəbḷ/adj
1 impossible or very difficult to believe 不可思议的；难以置信的: I found his account of the event incredible. 他说的事情经过叫我难以相信。 [OPP] credible 反义词为credible ☞Look at unbelievable. 参看unbelievable。
2 (informal 非正式) extremely good or big 极好的；极大的: He earns an incredible salary. 他的收入高得了不得。 ➔incredibly /-əbli/ adv We have had some incredibly strong winds recently. 近来我们这儿刮了几次极大的风。

increment
/ˈɪŋkrəmənt ||; ˈɪnkrəmənt/noun[C]
1 a regular increase in the amount of money that sb is paid for his/her job （薪金的）增额: a salary with annual increments 每年都加一次的薪金
2 (formal 正式) an increase in a number or an amount （数目或数量的）增加，增长 ➔incremental /ˌɪŋkrəˈməntl ||; ˌɪnkrəˈmɛntḷ/ adj incremental costs 增加的成本 ➔incrementally /-təli ||; -təlɪ/ adv

incriminate
/ɪnˈkrɪmɪneɪt ||; ɪnˈkrɪməˌnet/verb [T] to provide evidence that sb is guilty of a crime 提供证据以证明某人有罪: The police searched the house but found nothing to incriminate the man. 警察搜过那座房子，可是找不到可以给名男子定罪的证据。

incubate
/ˈɪŋkjubeɪt ||; ˈɪŋkjəˌbet/verb[T]
1 to keep an egg at the right temperature so that it can develop and produce a bird (hatch) 孵；孵育；孵化
2 [I,T] (used about a disease) to develop without showing signs; (used about a person or an animal) to carry a disease without showing signs （指疾病）潜伏；（指人或动物）带有潜伏的疾病: Some viruses take weeks to incubate. 有些病毒要几个星期才能培养出来。

incubation
/ˌɪŋkjuˈbeɪʃn ||; ˌɪnkjəˈbeʃən/noun
1 [U] the process of incubating eggs 孵化；孵育
2 [C] (also ˌincuˈbation period) the period between catching a disease and the time when signs of it (symptoms) appear （疾病的）潜伏期

incubator
/ˈɪŋkjubeɪtə(r) ||; ˈɪŋkjəˌbetɚ/noun[C]
1 a heated machine used in hospitals for keeping small or weak babies alive （医院里用来放置弱小婴儿的）恒温箱，保温箱
2 a heated machine for keeping eggs warm until they break open (hatch) 孵化器

incur
/ɪnˈkɜ:(r) ||; ɪnˈkɝ/verb [T] (incurred;incurring) (formal 正式) to suffer the unpleasant results of a situation that you have caused 招致；招惹: to incur debts/sb's anger 负债；惹某人生气

incurable
/ɪnˈkjʊərəbl ||; ɪnˈkjυrəbḷ/adj that cannot be cured or made better 无法治愈的；不可救药的: an incurable disease 不治之症 [OPP] curable 反义词为curable ➔incurably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv incurably ill 病入膏肓

indecent
/ɪnˈdi:snt ||; ɪnˈdisṇt/adj shocking to many people in society, especially because sth involves sex or the body 有伤风化的；下流的: indecent photos/behaviour/language 下流的照片╱行为╱语言 You can't wear those tiny swimming trunks -- they're indecent! 你不可以穿那么小的游泳裤，有伤风化！ [OPP] decent 反义词为decent ➔indecency /-nsi ||; -ṇsɪ/ noun [U] [sing] ➔indecently adv

*indeed
/ɪnˈdi:d ||; ɪnˈdid/adv
1 (used for emphasizing a positive statement or answer) really; certainly （用于强调肯定的陈述或答复）确实，当然: ‘Have you had a good holiday?’ ‘We have indeed.’ “假期玩得开心吗？”“很开心。”
2 used after ‘very’ with an adjective or adverb to emphasize the quality mentioned （放在very加形容词或副词后面，用于强调）: Thank you very much indeed. 实在很感谢你们。 She's very happy indeed. 她真是高兴极了。
3 (used for adding information to a statement) in fact （用于说话的补充部份）其实，实际上: It's important that you come at once. Indeed, it's essential. 你得马上来。这十分重要。
4 used for showing interest, surprise, anger, etc （用于表示兴趣、惊奇、愤怒等）: ‘They were talking about you last night.’ ‘Were they indeed!’ “他们昨晚谈起你来着。”“真的吗？”

indefensible
/ˌɪndɪˈfensəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈfɛnsəbḷ/adj (used about behaviour, etc) completely wrong; that cannot be defended or excused （指行为等）无法辩解的，不可原谅的

indefinable
/ˌɪndɪˈfaɪnəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈfaɪnəbḷ/adj difficult or impossible to describe 难以描述的；说不清楚的: There was an indefinable atmosphere of hostility. 当时有一种说不清的敌对气氛。 ➔indefinably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

indefinite
/ɪnˈdefɪnət ||; ɪnˈdɛfənɪt/adj not fixed or clear 不确定的；不明确的: Our plans are still rather indefinite. 我们的计划仍然很不明确。 [OPP] definite 反义词为definite

indefinitely
/ɪnˈdefɪnətli ||; ɪnˈdɛfənɪtlɪ/adv for a period of time that has no fixed end 无限期: The meeting was postponed indefinitely. 会议无限期推迟。

indelible
/ɪnˈdeləbl ||; ɪnˈdɛləbḷ/adj that cannot be removed or washed out 难以去除的；洗不掉的: indelible ink 不褪色的墨水 (figurative 比喻) The experience made an indelible impression on me. 那次经历给我留下了不可磨灭的印象。 ➔indelibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

indemnify
/ɪnˈdemnɪfaɪ ||; ɪnˈdɛmnəˌfaɪ/verb [T] (present participle indemnifying third person singular present indemnifies;past tense present participle indemnified) (law法津)
1 indemnify sb (against sth) to promise to pay sb an amount of money if he/she suffers any damage or loss （给予）保障，保证
2 indemnify sb (for sth) to pay sb an amount of money because of the damage or loss that he/she has suffered 补偿；赔偿 ➔indemnification /ɪnˌdemnɪfɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌdɛmnəfəˈkeʃən/ noun [U]

indemnity
/ɪnˈdemnəti ||; ɪnˈdɛmnətɪ/noun (formal 正式)
1 [U] protection against damage or loss, especially in the form of a promise to pay for any that happens 保障（尤指在发生万一的情况下给予补偿或赔偿）
2 [C] (plural indemnities) an amount of money that is given as payment for damage or loss 补偿金；赔偿金

indent
/ɪnˈdent ||; ɪnˈdɛnt/verb [I,T] to start a line of writing further from the left-hand side of the page than the other lines 缩格书写；缩排

*independence
/ˌɪndɪˈpendəns ||; ˌɪndɪˈpɛndəns/noun [U]: independence (from sb/sth) (used about a person, country, etc) the state of being free and not controlled by another person, country, etc （指人、国家等）独立，自主: In 1947 India achieved independence from Britain. 印度在1947年脱离英国独立。 financial independence 财政自主 On Independence Day (4 July) Americans celebrate the day in 1776 when America declared itself independent from Britain. 1776年7月4日美国宣布脱离英国独立，美国人以该日为独立纪念日(Independence Day)。
*independent
/ˌɪndɪˈpendənt ||; ˌɪndɪˈpɛndənt/adj
1 independent (of/from sb/sth) free from and not controlled by another person, country, etc 不受（别人、别国等）控制或支配的；独立的: Many former colonies are now independent nations. 从前的殖民地如今很多都变成了独立国家。 independent schools/television (= not supported by government money) 私立学校；私营电视台
2 independent (of/from sb/sth) not needing or wanting help 不依靠外力的；自力更生的；自立的: I got a part-time job because I wanted to be financially independent from my parents. 我找了一份兼职，因为我不想在经济上依靠父母。 [OPP] dependent 反义词为dependent
3 not influenced by or connected with sb/sth 不受外界影响的；没有关联的: Complaints against the police should be investigated by an independent body. 针对警察的投诉应该由独立机构加以调查。 Two independent opinion polls have obtained similar results. 两个独立的民意测验都得到了近似的结果。 ➔independently adv independently (of sb/sth) Scientists working independently of each other have had very similar results in their experiments. 独立进行研究的科学家都得到了非常近似的实验结果。

indescribable
/ˌɪndɪˈskraɪbəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈskraɪbəbḷ/adj too good or bad to be described （好或坏得）难以形容的: indescribable poverty/luxury/noise 难以名状的贫困╱奢侈╱噪音 ➔indescribably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

indestructible
/ˌɪndɪˈstrʌktəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈstrʌktəbḷ/adj that cannot be easily damaged or destroyed 难以损坏的；难以毁灭的

index
/ˈɪndeks ||; ˈɪndɛks/noun [C] (plural indexes)
1 a list in order from A to Z, usually at the end of a book, of the names or subjects that are referred to in the book （书后的）索引，引得: If you want to find all the references to London, look it up in the index. 查一查索引，你就可以找到关于伦敦的全部参考数据。
2 (Brit 英) =CARD INDEX
3 (plural indexes or indices) a way of showing how the price, value, rate, etc of sth has changed 指数（显示价格、价值、比率等的变动）: the cost-of-living index 生活费用指数 index verb The books in the library are indexed by subject and title. 图书馆里的书按学科和书名编目录。

ˈindex card
noun [C] a small card that you can write information on and keep with other cards in a box or file 索引卡 ☞picture at stationery 见stationery插图

ˈindex finger

*Indian
/ˈɪndiən ||; ˈɪndɪən/noun [C] adj
1 (a person) from the Republic of India 印度人（的）: Indian food is hot and spicy. 印度菜又辣又多香料。
2 =NATIVE AMERICAN The Sioux were a famous Indian tribe. 苏人是一个著名的印第安部落。 ☞Look at West Indian. 参看West Indian。

*indicate
/ˈɪndɪkeɪt ||; ˈɪndəˌket/verb
1 [T] to show that sth is probably true or exists 显示；表明: Recent research indicates that children are getting too little exercise. 最近的研究显示，儿童缺少运动。
2 [T] to say sth in an indirect way 暗示: The spokesman indicated that an agreement was likely soon. 发言人暗示有可能很快达成协议。
3 [T] to make sb notice sth, especially by pointing to it 让人注意到（尤指指给人看）: The receptionist indicated where I should sign. 接待员指给我看在什么地方签名。 The boy seemed to be indicating that I should follow him. 那男孩好像示意我跟着他。
4 [I,T] to signal that your car, etc is going to turn 发出信号（表示汽车等要转弯） · The lorry indicated left but turned right. 这辆卡车打左转弯信号，却向右边拐去。

indication
/ˌɪndɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ˌɪndəˈkeʃən/noun [C,U] an indication (of sth/doing sth);an indication that... something that shows sth; a sign 迹象；标志: There was no indication of a struggle. 没有搏斗的痕迹。 There is every indication that he will make a full recovery. 种种迹象表明，他可望完全康复。

indicative
/ɪnˈdɪkətɪv ||; ɪnˈdɪkətɪv/adj (formal 正式) being or giving a sign of sth 表明；显示: Is the unusual weather indicative of climatic changes? 这种异常的天气是否表明气候已经发生根本的变化？

indicator
/ˈɪndɪkeɪtə(r) ||; ˈɪndəˌketɚ/noun[C]
1 something that gives information or shows sth; a sign 指示器；指示牌；指标: The indicator showed that we had plenty of petrol. 指示器显示，我们的汽车有充足的汽油。 The unemployment rate is a reliable indicator of economic health. 失业率是显示经济状况是否正常的可靠指标。
2 (US 美 turn signal) the flashing light on a car, etc that shows that it is going to turn right or left （汽车等的）方向指示灯 ☞picture at car 见car插图

indict
/ɪnˈdaɪt ||; ɪnˈdaɪt/verb [T] (usually passive 通常使用被动语态) indict sb (for sb) (especially US 尤为美) (law法津) to officially charge sb with a crime 控告；起诉: The senator was indicted for murder. 那名参议员被控以谋杀罪。

indictment
/ɪnˈdaɪtmənt ||; ɪnˈdaɪtmənt/noun[C]
1 a written paper that officially accuses sb of a crime 起诉书
2 an indictment (of sth) something that shows how bad sth is 控诉；谴责: The fact that many children leave school with no qualifications is an indictment of our education system. 很多儿童未能毕业就离校，这个事实本身就是对我们的教育制度的严厉批评。

indifference
/ɪnˈdɪfrəns ||; ɪnˈdɪfrəns/noun [U]: indifference (to sb/sth) a lack of interest or feeling towards sb/sth 冷淡；漠不关心: He has always shown indifference to the needs of others. 他对别人的需求总是无动于衷。

indifferent
/ɪnˈdɪfrənt ||; ɪnˈdɪfrənt/adj
1 indifferent (to sb/sth) not interested in or caring about sb/sth 不感兴趣；漠不关心: The manager of the shop seemed indifferent to our complaints. 商店经理对我们的投诉似乎不加理会。
2 not very good 不很好的: The standard of football in the World Cup was rather indifferent. 这次世界杯的足球水平相当差。 ➔indifferently adv

indigenous
