indigestible
/ˌɪndɪˈdʒestəbl ||; ˌɪndəˈdʒɛstəbḷ/adj (used about food 指食物) difficult or impossible for the stomach to deal with 难以消化的 [OPP] digestible 反义词为digestible

indigestion
/ˌɪndɪˈdʒestʃən ||; ˌɪndəˈdʒɛstʃən/noun [U] pain in the stomach that is caused by difficulty in dealing with food 消化不良: Peppers give me indigestion. 我吃辣椒不好消化。

indignant
/ɪnˈdɪgnənt ||; ɪnˈdɪgnənt/adj indignant (with sb) (about/at sth);indignant that... shocked or angry because sb has said or done sth that you do not like and do not agree with 愤慨的: They were indignant that they had to pay more for worse services. 服务越来越差，费用却越来越高，他们很气愤。 ➔indignantly adv

indignation
/ˌɪndɪgˈneɪʃn ||; ˌɪndɪgˈneʃən/noun [U]: indignation (at/about sth);indignation that… shock and anger 愤慨；愤怒: commuters' indignation at the rise in fares 通勤者对交通费上涨的愤慨

indignity
/ɪnˈdɪgnəti ||; ɪnˈdɪgnətɪ/noun [U] [C] (plural indignities)indignity (of sth/of doing sth) a situation that makes you feel embarrassed because you are not treated with respect; an act that causes these feelings 不受尊敬；侮辱；无礼举动 [SYN] humiliation 同义词为humiliation The chairman suffered the indignity of being refused admission to the meeting. 主席被拒会议门外，蒙受了侮辱。 the daily indignities of imprisonment 天天受侮辱的监狱生活

indigo
/ˈɪndɪgəʊ ||; ˈɪndɪˌgo/adj very dark blue in colour 靛蓝色的；靛色的 ➔indigo noun [U]

indirect
/ˌɪndəˈrekt;-daɪˈr- ||; ˌɪndəˈrɛkt,; -daɪˈr-/adj
1 not being the direct cause of sth; not having a direct connection with sth 间接的: an indirect result 间接的结果
2 that avoids saying sth in an obvious way 拐弯抹角的: She gave only an indirect answer to my question. 她只给我的问题一个拐弯抹角的答复。
3 not going in a straight line or using the shortest route 迂回的；不抄近路的: We came the indirect route to avoid driving through London. 我们绕道走，避免开车经过伦敦。 [OPP] direct 反义词为direct ➔indirectly adv [OPP] directly 反义词为directly ➔indirectness noun [U]

ˌindirect ˈobject
noun [C] (grammar语法) a person or thing that an action is done to or for 间接宾语；间接受词: In the sentence, ‘I wrote him a letter’,‘him’ is the indirect object. 在I wrote him a letter这个句子里，him是间接宾语。 ☞Look at direct object. 参看direct object。 For more information about indirect objects, look at the Quick Grammar Reference at the back of this dictionary. 有关间接宾语的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。
ˌindirect ˈspeech
(also reˈported speech) noun [U] (grammar语法) reporting what sb has said, not using the actual words 间接引语；间接叙述 ☞Look at direct speech. 参看direct speech。 Hadi's words were ‘I'll phone again later.’ In indirect speech this becomes Hadi said that he would phone again later. 哈迪的原话是：I'll phone again later（我过一会儿再打电话来）。在间接引语中，这句话就变为：Hadi said that he would phone again later（哈迪说他过一会儿再打电话来）。 ☞For more information about indirect speech, look at the Quick Grammar Reference at the back of this dictionary. 有关间接引语的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

indiscreet
/ˌɪndɪˈskri:t ||; ˌɪndɪˈskrit/adj not careful or polite in what you say or do 轻率的；莽撞的 [OPP] discreet 反义词为discreet ➔indiscreetly adv

indiscretion
/ˌɪndɪˈskreʃn ||; ˌɪndɪˈskrɛʃən/noun [C,U] behaviour that is not careful or polite, and that might cause embarrassment or offence 轻率或莽撞的行为

indiscriminate
/ˌɪndɪˈskrɪmɪnət ||; ˌɪndɪˈskrɪmənɪt/adj done or acting without making sensible judgement or caring about the possible harmful effects 不加区别的；恣意的: He's indiscriminate in his choice of friends. 他滥交朋友。 ➔indiscriminately adv

indispensable
/ˌɪndɪˈspensəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈspɛnsəbḷ/adj very important, so that it is not possible to be without it 不可或缺: A car is indispensable nowadays if you live in the country. 现今住在郊外的人不可没有汽车。 [SYN] essential 同义词为essential [OPP] dispensable 反义词为dispensable

indisputable
/ˌɪndɪˈspju:təbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈspjutəbḷ/adj definitely true; that cannot be shown to be wrong 无可置疑的

indistinct
/ˌɪndɪˈstɪŋkt ||; ˌɪndɪˈstɪŋkt/adj not clear 模糊的: indistinct figures/sounds/memories 模糊的身影╱声音╱记忆 [OPP] distinct 反义词为distinct ➔indistinctly adv

indistinguishable
/ˌɪndɪˈstɪŋgwɪʃəbl ||; ˌɪndɪˈstɪŋgwɪʃəbḷ/adj indistinguishable (from sth) appearing to be the same 难以区别: From a distance the two colours are indistinguishable. 从远处看，这两种颜色可没有分别。 [OPP] distinguishable 反义词为distinguishable

*individual¹
/ˌɪndɪˈvɪdʒuəl ||; ˌɪndəˈvɪdʒυəl/adj
1 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) considered separately rather than as part of a group 单个的；个别的: Each individual animal is weighed and measured before being set free. 每只动物都磅体重、量高度后才被放掉。
2 for or from one person 给每个人的；属于每个人的: an individual portion of butter 一份黄油 Children need individual attention when they are learning to read. 孩子学习阅读的时候，需要给予个别辅导。
3 typical of one person in a way that is different from other people 独特的；有个性的: I like her individual style of dressing. 她的衣着风格独特，我很喜欢。
individual²
/ˌɪndɪˈvɪdʒuəl ||; ˌɪndəˈvɪdʒυəl/noun[C]
1 one person, considered separately from others or a group 个人: Are the needs of society more important than the rights of the individual? 社会的需求是不是比个人的权利更为重要？
2 (informal 非正式) a person of the type that is mentioned 某种类型的人: She's a strange individual. 她这个人很古怪。

individualism
/ˌɪndɪˈvɪdʒuəlɪzəm ||; ˌɪndəˈvɪdʒυəlˌɪzəm/noun [U]:
1 the quality of being different from other people and doing things in your own way 个性；与众不同的特性: She owes her success to her individualism and flair. 她把成功归因于自己的个性和天赋。
2 the belief that individual people in society should have the right to make their own decisions, etc, rather than being controlled by the government 个人主义 ➔individualist /-əlɪst ||; -əlɪst/ noun [C]: He's a complete individualist in the way he paints. 就绘画风格而言，他是个十足的个人主义者。 ➔individualistic /ˌɪndɪˌvɪdʒuəˈlɪstɪk ||; ˌɪndəˌvɪdʒυəlˈɪstɪk/(also individualist) adj an individualistic culture 独特的文化 Her music is highly individualistic and may not appeal to everyone. 她的音乐别具一格，不一定人人都喜欢。

individuality
/ˌɪndɪˌvɪdʒuˈæləti ||; ˌɪndəˌvɪdʒυˈælətɪ/noun [U] the qualities that make sb/sth different from other people or things 特性；个性: Young people often try to express their individuality by the way they dress. 年轻人往往想通过衣着来表现个性。

individually
/ˌɪndɪˈvɪdʒuəli ||; ˌɪndəˈvɪdʒυəlɪ/adv separately; one by one 各个；分别；一一: The teacher talked to each member of the class individually. 老师跟班里的每个学生分别谈话。

indivisible
/ˌɪndɪˈvɪzəbl ||; ˌɪndəˈvɪzəbḷ/adj that cannot be divided or split into smaller pieces 不可分割

indoctrinate
/ɪnˈdɒktrɪneɪt ||; ɪnˈdɑktrɪnˌet/verb [T] to force sb to accept particular beliefs without considering others 灌输: For 20 years the people have been indoctrinated by the government. 20年来，人民一直被政府灌输特定思想。 ➔indoctrination /ɪnˌdɒktrɪˈneɪʃn ||; ɪnˌdɑktrɪˈneʃən/ noun [U]

*indoor
/ˈɪndɔ:(r) ||; ˈɪnˌdɔr/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) done or used inside a building 室内的: indoor games 室内体育活动 an indoor swimming pool 室内游泳池 [OPP] outdoor 反义词为outdoor

*indoors
/ˌɪnˈdɔ:z ||; ˈɪnˈdɔrz/adv in or into a building 在或往室内: Let's go indoors. 我们进屋里吧。 Oh dear! I've left my sunglasses indoors. 哎呀！我把太阳镜忘在屋里了。 [OPP] outdoors or out of doors 反义词为outdoors或out of doors

induce
/ɪnˈdju:s; US -du:s ||; ɪnˈdus/verb [T] (formal 正式)
1 to make or persuade sb to do sth 使；劝诱；说服: Nothing could induce him to change his mind. 什么也无法使他改变主意。
2 to cause or produce 引起；引致；导致: drugs that induce sleep 导致睡眠的药物 a drug-induced coma 药物引致的昏迷
3 (medical医学) to make a woman start giving birth to her baby by giving her special drugs 引产

inducement
/ɪnˈdju:smənt ||; ɪnˈdusmənt/noun [C,U] something that is offered to sb to make him/her do sth 引诱；引诱物: The player was offered a car as an inducement to join the club. 人家提出给一辆汽车的条件来诱使那位选手加入俱乐部。

induction
/ɪnˈdʌkʃn ||; ɪnˈdʌkʃən/noun
1 [U] [C] the process of introducing sb to a new job, skill, organization, etc; an event at which this takes place 向某人介绍新的工作、技术、组织等；入门；与此有关的活动: an induction day for new students 给新学生介绍情况的一天
2 [U] (technical术语) a method of discovering general rules and principles from particular facts and examples 归纳（法） ☞Compare deduction. 与deduction比较。
3 [U] (technical术语) the process by which electricity or MAGNETISM passes from one object to another without them touching （电磁）感应

inductive
/ɪnˈdʌktɪv ||; ɪnˈdʌktɪv/adj (technical术语)
1 using particular facts and examples to form general rules and principles 归纳（法）的: an inductive argument 归纳论证 inductive reasoning 归纳推理 ☞Compare deductive. 与deductive比较。
2 connected with the induction of electricity 电磁感应的

indulge
/ɪnˈdʌldʒ ||; ɪnˈdʌldʒ/verb
1 [I,T] indulge (yourself) (in sth) to allow yourself to have or do sth for pleasure 让自己享受（某事物带来的乐趣）；沉迷；沉溺；纵容: I'm going to indulge myself and go shopping for some new clothes. 我打算放纵一下自己，出去买几件新衣服。 Maria never indulges in gossip. 玛丽亚从不纵情于说长道短。
2 [T] to give sb/sth what he/she/it wants or needs 纵容: You shouldn't indulge that child. It will make him very selfish. 这个孩子宠不得，惯坏了准使他变得十分自私。 At the weekends he indulges his passion for fishing. 他酷爱钓鱼，每到周末总要放任一下。

indulgence
/ɪnˈdʌldʒəns ||; ɪnˈdʌldʒəns/noun
1 [U] the state of having or doing whatever you want 放纵: to lead a life of indulgence 过放纵的生活 Over-indulgence in chocolate makes you fat. 毫无节制地吃巧克力会使人发胖。
2 [C] something that you have or do because it gives you pleasure 嗜好: A cigar after dinner is my only indulgence. 晚饭后抽一支雪茄是我唯一的嗜好。

indulgent
/ɪnˈdʌldʒənt ||; ɪnˈdʌldʒənt/adj allowing sb to have or do whatever he/she wants 纵容的；放任的: indulgent parents 惯纵子女的父母 ➔indulgently adv

*industrial
/ɪnˈdʌstriəl ||; ɪnˈdʌstrɪəl/adj
1 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) connected with industry 工业的；产业的: industrial development 工业发展 industrial workers 产业工人
2 having a lot of factories, etc 工业发达的: an industrial region/country/town 工业地区╱国家╱城镇

inˌdustrial ˈaction
noun [U] action that workers take, especially stopping work, in order to protest about sth to their employers; a strike 工业行动，工潮（尤指为某事向老板表示抗议的停工）；罢工: to threaten (to take) industrial action 扬言要罢工

industrialist
/ɪnˈdʌstriəlɪst ||; ɪnˈdʌstrɪəlɪst/noun [C] a person who owns or manages a large industrial company 工业家；实业家

industrialize
/ɪnˈdʌstrɪəlaɪz ||; ɪnˈdʌstrɪəlˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [I,T] to develop industries in a country 发展工业；工业化: Japan industrialized rapidly in the late nineteenth century. 日本在十九世纪末迅速实现了工业化。 ➔industrialization(also -isation) /-eɪʃn; US -lɪˈz- ||; -ləˈzeʃən/ noun [U]

industrious
/ɪnˈdʌstriəs ||; ɪnˈdʌstrɪəs/adj always working hard 辛勤的；勤奋的

*industry
/ˈɪndəstri ||; ˈɪndəstrɪ/noun (plural industries)
1 [U] the production of goods in factories 工业；产业: Is British industry being threatened by foreign imports? 英国工业是否受到了外国进口产品的威胁？ heavy/light industry 重╱轻工业
2 [C] the people and activities involved in producing sth, providing a service, etc 行业: the tourist/catering/entertainment industry 旅游╱饮食╱娱乐业

inedible
/ɪnˈedəbl ||; ɪnˈɛdəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) not suitable to be eaten 不宜食用的: an inedible plant 不宜食用的植物 [OPP] edible 反义词为edible

ineffective
/ˌɪnɪˈfektɪv ||; ˌɪnəˈfɛktɪv/adj not producing the effect or result that you want 无效果的；无结果的 [OPP] effective 反义词为effective

inefficient
/ˌɪnɪˈfɪʃnt ||; ˌɪnəˈfɪʃənt/adj not working or producing results in the best way, so that time or money is wasted 低效率的: Our heating system is very old and extremely inefficient. 我们的暖气设备非常陈旧，根本不管用。 an inefficient secretary 不称职的秘书 [OPP] efficient 反义词为efficient ➔inefficiency /-ənsi ||; -ənsɪ/ noun [U] ➔inefficiently adv

ineligible
/ɪnˈelɪdʒəbl ||; ɪnˈɛlɪdʒəbḷ/adj ineligible (for/to do sth) without the necessary certificates, etc to do or get sth 没有资格: She was ineligible for the job because she wasn't a German citizen. 她不是德国公民，没有资格担当这项工作。 [OPP] eligible 反义词为eligible ➔ineligibility /ɪnˌelɪdʒəˈbɪləti ||; ɪnˌɛlɪdʒəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

inept
/ɪˈnept ||; ɪnˈɛpt/adj inept (at sth) not able to do sth well 不胜任的；不擅长的: She is totally inept at dealing with people. 她完全不善交际。 [OPP] adept 反义词为adept

inequality
/ˌɪnɪˈkwɒləti ||; ˌɪnɪˈkwɑlətɪ/noun [C,U] (plural inequalities) (a) difference between groups in society because one has more money, advantages, etc than the other 不平等 · There will be problems as long as inequality between the races exists. 种族间的不平等存在一天，问题就会存在一天。 [OPP] equality 反义词为equality

inert
/ɪˈnɜ:t ||; ɪnˈɝt/adj
1 not able to move or act 无活动力的
2 (used about chemical elements 指化学元素) that do not react with other chemicals 惰性的；不活泼的
Inert gases are also called noble gases. Helium, argon, krypton and neon are inert gases. 惰性气体(inert gas)也称noble gas。氦(helium)、氩(argon)、氪(krypton)和氖(neon)都是惰性气体。
inertia
/ɪˈnɜ:ʃə ||; ɪnˈɝʃə/noun [U]:
1 a lack of energy; an inability to move or change 惰性；不活动
2 the physical force that keeps things where they are or keeps them moving in the direction they are travelling （物理学上的）惯性，惰性

inescapable
/ˌɪnɪˈskeɪpəbl ||; ˌɪnəˈskepəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) that cannot be avoided 无可避免的: an inescapable conclusion 必然的结论

inevitable
/ɪnˈevɪtəbl ||; ɪnˈɛvətəbḷ/adj that cannot be avoided or prevented from happening 无可避免的；无可防范的: With more cars on the road, traffic jams are inevitable. 汽车增加，路上也就少不了交通挤塞。 the inevitable noun [sing] They fought to save the firm from closure, but eventually had to accept the inevitable. 他们竭力不让公司关门，但到头来不得不接受这不可避免的结局。 ➔inevitability /ɪnˌevɪtəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪnɛvətəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U] ➔inevitably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

inexcusable
/ˌɪnɪkˈskju:zəbl ||; ˌɪnɪkˈskjuzəbḷ/adj that cannot be allowed or forgiven 无可宽恕的；不可原谅的: Their behaviour was quite inexcusable. 他们的行径实在不可宽恕。 [SYN] unforgivable 同义词为unforgivable [OPP] excusable 反义词为excusable

inexhaustible
/ˌɪnɪgˈzɔ:stəbl ||; ˌɪnɪgˈzɔstəbḷ/adj that cannot be finished or used up completely 无穷尽的；用不完的: Our energy supplies are not inexhaustible. 我们的能源并非取之不尽。

inexpensive
/ˌɪnɪkˈspensɪv ||; ˌɪnɪkˈspɛnsɪv/adj low in price 便宜的: an inexpensive camping holiday 花费不多的露营式度假 [SYN] cheap 同义词为cheap [OPP] expensive 反义词为expensive ➔inexpensively adv

inexperience
/ˌɪnɪkˈspɪəriəns ||; ˌɪnɪkˈspɪrɪəns/noun [U] not knowing how to do sth because you have not done it before 缺乏经验；经验不足: The mistakes were all due to inexperience. 出现这些错误完全是因为经验不足。 [OPP] experience 反义词为experience ➔inexperienced adj He's too young and inexperienced to be given such responsibility. 他太年轻，经验不足，不能畀予这种重担。

inexplicable
/ˌɪnɪkˈsplɪkəbl ||; ˌɪnɪkˈsplɪkəbḷ/adj that cannot be explained 莫名其妙的；难以理解的；难以解释的: Her sudden disappearance is quite inexplicable. 她突然失踪，叫人百思不解。 [OPP] explicable 反义词为explicable ➔inexplicably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

infallible
/ɪnˈfæləbl ||; ɪnˈfæləbḷ/adj
1 (used about a person) never making mistakes or being wrong （指人）不会犯错的: Even the most careful typist is not infallible. 哪怕是最仔细的打字员也有出错的时候。
2 always doing what you want it to do; never failing 绝对可靠的: No computer is infallible. 哪台计算机都会出毛病。 [OPP] fallible 反义词为fallible ➔infallibility /ɪnˌfæləˈbɪləti ||; ɪnˌfæləˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

infamous
/ˈɪnfəməs ||; ˈɪnfəməs/adj infamous (for sth) famous for being bad 臭名昭著的: The area is infamous for drugs and crime. 这个地区因毒品和犯罪活动臭名远扬。 [SYN] notorious 同义词为notorious ☞Look at famous. 参看famous。

infancy
/ˈɪnfənsi ||; ˈɪnfənsɪ/noun [U] the time when you are a baby or young child 婴儿期；幼儿期 (figurative 比喻) Research in this field is still in its infancy. 这个领域的研究工作仍在起步阶段。

infant
/ˈɪnfənt ||; ˈɪnfənt/noun [C] a baby or very young child 婴儿；幼儿: There is a high rate of infant mortality (= many children die when they are still babies). 婴儿夭折率很高。 Mrs Davies teaches infants (= children aged between four and seven). 戴维斯太太是幼儿教师。 Baby, toddler and child are more common in spoken or informal English. 口语及非正式英语里，baby、toddler或child较为常用。
infanticide
/ɪnˈfæntɪsaɪd ||; ɪnˈfæntəˌsaɪd/noun (formal 正式) [U] [C] the crime of killing a baby, especially when a parent kills his/her own child 杀婴罪（尤指父母杀害自己的儿女）

infantile
/ˈɪnfəntaɪl ||; ˈɪnfənˌtaɪl/adj (of behaviour) typical of, or connected with, a baby or very young child and therefore not appropriate for adults or older children （行为）婴儿的，幼稚的: infantile jokes 孩子气的玩笑

infantry
/ˈɪnfəntri ||; ˈɪnfəntrɪ/noun [U] [with.sop] soldiers who fight on foot 步兵: The infantry was/were supported by heavy gunfire. 步兵得到强大炮火的支持。

ˈinfant school
noun [C] a school for children between the ages of four and seven 幼儿学校（对象是四岁至七岁的儿童）

infatuated
/ɪnˈfætʃueɪtɪd ||; ɪnˈfætʃυˌetɪd/adj infatuated (with sb/sth) having a very strong feeling of love or attraction for sb/sth that usually does not last long and makes you unable to think about anything else 迷恋，痴迷（常为不长久的）: The young girl was infatuated with one of her teachers. 这个小姑娘迷恋她的一位老师。 ➔infatuation /ɪnˌfætʃuˈeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌfætʃυˈeʃən/ noun [C,U]

*infect
/ɪnˈfekt ||; ɪnˈfɛkt/verb[T]
1 infect sb/sth (with sth) (usually passive 通常用于被动语态) to cause sb/sth to have a disease or illness 传染；使感染: We must clean the wound before it becomes infected. 尽快清洗伤口，免得受到感染。 Many thousands of people have been infected with the virus. 数以千计的人感染了这种病毒。
2 to make people share a particular feeling or emotion 感受；使受影响: Paul's happiness infected the whole family. 保罗的喜悦感染了全家上下。

*infection
/ɪnˈfekʃn ||; ɪnˈfɛkʃən/noun
1 [U] the act of becoming or making sb ill 传染；感染: A dirty water supply can be a source of infection. 不洁的供水可以成为感染疾病的来源。 There is a danger of infection. 有感染病毒的危险。
2 [C] a disease or illness that is caused by harmful bacteria, etc and affects one part of your body （身体某部份的）感染: She is suffering from a chest infection. 她肺部受了感染。 an ear infection 耳部感染
Infections can be caused by bacteria or viruses. An informal word for these is germs. 传染病的起因是感染了细菌(bacteria)或病毒(virus)。非正式场合用germ。

*infectious
/ɪnˈfekʃəs ||; ɪnˈfɛkʃəs/adj (used about a disease, illness, etc) that can be easily passed on to another person （指疾病等）传染的: Flu is very infectious. 流感极易传染。 (figurative 比喻) infectious laughter 很有感染力的笑声 Infectious diseases are usually passed on by the air that we breathe. Contagious diseases are passed from one person to another by touch. 通过呼吸传染的疾病叫做infectious diseases﹐通过接触传染的疾病则叫做contagious diseases。

infer
/ɪnˈfɜ:(r) ||; ɪnˈfɝ/verb [T] (inferring;inferred)infer sth (from sth) to form an opinion or decide that sth is true from the information you have （从…）归结或推断出…: I inferred from our conversation that he was unhappy with his job. 从我们的谈话中，可以推断出他不大满意那份工作。 ➔inference /ˈɪnfərəns/ noun [C]

inferior
/ɪnˈfɪəriə(r) ||; ɪnˈfɪrɪɚ/adj inferior (to sb/sth) low or lower in social position, importance, quality, etc （社会地位、重要性、质量等）低的，较低的，低下的: This material is obviously inferior to that one. 这种材料的质量显然不如那种材料。 Don't let people make you feel inferior. 不要让别人使你感到自卑。 [OPP] superior 反义词为superior ➔inferior noun [C]: She always treats me as her intellectual inferior. 她总是把我看作是智力上不如她的人。 ➔inferiority /ɪnˌfɪəriˈɒrəti; US -ˈɔ:r- ||; ɪnˌfɪrɪˈɔrətɪ/ noun [U]

infinite
/ˈɪnfɪnət ||; ˈɪnfənɪt/adj

2 without limits; that never ends 无穷；无限: Supplies of oil are not infinite. 石油供应并非取之不尽。 [OPP] finite 反义词为finite

infinitive
/ɪnˈfɪnətɪv ||; ɪnˈfɪnətɪv/noun [C] (grammar语法) the basic form of a verb （动词的）不定式，不定词 In English the infinitive can be used either with or without to depending on what comes before it He can sing. He wants to sing. 英语的动词不定式后面接不接to取决于前面的成分：He can sing.他会唱歌。·He wants to sing.他想唱歌。

/ɪnˈflekʃn ||; ɪnˈflɛkʃən/ (also inflexion) noun [C,U]
1 (grammar语法) a change in the form of a word, especially its ending, that changes its function in the grammar of the language, for example -ed, -est 词形的屈折变化，词形变化（尤指词尾变化，显示其语法功能的改变，如-ed、-est）

2 (used about a material) not able to bend or be bent easily （指材料）不可或不易弯曲的 [OPP] flexible 反义词为flexible ➔inflexibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv ➔inflexibility /ɪnˌfleksəˈbɪləti ||; ɪnˌflɛksəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U]

*influence¹
/ˈɪnfluəns ||; ˈɪnflυəns/noun
1 [U] [C] (an) influence (on/upon sb/sth) the power to affect, change or control sb/sth 影响；感化力；支配力: Television can have a strong influence on children. 电视对儿童可有强大的影响力。 Nobody should drive while they are under the influence of alcohol. 谁也不得酒后开车。
2 [C] an influence (on sb/sth) a person or thing that affects or changes sb/sth 产生影响的人或事物: His new girlfriend has been a good influence on him. 他的新女朋友对他有着好的影响。 cultural/environmental influences 文化╱环境影响
influence²
/ˈɪnfluəns ||; ˈɪnflυəns/verb [T] to have an effect on or power over sb/sth so that he/she/it changes 影响: You must decide for yourself. Don't let anyone else influence you. 你得自己拿主意，别让他人影响你。 Her style of painting has been influenced by Japanese art. 她的画风受到日本艺术的影响。 Affect and influence are often very similar in meaning. Affect is usually used when the change is physical and influence is more often used to describe a change of opinion or attitude Drinking alcohol can affect your ability to drive. TV advertisements have influenced my attitude towards the homeless. affect和influence的意义很相近。affect一般指生理或物质上的改变，influence较多用于指看法或态度上的改变：Drinking alcohol can affect your ability to drive.喝酒可影响驾驶能力。·TV advertisements have influenced my attitude towards the homeless.电视广告改变了我对无家可归的人的态度。
influential
/ˌɪnfluˈenʃl ||; ˌɪnflυˈɛnʃəl/adj influential (in sth/in doing sth) having power or influence 有影响力的: an influential politician 有影响力的政治家 He was influential in getting the hostages set free. 在让人质获释一事上，他发挥了作用。

*inform
/ɪnˈfɔ:m ||; ɪnˈfɔrm/verb [T] inform sb (of/about sth) to give sb information (about sth), especially in an official way 通知，告知（尤指通过正式途径）: You should inform the police of the accident. 你应该告之警方这起事故。 Do keep me informedof any changes. 有什么变动，请你通知我。 inform on sb to give information to the police, etc about what sb has done wrong 告发；密告: The wife of the killer informed on her husband. 杀人凶手的妻子告发了她的丈夫。

*informal
/ɪnˈfɔ:ml ||; ɪnˈfɔrmḷ/adj relaxed and friendly or suitable for a relaxed occasion 轻松友好的；不拘礼节的；非正式的: Don't get dressed up for the party -- it'll be very informal. 这个酒会十分不拘形式，用不着盛装出席。 The two leaders had informal discussions before the conference began. 两位领袖在会议之前进行过非正式的讨论。 [OPP] formal 反义词为formal ☞Some words and expressions in this dictionary are described as (informal). This means that you can use them when you are speaking to friends or people that you know well but that you should not use them in written work, official letters, etc. 本词典里有些词语、词组都有（informal非正式）这标示，表示这些词语可在跟熟人讲话时使用，书面语或正式信件则不宜用。 ➔informality /ˌɪnfɔ:ˈmæləti ||; ˌɪnfɔrˈmælətɪ/ noun [U]: an atmosphere of informality 轻松的气氛 ➔informally /-məli/ adv I was told informally (= unofficially) that our plans had been accepted. 我接到非正式的通知，我们的计划已经通过了。

*information
/ˌɪnfəˈmeɪʃn ||; ˌɪnfɚˈmeʃən/ (informal 非正式info) noun [U]: information (on/about sb/sth) knowledge or facts 资料；信息；信息: For further information please send for our fact sheet. 欲知详情，请来函索取简介。 Can you give me some information about evening classes in Italian, please? 可不可以给我一些有关意大利语晚间课程的资料？ The word information is uncountable so you CANNOT say: I need an information. You can, however, talk about a bit or piece of information. information为不可数名词，不能说I need an information，只可以说a bit／piece of information。

infringe
/ɪnˈfrɪndʒ ||; ɪnˈfrɪndʒ/verb (formal 正式)
1 [T] to break a rule, law, agreement, etc 违反（规则、法律、协议等）: The material can be copied without infringing copyright. 这篇材料可以复制，不会侵犯版权。
2 [I] infringe on/upon sth to reduce or limit sb's rights, freedom, etc 侵犯（某人的权利、自由等）: She refused to answer questions that infringed on her private affairs. 她拒绝回答涉及她隐私的问题。 ➔infringement noun [C,U]

infuse
/ɪnˈfju:z ||; ɪnˈfjuz/verb
1 [T] infuse A into B;infuse B with A(formal 正式) to make sb/sth have a particular quality 灌输；使具有某特质: Her novels are infused with sadness. 她的小说充满感伤。
2 [T] (formal 正式) to have an effect on all parts of sth 渗入；注入: Politics infuses all aspects of our lives. 政治渗入我们生活的各方面。
3 [I,T] if you infuse HERBS (= plants whose leaves are used to give flavour to sth or as medicine) or they infuse, you put them in hot water until the flavour has passed into the water （用热水）泡；泡制（草药）

infusion
/ɪnˈfju:ʒn ||; ɪnˈfjuʒən/noun
1 [C,U] infusion of sth (into sth)(formal 正式) the act of adding sth to sth else in order to make it stronger or more successful 注入；输送: an infusion of new talent into teaching 将有才华的新人送到教学岗位 The company needs an infusion of new blood (= new employees with new ideas). 这公司需要注入新鲜血液。
2 [C] a drink or medicine made by putting HERBS (= plants whose leaves are used to give flavour to sth or as medicine) in hot water 用热水泡制的饮料或草药
3 [C,U] (medical医学) the act of introducing a liquid substance into the body, especially into a VEIN 输液，输注（尤指到静脉）

ingenious

2 (used about a person) full of new ideas and clever at finding solutions to problems or at inventing things （指人）头脑灵敏的，足智多谋的 ➔ingeniously adv ➔ingenuity /ˌɪndʒəˈnju:əti; US -ˈnu:- ||; ˌɪndʒəˈnuətɪ/ noun [U]

/ɪnˈgreɪnd ||; ɪnˈgrend/adj ingrained (in sb/sth) (used about a habit, an attitude, etc) that has existed for a long time and is therefore difficult to change （指习惯、态度等）根深蒂固的: ingrained prejudices/beliefs 根深蒂固的偏见╱信念

ingratitude
/ɪnˈgrætɪtju:d; US -tu:d ||; ɪnˈgrætəˌtud/noun [U] (formal 正式) the state of not showing or feeling thanks for sth that has been done for you; not being grateful 没有感谢的心意或表示；忘恩负义 ☞A less formal word is ungratefulness. 不大正式的场合用ungratefulness。 [OPP] gratitude 反义词为gratitude

ingredient
/ɪnˈgri:diənt ||; ɪnˈgridɪənt/noun[C]
1 one of the items of food you need to make sth to eat （食物的）成分，配料: Mix all the ingredients together in a bowl. 把所有配料放在碗里拌和。
2 one of the qualities necessary to make sth successful （成功的）因素，要素: The film has all the ingredients of success. 这部电影具备成功的所有要素。

*inhabit
/ɪnˈhæbɪt ||; ɪnˈhæbɪt/verb [T] to live in a place 居住；栖息: Are the Aran Islands still inhabited (= do people live there)? 阿伦群岛上仍然有人居住吗？

inhabitant
/ɪnˈhæbɪtənt ||; ɪnˈhæbɪtənt/noun [C] [usu.pl] a person or animal that lives in a place 居住或栖息某地的人或动物: The local inhabitants protested at the plans for a new motorway. 当地居民强烈反对兴建新高速公路的计划。 ☞When you want to know how many people live in a particular place, you say What is the population of...? NOT How many inhabitants are there in...? However, when you answer this question you can say The population is 10000. OR It has 10000 inhabitants. 想知道某地有多少居民要说：What is the population of... ?不说：How many inhabitants are there in ... ?然而，回答这个问题时可说：The population is 10000.／It has 10000 inhabitants.

inhale
/ɪnˈheɪl ||; ɪnˈhel/verb [I,T] to breathe in 吸气；吸入: Be careful not to inhale the fumes from the paint. 小心不要吸入油漆的气味。 [OPP] exhale 反义词为exhale ➔inhalation /ˌɪnhəˈleɪʃn ||; ˌɪnhəˈleʃən/ noun [U]: They were treated for the effects of smoke inhalation. 他们吸入烟雾感到不适，接受了治疗。

inhaler
/ɪnˈheɪlə(r) ||; ɪnˈhelɚ/noun [C] a small device containing medicine that you breathe in through your mouth, used by people who have problems with breathing 吸入器（内装药物，用嘴吸入，供呼吸有困难的人使用）

inherent
/ɪnˈhɪərənt ||; ɪnˈhɪrənt/adj inherent (in sb/sth) that is a basic or permanent part of sb/sth and that cannot be removed 内在的；固有的: The risk of collapse is inherent in any business. 任何企业都有倒闭的风险。 inherently adv No matter how safe we make them, cars are inherently dangerous. 无论想出什么保险办法，汽车有其固有的危险性。

inherit
/ɪnˈherɪt ||; ɪnˈhɛrɪt/verb [T] inherit sth (from sb)
1 to receive property, money, etc from sb who has died 继承（遗产）: I inherited quite a lot of money from my mother. She left me $12000 when she died. 我继承了妈妈的一大笔钱。她死时留给我12000元。 ☞Look at heir. 参看heir。 ☞Look at disinherit. 参看disinherit。
2 to receive a quality, characteristic, etc from your parents or family 经遗传而得（特性、特点等）: She has inherited her father's gift for languages. 她的语言天分得自父亲的遗传。

inheritance
/ɪnˈherɪtəns ||; ɪnˈhɛrɪtəns/noun [C,U] the act of inheriting; the money, property, etc that you inherit 继承；遗产: inheritance tax 遗产税

inhibit
/ɪnˈhɪbɪt ||; ɪnˈhɪbɪt/verb[T]
1 to prevent sth or make sth happen more slowly 阻止；抑制: a drug to inhibit the growth of tumours 抑制肿瘤生长的药物
2 inhibit sb (from sth/from doing sth) to make sb nervous and embarrassed so that he/she is unable to do sth 约束；使拘束: The fact that her boss was there inhibited her from saying what she really felt. 她的老板在场，所以她很拘束，不敢说心里话。 ➔inhibited adj The young man felt shy and inhibited in the roomful of women. 在满屋子的女人面前，这个小伙子又害羞又拘谨。 [OPP] uninhibited 反义词为uninhibited

inhibition
/ˌɪnhɪˈbɪʃn;ˌɪnɪˈb- ||; ˌɪnhɪˈbɪʃən,; ˌɪnɪˈb-/noun [C,U] a shy or nervous feeling that stops you from saying or doing what you really want 拘束；拘谨: After the first day of the course, people started to lose their inhibitions. 第一天课程结束以后，大家开始无拘无束了。

inhospitable
/ˌɪnhɒˈspɪtəbl ||; ɪnˈhɑspɪtəbḷ/adj
1 (used about a place) not pleasant to live in, especially because of the weather （指地方）不适宜居住的（尤指因为天气）: the inhospitable Arctic regions 不适宜居住的北极地区
2 (used about a person) not friendly or welcoming to guests （指人）不好客的 [OPP] hospitable 反义词为hospitable

inhuman
/ɪnˈhju:mən ||; ɪnˈhjumən/adj
1 very cruel and without pity 残酷的；不人道的；非人的: inhuman treatment/conditions 非人的待遇╱条件
2 not seeming to be human and therefore frightening 不像人类的；可怕的: an inhuman noise 骇人的声音

inhumane
/ˌɪnhju:ˈmeɪn ||; ˌɪnhjuˈmen/adj very cruel; not caring if people or animals suffer 残酷的；不人道的: the inhumane conditions in which animals are kept on some large farms 一些大农庄里动物受到的不人道待遇 [OPP] humane 反义词为humane

inhumanity
/ˌɪnhju:ˈmænəti ||; ˌɪnhjuˈmænətɪ/noun [U] very cruel behaviour 惨无人道的行为: The twentieth century is full of examples of man's inhumanity to man. 二十世纪充斥着人类互相残暴对待的例子。 [OPP] humanity 反义词为humanity

*initial¹
/ɪˈnɪʃl ||; ɪˈnɪʃəl/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) happening at the beginning; first 最初的；开始的: My initial reaction was to refuse, but I later changed my mind. 我最初的反应是拒绝，但后来改变了主意。 the initial stages of our survey 我们这个调查的最初阶段
*initial²
/ɪˈnɪʃl ||; ɪˈnɪʃəl/noun [C] [usu.pl] the first letter of a name （姓名的）首字母: Alison Elizabeth Waters' initials are A.E.W. Alison Elizabeth Waters的首字母是A.E.W。
initial³
/ɪˈnɪʃl ||; ɪˈnɪʃəl/verb [T] (initialling;initialled (US 美) initialing;initialed) to mark or sign sth with your initials 用姓名的首字母作标记或签名: Any changes made when writing a cheque should be initialled by you. 开支票时如有涂改，要用姓名的首字母签名。

initially
/ɪˈnɪʃəli ||; ɪˈnɪʃəlɪ/adv at the beginning; at first 最初；起初: I liked the job initially but it soon got quite boring. 我最初挺喜欢这份工作，可是不久就觉得相当枯燥乏味了。

initiate
/ɪˈnɪʃieɪt ||; ɪˈnɪʃɪˌet/verb[T]
1 (formal 正式) to start sth 着手进行；开始: to initiate peace talks 展开和谈
2 initiate sb (into sth) to explain sth to sb or make him/her experience sth for the first time 初步传授；使初步经历: I wasn't initiated into the joys of skiing until I was 30. 我到30岁才领略滑雪之乐。
3 initiate sb (into sth) to bring sb into a group by means of a special ceremony （通过特别仪式）使（某人）加入（某组织）: to initiate sb into a secret society 正式接纳某人加入秘密会社 ➔initiation /-ˈeɪʃn ||; -ˈeʃən/ noun [U]: All the new students had to go through a strange initiation ceremony. 所有的新生都得经过古怪的入会仪式。

*initiative
/ɪˈnɪʃətɪv ||; ɪˈnɪʃɪətɪv/noun
1 [C] official action that is taken to solve a problem or improve a situation 为了解决问题或改善情势而作出的正式行动: a new government initiative to help people start small businesses 政府为协助人民开办小企业的新措施
2 [U] the ability to see and do what is necessary without waiting for sb to tell you 主动性；自发性: Don't keep asking me how to do it. Use your initiative. 不要老问我怎么做，你要发挥主观能动性。
3 the initiative [sing] the stronger position because you have done sth first; the advantage 有利的位置；主动权: The enemy forces have lost the initiative. 敌军丧失了主动权。
on your own initiative without being told by sb else what to do 主动地 take the initiative to be first to act to influence a situation 采取主动；发起: Let's take the initiative and start organizing things now. 我们采取主动吧，现在就着手筹备工作。

*inject
/ɪnˈdʒekt ||; ɪnˈdʒɛkt/verb[T]
1 to put a drug under the skin of person's or an animal's body with a needle (syringe) 注射
2 inject sth (into sth) to add sth 加入；注入: They injected a lot of money into the business. 他们给这家企业投入了巨款。

*injection
/ɪnˈdʒekʃn ||; ɪnˈdʒɛkʃən/noun
1 [C,U] (an) injection (of sth) (into sb/sth) the act of putting a drug or substance under the skin of a person's or an animal's body with a needle (a syringe) 注射: to give sb an injection 给某人注射 a tetanus injection 破伤风注射剂: An anaesthetic was administered by injection. 以注射进行麻醉。 [SYN] jab 同义词为jab
2 [C] a large amount of sth that is added to sth to help it 投入的大量…: The theatre needs a huge cash injection if it is to stay open. 这家剧院需要投入巨额现金才不致倒闭。
3 [U] [C] the act of forcing liquid into sth 喷射: fuel injection 燃油喷射

*injury

*innocence
/ˈɪnəsns ||; ˈɪnəsṇs/noun [U]:

*innocent
/ˈɪnəsnt ||; ˈɪnəsṇt/adj
1 innocent (of sth) not having done wrong 清白的；无罪的: An innocent man was arrested by mistake. 有个无辜的男子被错误逮捕了。 to be innocent of a crime 清白无罪 [SYN] blameless 同义词为blameless [OPP] guilty 反义词为guilty
2 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) being hurt or killed in a crime, war, etc although not involved in it in any way 在罪行、战争等中受伤或遇害的（虽然没有参与）；无辜的: innocent victims of a bomb blast 炸弹爆炸事件中的无辜受害者 an innocent bystander 无辜的旁观者
3 not wanting to cause harm or upset sb, although it does 非故意伤害或令人不高兴的: He got very aggressive when I asked an innocent question about his past life. 我问了一个有关他过去生活的问题，并无恶意，他却变得满怀敌意。
4 not knowing the bad things in life; believing everything you are told 不谙世情；天真: She was so innocent as to believe that politicians never lie. 她天真到以为政治家从不撒谎。 [SYN] naive 同义词为naive ➔innocently adv ‘What are you doing here?’ she asked innocently (= pretending she did not know the answer). “你们在这儿干什么呀？”她假装不知道地问。

*insect
/ˈɪnsekt ||; ˈɪnsɛkt/noun [C] a small animal with six legs, two pairs of wings and a body which is divided into three parts 昆虫: Ants, flies, beetles, butterflies and mosquitoes are all insects. 蚂蚁、苍蝇、甲虫、蝴蝶、蚊子都是昆虫。 an insect bite/sting 虫咬╱螫 ☞ Some other small animals, for example spiders, are often also called insects although this is technically incorrect. 其他有些小动物如蜘蛛一般也叫昆虫，虽然在学术上是不确切的。

insecure
/ˌɪnsɪˈkjʊə(r) ||; ˌɪnsɪˈkjυr/adj
1 insecure (about sb/sth) not confident about yourself or your relationships with other people 对自己或跟别人的关系缺乏信心的；焦虑不安的: Many teenagers are insecure about their appearance. 许多青少年对自己的外表感到局促不安。
2 not safe or protected 不安全的；无保障的: This ladder feels a bit insecure. 这梯子令人觉得不大安全。 The future of the company looks very insecure. 公司的前景看来很不稳固。 [OPP] secure 反义词为secure ➔insecurely adv ➔insecurity /-rəti/ noun [uc] (plural insecurities) Their aggressive behaviour is really a sign of insecurity. 他们那种侵略性行为其实反映了内心的不安。 [OPP] security 反义词为security

*inside¹
/ˌɪnˈsaɪd ||; ɪnˈsaɪd/prep adj adv
1 in, on or to the inner part or surface of sth 内部或内面的；在或往内部、里面；在…里面: Is there anything inside the box? 箱子里有没有东西？ It's safer to be inside the house in a thunderstorm. 遇有雷暴，留在屋内较安全。 We'd better stay inside until the rain stops. 我们最好待在里面，等雨停了再出去。 It's getting cold. Let's go inside. 越来越冷了，我们到里边去吧。 the inside pages of a newspaper 报纸的内版
2 (formal 正式) (used about time) in less than; within （指时间）少于，在…之内: Your photos will be ready inside an hour. 你的照片一个钟头内可以冲好。
3 (used about information, etc) told secretly by sb who belongs to a group, organization, etc （指信息等）外界不知道的，内幕的: The robbers seemed to have had some inside information about the bank's security system. 看来劫匪掌握了一些有关这家银行保安系统的内情。
4 (slang 俚语) in prison 坐牢；在狱中
*inside²
/ˌɪnˈsaɪd ||; ˈɪnˈsaɪd/noun

2 insides [pl] (informal 非正式) the organs inside the body 内脏: The coffee warmed his insides. 他喝了咖啡觉得肚子里暖呼呼的。
inside out
1 with the inner surface on the outside 里面朝外: You've got your jumper on inside out. 你把羊毛套衫穿反了。 ☞picture at back 见back插图

*insist
/ɪnˈsɪst ||; ɪnˈsɪst/verb[I]
1 insist (on sth/doing sth);insist that... to say strongly that you must have or do sth, or that sb else must do sth 坚决要求，坚持（要做某事）: He always insists on the best. 他总是要求完美。 Dan insisted on coming too. 丹也坚持要来。 My parents insist that I come home by taxi. 父母千叮万嘱要我搭出租车回家。 ‘Have another drink.’ ‘Oh all right, if you insist.’ “再喝一杯吧。”“好吧，如果你坚持的话。”
2 insist (on sth);insist that... to say firmly that sth is true (when sb does not believe you) 坚称（某事属实）: She insisted on her innocence. 她坚持说自己是清白的。 James insisted that the accident wasn't his fault. 詹姆斯坚决认为这起事故不是他的过失。 ➔insistence noun [U]

*inspect

/ˌɪnspəˈreɪʃn ||; ˌɪnspəˈreʃən/noun
1 [C,U] an inspiration (to/for sb);inspiration (to do/for sth) a feeling, person or thing that makes you want to do sth or gives you exciting new ideas 灵感；触发灵感的人或事物: The beauty of the mountains was a great source of inspiration to the writer. 山间的美景是作者灵感的重要泉源。 What gave you the inspiration to become a dancer? 是什么激发你去当舞蹈家的？

inspire
/ɪnˈspaɪə(r) ||; ɪnˈspaɪr/verb[T]

*institute¹
/ˈɪnstɪtju:t; US -tu:t ||; ˈɪnstəˌtut/noun [C] an organization that has a particular purpose; the building used by this organization 有特定目的的组织；此类组织使用的建筑物: the Institute of Science and Technology 科技学院 institutes of higher education 高等教育机构

*institution
/ˌɪnstɪˈtju:ʃn; US -tu:ʃn ||; ˌɪnstəˈtuʃən/noun
1 [C] a large, important organization that has a particular purpose, such as a bank, a university, etc （有特定目的的）大机构（如银行、大学等）: the financial institutions in the City of London 伦敦商业区的金融机构
2 [C] a building where certain people with special needs live and are looked after 为有特殊需要者设立的建筑物: a mental institution (= a hospital for the mentally ill) 精神病院 She's been in institutions all her life. 她在不同的特殊服务机构里度过了一辈子。
3 [C] a social custom or habit that has existed for a long time 习俗；惯例: the institution of marriage 婚姻制度
4 [U] the act of introducing a system, policy, etc, or of starting a process 建立；设立；制定: the institution of new safety procedures 制定新的安全程度

institutional
/ˌɪnstɪˈtju:ʃənl ||; ˌɪnstəˈtuʃənḷ/adj connected with an institution 与大机构、特殊用途建筑物或制度有关的: The old lady is in need of institutional care. 这位老太太需要有关机构的照料。

*instruct
/ɪnˈstrʌkt ||; ɪnˈstrʌkt/verb[T]
1 instruct sb (to do sth) to give an order to sb; to tell sb to do sth 命令；指示: The soldiers were instructed to shoot above the heads of the crowd. 士兵接到指示，奉命朝群众头顶上空开火。
2 (formal 正式)instruct sb (in sth) to teach sb sth 教导: Children must be instructed in road safety before they are allowed to ride a bike on the road. 必须先教导儿童道路安全知识，才可以让他们在路上骑自行车。

*instruction
/ɪnˈstrʌkʃn ||; ɪnˈstrʌkʃən/noun
1 instructions [pl] detailed information on how you should use sth, do sth, etc 说明（书）；用法；做法: Read the instructions on the back of the packet carefully. 仔细读读包装背后的说明。 You should always follow the instructions. 你一定要按说明书办事。
2 [C] an instruction (to do sth) an order that tells you what to do or how to do sth 命令；指示: The guard was under strict instructionsnot to let anyone in or out. 守恒接到指示，严禁任何人出入。
3 [U] instruction (in sth) the act of teaching sth to sb 教导；指导: The staff need instruction in the use of computers. 员工们需要接受使用计算机指导。

instructive
/ɪnˈstrʌktɪv ||; ɪnˈstrʌktɪv/adj giving useful information 有教益的；增进有用知识的 ➔instructively adv

instructor
/ɪnˈstrʌktə(r) ||; ɪnˈstrʌktɚ/noun [C] a person whose job is to teach a practical skill or sport 教练: a driving/fitness/golf instructor 驾驶╱健身╱高尔夫球教练

*instrument
/ˈɪnstrəmənt ||; ˈɪnstrəmənt/noun[C]
1 a tool that is used for doing a particular job or task 器械；工具；仪器: surgical/optical/precision instruments 外科器材；光学仪器；精密仪器 ☞ Look at the note at tool. 参看tool的注释。
2 something that is used for playing music 乐器: ‘What instrument do you play?’ ‘The violin.’ “你演奏什么乐器？”“小提琴。” ☞picture at music 见music插图
Musical instruments may be stringed (violins, guitars, etc), brass (horns, trumpets, etc), woodwind (flutes, clarinets, etc) or keyboard (piano, organ, synthesizer, etc). Percussion instruments include drums and cymbals. 乐器(musical instrument)分为以下几类：弦乐器(strings)（小提琴、吉他等）、铜管乐器(brass)（号、小号等）、木管乐器(woodwind)（长笛、单簧管等）、键盘乐器(keyboard)（钢琴、风琴、音响合成器等）。鼓、钹都是打击乐器(percussion)。
3 something that is used for measuring speed, distance, temperature, etc in a car, plane or ship 仪表: the instrument panel of a plane 飞机的仪表板
4 something that sb uses in order to achieve sth 手段；工具: The press should be more than an instrument of the government. 报刊不该仅为政府服务。

*instrumental
/ˌɪnstrəˈmentl ||; ˌɪnstrəˈmɛntḷ/adj
1 instrumental in doing sth helping to make sth happen 起推动作用的: She was instrumental in getting him the job. 她促使他获得这份工作。
2 for musical instruments without voices 用乐器演奏（不含声乐部份）的: instrumental music 器乐

insubordinate
/ˌɪnsəˈbɔ:dɪnət ||; ˌɪnsəˈbɔrdṇɪt/adj (formal 正式) (used about a person or behaviour) not obeying rules or orders （指人或行为）不服从（规定或命令），抗命 ➔insubordination /ˌɪnsəˌbɔ:dɪˈneɪʃn ||; ˌɪnsəˌbɔrdṇˈeʃən/ noun [C,U] He was dismissed from the army for insubordination. 他因为不服从命令而被开除军籍。

insubstantial
/ˌɪnsəbˈstænʃl ||; ˌɪnsəbˈstænʃəl/adj not large, solid or strong 不大的；不结实的；不坚固的: a hut built of insubstantial materials 用不大坚固的材料盖起来的小屋 [OPP] substantial 反义词为substantial

insufferable
/ɪnˈsʌfrəbl ||; ɪnˈsʌfrəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) (used about a person or behaviour) extremely unpleasant or annoying （指人或行为）极度讨厌的，令人难以忍受的

insufficient
/ˌɪnsəˈfɪʃnt ||; ˌɪnsəˈfɪʃənt/adj insufficient (for sth/to do sth) not enough 不足的；不充分的: The students complained that they were given insufficient time for the test. 学生抱怨没有给足够的时间来准备考试。 [OPP] sufficient 反义词为sufficient ➔insufficiently adv

insular
/ˈɪnsjələ(r); US -sələr ||; ˈɪnsəlɚ/adj not interested in or able to accept new people or different ideas 思想狭隘的；褊狭保守的 [SYN] narrow-minded 同义词为narrow-minded ➔insularity /ˌɪnsjəˈlærəti; US -səˈl- ||; ˌɪnsəˈlærətɪ/ noun [U]

insulate
/ˈɪnsjuleɪt; US -səl- ||; ˈɪnsəˌlet/verb [T] insulate sth (against/from sth) to protect sth with a material that prevents electricity, heat or sound from passing through 使绝缘；使隔热；使隔音: The walls are insulated against noise. 这墙有隔音设备。 (figurative 比喻) This industry has been insulated from the effects of competition. 这个行业一直不受竞争的影响。 ➔insulation /ˌɪnsjuˈleɪʃn ||; ˌɪnsəˈleʃən/ noun [U]

ˈinsulating tape
noun [U] a thin band of sticky material used for covering electrical wires to prevent the possibility of an electric shock 绝缘胶带

/ˈɪnsjuleɪtə(r) ||; ˈɪnsəˌletɚ/noun [C] a material or device used to prevent heat, electricity or sound from escaping from sth 绝热体；绝缘体；隔音物 ☞picture at bulb 见bulb插图

insulin
/ˈɪnsjəlɪn ||; ˈɪnsəlɪn/noun [U] a substance, normally produced by the body itself, which controls the amount of sugar in the blood 胰岛素: a diabetic relies on insulin injections 糖尿病患者依赖胰岛素制剂注射

*insult¹
/ɪnˈsʌlt ||; ɪnˈsʌlt/verb [T] to speak or act rudely to sb 侮辱；辱骂: I felt very insulted when I didn't even get an answer to my letter. 连回信也没有，我觉得受到侮辱。 He was thrown out of the hotel for insulting the manager. 他因为侮辱经理而给撵出了饭店。
insult²
/ˈɪnsʌlt ||; ˈɪnsʌlt/noun [C] a rude remark or action 侮辱；辱骂: The drivers were standing in the road yelling insults at each other. 司机站在马路上互相叫骂。

insuperable
/ɪnˈsu:pərəbl ||; ɪnˈsupərəbḷ/adj (formal 正式) (used about a problem, etc) impossible to solve （指难题、困难等）无法解决的，难以克服的

*insurance
/ɪnˈʃɔ:rəns; US -ˈʃʊər- ||; ɪnˈʃυrəns/noun
1 [U] insurance (against sth) an arrangement with a company in which you pay them regular amounts of money and they agree to pay the costs if, for example, you die or are ill, or if you lose or damage sth 保险: Builders should always have insurance against personal injury. 建筑工人应该时常受人身伤害保险的保障。
We take out an insurance policy. An insurance premium is the regular amount you pay to the insurance company. We can take out life, health, car, travel and household insurance. 投保叫做take out an insurance policy。保险费(insurance premium)是定期付予保险公司的费用。各类保险包括人寿保险(life insurance)、健康保险(health insurance)、汽车保险(car insurance)、旅游保险(travel insurance)和家居保险(household insurance)。
2 [U] the business of providing insurance 保险业: He works in insurance. 他从事保险业。
3 [U] [sing] (an) insurance (against sth) something you do to protect yourself (against sth unpleasant) 保障；防备；预防: Many people take vitamin pills as an insurance against illness. 很多人服用维生素丸以防疾病。

*insure
/ɪnˈʃɔ:(r); US ɪnˈʃʊər ||; ɪnˈʃυr/verb[T]
1 insure yourself/sth (against/for sth) to buy or to provide insurance 投保；承保: They insured the painting for £10000 against damage or theft. 他们为这幅画买了10000英镑的损毁或盗窃保险。
2 (US 美) =ENSURE

intake
/ˈɪnteɪk ||; ˈɪnˌtek/noun[C] [usu.sing]
1 the amount of food, drink, etc that you take into your body （食物、饮料等的）摄取量: The doctor told David to cut down his alcohol intake. 医生嘱咐戴维减少饮酒量。
2 the (number of) people who enter an organization or institution during a certain period （在一定时期内组织或机构的）新成员，新成员数目: This year's intake of students is down 10%. 今年招收的新生减少了一成。
3 the act of taking sth into your body, especially breath 摄取（尤指空气）
4 a place where liquid, air, etc enters a machine （液体、气体等进入机器的）入口

intangible
/ɪnˈtændʒəbl ||; ɪnˈtændʒəbḷ/adj difficult to describe, understand or measure 难以描述的；难以衡量的；不易捉摸的；无形的: The benefits of good customer relations are intangible. 与客户有良好关系所带来的好处是无形的。 [OPP] tangible 反义词为tangible

integral
/ˈɪntɪgrəl ||; ˈɪntəgrəl/adj

2 including sth as a part 包括在内的: The car has an integral CD player. 汽车装有激光唱片唱机。

integrate
/ˈɪntɪgreɪt ||; ˈɪntəˌgret/verb
1 [T] integrate sth (into sth);integrate A and B/integrate A with B to join things so that they become one thing or work together 使成为一体: The two small schools were integrated into one large one. 这两所规模小的学校合并成一所规模大的学校。 These programs will integrate with your existing software. 这些程序将跟现存的软件配套。
2 [I,T] integrate (sb) (into/with sth) to join in and become part of a group or community, or to make sb do this （使）融入: It took Amir a while to integrate into his new school. 埃米尔过了一段时间才融入新的学校。 ☞ Look at segregate. 参看segregate。 ➔integration /ˌɪntɪˈgreɪʃn ||; ˌɪntəˈgreʃən/ noun [U]: racial integration 种族融合 ☞ Look at segregation. 参看segregation。

*intellectual¹

*intelligence

*intend
/ɪnˈtend ||; ɪnˈtɛnd/verb[T]
1 intend to do sth/doing sth to plan or mean to do sth 计划；打算: I'm afraid I spent more money than I had intended. 我的开支恐怕超出了预算。 I certainly don't intend to wait here all day! 我当然不打算在这儿等一整天！ They had intended staying in Wales for two weeks but the weather was so bad that they left after one. 他们本来打算在威尔士逗留两个星期，可是天气太差，只待一个星期便离开了。 ☞noun intention 名词为intention
2 intend sth for sb/sth;intend sb to do sth to plan, mean or make sth for a particular person or purpose 为…而准备；预定；打算使…: You shouldn't have read that letter -- it wasn't intended for you. 你不该看那封信，它不是给你的。 I didn't intend you to have all the work. 我没有想让你把所有工作都包揽下来。

*intense
/ɪnˈtens ||; ɪnˈtɛns/adj very great, strong or serious 强烈的；严重的: intense heat/cold/pressure 酷热；严寒；高压 intense anger/interest/desire 盛怒；浓厚的兴趣；强烈的欲望 ➔intensely adv They obviously dislike each other intensely. 他们显然都十分讨厌对方。 ➔intensity /-səti ||; -sətɪ/ noun [U]: I wasn't prepared for the intensity of his reaction to the news. 我没有想到他对这个消息的反应会这么强烈。

intensive

intent¹
/ɪnˈtent ||; ɪnˈtɛnt/adj
1 intent (on/upon sth) showing great attention 专注的；用心的: She was so intent upon her work that she didn't hear me come in. 她工作很专心，我进来她也没有听见。
2 intent on/upon sth/doing sth determined to do sth 一心想…: He's always been intent on making a lot of money. 他总是想赚大钱。 ➔intently adv
intent²
/ɪnˈtent ||; ɪnˈtɛnt/noun [U] (formal 正式) what sb intends to do; intention 意图；意向: He was charged with possession of a gun with intent to commit a robbery. 他被控持有枪枝企图抢劫。 to do sth with evil/good intent 怀着恶意╱善意干某事 to/for all intents and purposes in effect, even if not completely true 实际上；即使不尽然: When they scored their fourth goal the match was, to all intents and purposes, over. 他们射进第四球的时候，比赛实际上已结束了。

*intention
/ɪnˈtenʃn ||; ɪnˈtɛnʃən/noun [C,U] (an) intention (of doing sth/to do sth) what sb intends or means to do; a plan or purpose 意图；打算；计划；目的: Our intention was to leave early in the morning. 我们打算一早就走。 I have no intention of staying indoors on a nice sunny day like this. 天气这么好，阳光灿烂，我可不想呆在屋里。 I borrowed the money with the intention of paying it back the next day. 我借了钱，打算第二天就还。

*intentional
/ɪnˈtenʃənl ||; ɪnˈtɛnʃənḷ/adj done on purpose, not by chance 故意的: I'm sorry I took your jacket -- it wasn't intentional! 我不小心拿了你的上衣，真对不起！ [SYN] synonym deliberate 同义词为deliberate [OPP] unintentional or inadvertent 反义词为unintentional或inadvertent ➔intentionally /-ʃənəli ||; -ʃnəlɪ/ adv I can't believe the boys broke the window intentionally. 我无法相信那些男孩是故意把窗子打破的。

inter-
/ˈɪntə(r) ||; ˈɪntɚ/prefix (in verbs, nouns, adjectives and adverbs) between; from one to another （用于构成动词、名词、形容词及副词）在…之间，相互: interface 接合部位 interaction 相互作用 international 国际的 ☞Compare intra-. 与intra-比较。

interact
/ˌɪntərˈækt ||; ˌɪntɚˈækt/verb[I]
1 interact (with sb) (used about people) to communicate or mix with sb, especially while you work, play or spend time together （指人）相处，交往: He is studying the way children interact with each other at different ages. 他正在研究不同年纪的儿童与同辈的相互影响。
2 (of two things) to have an effect on each other （两个事物）互相作用 ➔interaction noun [U, C]: interaction (between/with sb/sth): There is a need for greater interaction between the two departments. 这两个部门需要更好地互相配合。

interactive
/ˌɪntərˈæktɪv ||; ˌɪntɚˈæktɪv/adj

2 (computing计算机技术) involving direct communication both ways, between the computer and the person using it 人机互动的；交互式的；交互式的: interactive computer games 交互式计算机游戏

intercom
/ˈɪntəkɒm ||; ˈɪntɚˌkɑm/noun [C] a system of communication by radio or telephone inside an office, plane, etc; the device you press or switch on to start using this system （用于办公室、飞机等的）内部通话系统，对讲机

interconnect
/ˌɪntəkəˈnekt ||; ˌɪntɚkəˈnɛkt/verb [I,T] interconnect (A) (with B);interconnect A and B to connect similar things; to be connected to similar things （使类似事物）互相连接；连接到（类似事物）: electronic networks which interconnect thousands of computers around the world 使全世界数以千计的计算机互相连接的电子网络

intercontinental

*interest¹
/ˈɪntrəst ||; ˈɪntrɪst/noun
1 [U] [sing] an interest (in sb/sth) a desire to learn or hear more about sb/sth or to be involved with sb/sth 兴趣 [sing] She's begun to show a great interestin politics. 她开始对政治显示浓厚的兴趣。 I wish he'd take more interest inhis children. 我但愿他多关心一下自己的孩子。 Don't lose interest now! 现在可不能虎头蛇尾呀！
2 [U] the quality that makes sth interesting 趣味: I thought this article might be of interest to you. 我以为这篇文章会令你感兴趣。 Computers hold no interest for me. 计算机对我没有吸引力。 places of historical interest 历史名胜
3 [C] [usu.pl] something that you enjoy doing or learning about 感兴趣的事物: What are your interests and hobbies? 你有些什么兴趣和爱好？
4 [U] interest (on sth) the money that you pay for borrowing money from a bank, etc or the money that you earn when you keep money in a bank, etc 利息: We pay 6% interest on our mortgage at the moment. 目前我们付利率6厘的抵押贷款利息。 The interest rate has never been so high/low. 利率从来没有这么高╱低。 Some companies offer interest-free loans. 有些公司提供免息贷款。
have/with sb's interests at heart to want sb to be happy and successful, even though your actions may not show it 内心希望某人幸福、成功，以某人利益为念（即使行动上没有表现出来）: Don't be angry with your father -- you know he has your best interests at heart. 别生你父亲的气─你要知道，他心里总是为你设想。 in sb's interest(s) to sb's advantage 有利于某人；于…有益: Using lead-free petrol is in the public interest. 使用无铅汽油对大众有利。 in the interest(s) of sth in order to achieve or protect sth 为了实现或保护某事物；为…计；为…着想: In the interest(s) of safety, please fasten your seat belts. 为安全起见，请系上安全带。
*interest²
/ˈɪntrəst ||; ˈɪntrɪst/verb [T] to make sb want to learn or hear more about sth or to become involved in sth 使感兴趣；使介入: It might interest you to know that I didn't accept the job. 你或许想知道，我没有接受那份工作。 The subject of the talk was one that interests me greatly. 我对这个讲演题目很感兴趣。 interest sb in sth to persuade sb to buy, have, do sth 使某人有购买、拥有或做的欲望: Can I interest you in our new brochure? 我给你介绍一下这本新手册，好吗？

*interested
/ˈɪntrəstɪd ||; ˈɪntrɪstɪd/adj
1 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) interested (in sth/sb);interested in doing sth;interested to do sth wanting to know or hear more about sth/sb; enjoying or liking sth/sb （对…）感兴趣: They weren't interested in my news at all! 他们对我这个消息毫无兴趣！ I'm really not interested in going to university. 我确实不想上大学。 I was interested to hear that you've got a new job. Where is it? 听说你找了一份新工作，告诉我，在什么地方上班？ [OPP] uninterested 反义词为uninterested
If you like what you are doing, and want to know or hear more, then you are interested in it. The person or thing that makes you feel like this is interesting. 对某事物感兴趣要用interested，某人或某事物令你产生兴趣叫做interesting。
2 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) involved in or affected by sth; in a position to gain from sth 和…有关连；有利害关系的: As an interested party (= a person directly involved), I was not allowed to vote. 作为当事人，我不得参加表决。 [OPP] disinterested 反义词为disinterested

*interesting
/ˈɪntrəstɪŋ;-trest- ||; ˈɪntrəstɪŋ; -təˌrɛst-/adj interesting (to do sth);interesting that... enjoyable and entertaining; holding your attention 有趣的；有意思的: an interesting person/book/idea/job 有趣的人╱书╱主意╱工作 It's always interesting to hear about the customs of other societies. 异域风俗总能引起大家的兴趣。 It's interesting that Luisa chose Peru for a holiday. 路易莎决定去秘鲁度假，真有意思。 ➔interestingly adv

interface¹
/ˈɪntəfeɪs ||; ˈɪntɚˌfes/noun[C]
1 (computing计算机技术) the way a computer program presents information to or receives information from the person who is using it, in particular the LAYOUT of the screen and the MENUS （计算机程序与用户的）界面: the user interface 用户界面
2 (computing计算机技术) an electrical CIRCUIT, connection or program that joins one device or system to a another 接口: the interface between computer and printer 计算机与打印机的之间的接口
3 an interface (between A and B)(written 书面语) the point where two subjects, systems, etc meet and affect each other 相互连系: the interface between manufacturing and sales 生产与销售之间的相互连系
interface²
/ˈɪntəfeɪs ||; ˈɪntɚˌfes/verb [I,T] interface (sth) (with sth);interface A and B(computing计算机技术) to be connected with sth using an interface; to connect sth in this way （使）用连系程序接合: The new system interfaces with existing telephone equipment. 新系统与现存的电话设备接合。

*interfere
/ˌɪntəˈfɪə(r) ||; ˌɪntɚˈfɪr/verb[I]
1 interfere (in sth) to get involved in a situation which does not involve you and where you are not wanted 干涉；干预: You shouldn't interfere in your children's lives -- let them make their own decisions. 让孩子自己做决定，你不要干预他们的生活。
2 interfere (with sb/sth) to prevent sth from succeeding or to slow down the progress that sb/sth makes 妨碍；干扰: Every time the telephone rings it interferes with my work. 电话一响就干扰我的工作。 She never lets her private life interfere with her career. 她从来不让私生活干扰自己的事业。
3 interfere (with sth) to touch or change sth without permission 未经许可就接触或改变（某事物）；乱动…: Many people feel that scientists shouldn't interfere with nature. 很多人认为科学家不该干碍大自然。 ➔interfering adj

interference
/ˌɪntəˈfɪərəns ||; ˌɪntɚˈfɪrəns/noun [U]:
1 interference (in sth) the act of getting involved in a situation that does not involve you and where you are not wanted 干涉；干预: I left home because I couldn't stand my parents' interference in my affairs. 我离家是因为受不了父母干涉我的事情。
2 extra noise (because of other signals or bad weather) that prevents you from receiving radio, television or telephone signals clearly （电台、电视广播或电话信号所受到的）干扰
3 the combination of two or more wave movements to form a new wave, which may be bigger or smaller than the first （两个波或以上的）干涉，干扰

*interrupt
/ˌɪntəˈrʌpt ||; ˌɪntəˈrʌpt/verb
1 [I,T] interrupt (sb/sth) (with sth) to say or do sth that makes sb stop what he/she is saying or doing 打断（某人的讲话或工作）；打扰 · He kept interrupting me with silly questions. 他不断提一些可笑的问题来打断我的话。
2 [T] to stop the progress of sth for a short time 中止；中断: The programme was interrupted by an important news flash. 节目突然中断，随即插播一段重要的新闻简报。

interruption
/ˌɪntəˈrʌpʃn ||; ˌɪntəˈrʌpʃən/noun [U] [C] the act of interrupting sb/sth; the person or thing that interrupts sb/sth 打断；打扰；打断或打扰的人或事物: I need to work for a few hours without interruption. 我要不受打扰工作几个小时。 I've had so many interruptions this morning that I've done nothing! 这个早上多次受到打扰，弄得我什么事也没做成！
