intertwine
/ˌɪntəˈtwaɪn ||; ˌɪntɚˈtwaɪn/verb [I,T] if two things intertwine or if you intertwine them, they become very closely connected and difficult to separate （使）缠结；（使）缠绕在一起 · His interests in business and politics were closely intertwined. 他对商业和政治的兴趣紧密交织在一起。

*interval
/ˈɪntəvl ||; ˈɪntɚvḷ/noun[C]
1 a period of time between two events （两件事中的）间隔时间: There was a long interval between sending the letter and getting a reply. 信件寄出后很久才收到回信。
2 a short break separating the different parts of a play, film, concert, etc （戏剧、电影、音乐会等的）幕间休息，中场休息
3 [usu.pl] a short period during which sth different happens from what is happening for the rest of the time （在某过程中有不同事件穿插的）间歇: There'll be a few sunny intervals between the showers today. 今天将有阵雨，间中放晴。
Some words that have a similar meaning to interval are intermission, break, recess, interlude and pause. In British English we use interval for a break in a performance. The American English word is intermission. A break is especially used in connection with periods of work or study, for example a lunch/tea break in an office, factory or school The children play outside in the breaks at school. You've worked so hard you've earned a break. In American English a break at school is called (a) recess. In British English recess is a longer period of time when work or business stops, especially in Parliament or the law courts Parliament is in recess. the summer recess. An interlude is a short period of time that passes between two events, during which something different happens a peaceful interlude in the fightingand a pause is a short temporary stop in action or speech After a moment's pause, she answered. intermission、break、recess、interlude及pause的意思跟interval也差不多。演出中的休息时间，英国英语叫interval，美国英语叫intermission。工作或学习上的小歇叫break，如办公室、工厂或学校的午餐或喝茶／咖啡时间(lunch或tea break)：The children play outside in the breaks at school.课间休息时，学生都在教室外面玩耍。·You've worked so hard you've earned a break.你这样卖力，理该歇一歇。课间小歇，美国英语叫(a) recess。英国英语里，recess指较长的假期，尤指国会或法院的休会或休审期：Parliament is in recess.国会现在休会中。·the summer recess暑假。两个事件中发生不同事件的短时间叫interlude：a peaceful interlude in the fighting 战斗中的短暂和平，而行动或言语上的暂停叫pause：After a moment's pause, she answered.她停顿片刻，然后回答问题。 at intervals with time or spaces between 每隔…（时间或空间）；间歇: I write home at regular intervals. 我定时给家里写信。 Plant the trees at two-metre intervals. 每隔两米种一棵树。

intervene
/ˌɪntəˈvi:n ||; ˌɪntɚˈvin/verb[I]
1 intervene (in sth) to act in a way that prevents sth happening or influences the result of sth 介入；调停；斡旋: She would have died if the neighbours hadn't intervened. 要不是邻居出面调停，她早就没命了。 to intervene in a dispute 调停纠纷
2 to interrupt sb who is speaking in order to say sth 插嘴；打岔
3 (used about events, etc) to happen in a way that delays sth or stops it from happening （指事件等）阻碍，阻止（某事发生）: If no further problems intervene we should be able to finish in time. 如果不再出问题，我们当能按时完成。 ➔intervention /ˌɪntəˈvenʃn ||; ˌɪntɚˈvɛnʃən/ noun [U,C]: intervention (in sth) military intervention in the crisis 对这场危机的军事干预

intervening
/ˌɪntəˈvi:nɪŋ ||; ˌɪntɚˈvinɪŋ/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) coming or existing between two events, dates, objects, etc 发生于其间的；介于其间的: the intervening years/days/months 中间的那几年╱天╱月

*interview¹
/ˈɪntəvju: ||; ˈɪntɚˌvju/noun[C]
1 an interview (for sth) a meeting at which sb is asked questions to find out if he/she is suitable for a job, course of study, etc （招聘、入学等的）面试，面谈: to attend an interview 参加面试
2 an interview (with sb) a meeting at which a journalist asks sb questions in order to find out his/her opinion, etc （记者的）访问，访谈: There was an interview with the Prime Minister on television last night. 昨晚电视有首相接受采访的节目。 The actress refused to give an interview (= answer questions). 那位女演员拒绝接受访问。
*interview²
/ˈɪntəvju: ||; ˈɪntɚˌvju/verb[T]
1 interview sb (for sth) to ask sb questions to find out if he/she is suitable for a job, course of study, etc 对某人进行面试或面谈: How many applicants did you interview for the job? 为了这份工作你对多少个求职者进行过面试？
2 interview sb (about sth) to ask sb questions about his/her opinions, private life, etc especially on the radio or television or for a newspaper, magazine, etc 采访，访问（尤指在电台、电视上，或者为报纸、杂志等）
3 interview sb (about sth) to ask sb questions at a private meeting 单独询问: The police are waiting to interview the girl. 警方等待单独询问那名女孩。

interviewee
/ˌɪntəvju:ˈi: ||; ˌɪntɚvjuˈi/noun [C] a person who is questioned in an interview 参加面试者；受访者

interviewer
/ˈɪntəvju:ə(r) ||; ˈɪntɚˌvjuɚ/noun [C] a person who asks the questions in an interview 进行面试者；采访者

intestine
/ɪnˈtestɪn ||; ɪnˈtɛstɪn/noun [C] [usu.pl] the long tube in your body that carries food away from your stomach to the place where it leaves your body 肠: the small/large intestine 小肠；大肠 [SYN] Gut is a less formal word. gut较适用于非正式场合。 ☞picture at body 见body插图 ➔intestinal /ɪnˈtestɪnl ;ˌɪnteˈstaɪnl||; ɪnˈtɛstɪnḷ/ adj

intimacy
/ˈɪntɪməsi ||; ˈɪntəməsɪ/noun [U] the state of having a close personal relationship with sb 亲密: Their intimacy grew over the years. 这些年来他们的关系越来越亲密。

intimate
/ˈɪntɪmət ||; ˈɪntəmət/adj
1 (used about people) having a very close relationship （指人）亲密的，要好的: They're intimate friends. 他们是要好的朋友。
2 very private and personal 私密的；个人的: They told each other their most intimate thoughts and secrets. 他们互诉心曲。
3 (used about a place, an atmosphere, etc) quiet and friendly （指地方、气氛等）恬静的，怡人的: I know an intimate little restaurant we could go to. 我知道有一家幽静的小餐馆我们可以去。
4 very detailed 详尽的: He's lived here all his life and has an intimate knowledge of the area. 他一辈子都住在这里，对这个地区了如指掌。 ➔intimately adv

intimation
/ˌɪntɪˈmeɪʃn ||; ˌɪntəˈmeʃən/noun [C,U] (formal 正式) the act of stating sth or of making it known, especially in an indirect way 暗示；提示: There was no intimation from his doctor that his condition was serious. 医生没有说他的病情很严重的意思。

intimidate
/ɪnˈtɪmɪdeɪt ||; ɪnˈtɪməˌdet/verb [T] intimidate sb (into sth/doing sth) to frighten or threaten sb, often in order to make him/her do sth 恫吓，恐吓，胁迫（为使做某事）: She refused to be intimidated by their threats. 她不屈服于他们的恐吓。 ➔intimidating adj The teacher had rather an intimidating manner. 那位老师的态度相当吓人。 ➔intimidation /ɪnˌtɪmɪˈdeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌtɪməˈdeʃən/ noun [U]: The rebel troops controlled the area by intimidation. 叛军用威吓手段控制了那个地区。

*into
/ˈɪntə;before vowels ˈɪntə;ˈɪntu: ||; ˈɪntə; ˈɪntə; ˈɪntu/prep
1 moving to a position inside or in sth 进；入: Come into the house. 到屋里来。 I'm going into town. 我要进城去。 [OPP] out of (1) 反义词为out of(1)
2 in the direction of sth 朝着；对着: Please speak into the microphone. 请对着话筒说话。 At this point we were driving into the sun and had to shade our eyes. 我们这时候正驶到阳光底下，不得不遮住眼睛。
3 to a point at which you hit sth 跟…碰上；撞: I backed the car into a wall. 我倒车的时候撞在墙上。 She walked into a glass door. 她走路撞在玻璃门上。
4 showing a change from one thing to another 表示某一事物变成另一事物: We're turning the spare room into a study. 我们在把备用房间改成书房。 She changed into her jeans. 她换上了牛仔裤。 Translate the passage into German. 把这段文字译成德语。
5 concerning or involving sth 关于；牵涉到: an inquiry into safety procedures 关于安全措施的调查
6 used when you are talking about dividing numbers （用于除法运算）: 7 into 28 goes 4 times 7除28等于4。
be into sth(spoken 口语) to be very interested in sth, for example as a hobby 对…很感兴趣: I'm really into canoeing. 我很喜欢划独木舟。

intolerable
/ɪnˈtɒlərəbl ||; ɪnˈtɑlərəbḷ/adj too bad, unpleasant or difficult to bear or accept 令人难以忍受的；难以容忍的: The living conditions were intolerable. 那里的生活条件真让人受不了。 intolerable pain 令人难以忍受的痛楚 [SYN] unbearable 同义词为unbearable [OPP] tolerable 反义词为tolerable ☞verb tolerate 动词为tolerate ➔intolerably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

intolerant
/ɪnˈtɒlərənt ||; ɪnˈtɑlərənt/adj intolerant (of sb/sth) not able to accept behaviour or opinions that are different from your own; finding sb/sth too unpleasant to bear 褊狭的；不容忍的；无雅量的: She's very intolerant of young children. 她不能忍受小孩子。 [OPP] tolerant 反义词为tolerant ➔intolerance noun [U] [OPP] tolerance 反义词为tolerance ➔intolerantly adv

intonation
/ˌɪntəˈneɪʃn ||; ˌɪntoˈneʃən/noun [C,U] the rise and fall of your voice while you are speaking 语调；说话的抑扬顿挫 [SYN] inflection 同义词为inflection

intoxicated
/ɪnˈtɒksɪkeɪtɪd ||; ɪnˈtɑksəˌketɪd/adj (formal 正式)
1 having had too much alcohol to drink; drunk 喝醉的；醉醺醺的
2 very excited and happy 非常兴奋和快乐的；陶醉的: She was intoxicated by her success. 她陶醉在自己的成就里。 ➔intoxication /ɪnˌtɒksɪˈkeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌtɑksəˈkeʃən/ noun [U]

intra-
prefix (in adjectives and adverbs) inside; within （用于构成形容词及副词）内部，在内: intravenous 静脉内的 intra-departmental 部门内部的 ☞Compare inter-. 与inter-比较。

Intranet
/ˈɪntrənet ||; ˈɪntrənɛt/noun [C] (computing计算机技术) a system of computers inside an organization that makes it possible for people who work there to look at the same information and to send information to each other 内连网，内部网络（机构内部的计算机系统，该机构工作人员可参看同样的信息，并可互相发送信息） ☞Compare the Internet. 与the Internet比较。

intransitive
/ɪnˈtrænsətɪv ||; ɪnˈtrænsətɪv/adj (grammar语法) (used about a verb) used without an object （指动词）不及物的 [OPP] transitive 反义词为transitive Intransitive verbs are marked [I] in this dictionary. For more information about intransitive verbs, look at the Quick Grammar Reference section. 本词典里，不及物动词以[I]标示。有关不及物动词的详细用法，参看“语法便览”部份。 ➔intransitively adv

intrauterine
/ˌɪntrəˈju:təraɪn ||; ˌɪntrəˈjutəraɪn/adj (medical医学) inside the UTERUS (= the part of a woman's body where a baby grows) 子宫内的 ☞Look at IUD. 参看IUD。

intravenous
/ˌɪntrəˈvi:nəs ||; ˌɪntrəˈvinəs/adj (abbr IV) (used about drugs or food 指药物或食物) going into a VEIN(= a tube in your body that carries blood) 进入静脉内的: an intravenous injection 静脉注射 ➔intravenously adv The patient had to be fed intravenously. 病人必须靠静脉注射来维持生命。

intrepid
/ɪnˈtrepɪd ||; ɪnˈtrɛpɪd/adj without any fear of danger 勇敢无畏的: an intrepid climber 勇敢的登山运动员

intricacy
/ˈɪntrɪkəsi ||; ˈɪntrəkəsɪ/noun
1 intricacies [pl] the intricacies of sth the complicated parts or details of sth 错综复杂的部份或细节: It's difficult to understand all the intricacies of the situation. 局势错综复杂，实在搞不清楚。
2 [U] the quality of having complicated parts, details or patterns 错综复杂

intricate
/ˈɪntrɪkət ||; ˈɪntrəkɪt/adj having many small parts or details put together in a complicated way 错综复杂的: an intricate pattern 复杂的图案 The story has an intricate plot. 这故事的情节非常复杂。 ➔intricately adv

intrigue¹
/ɪnˈtri:g ||; ɪnˈtrig/verb [T] to make sb very interested and wanting to know more 使感兴趣或想了解更多: I was intrigued by the way he seemed to know all about us already. 他似乎已经对我们了如指掌，这使我感到很好奇。 ➔intriguing adj an intriguing story 引人入胜的故事
intrigue²
/ˈɪntri:g ||; ˈɪntrig/noun [C,U] secret plans to do sth, especially sth bad 秘密计划（尤指做坏事的）；阴谋 ；诡计: The film is about political intrigues against the government. 本片讲的是关于反对政府的政治阴谋。· His new novel is full of intrigue and suspense. 他新近写的那本小说充满阴谋悬疑。

intrinsic
/ɪnˈtrɪnsɪk;-zɪk||; ɪnˈtrɪnsɪk/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) belonging to sth as part of its nature; basic 内在的；本质的: The object is of no intrinsic value (= the material it is made of is not worth anything). 这件东西本身没有什么价值。 ➔intrinsically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

*introduce
/ˌɪntrəˈdju:s; US -du:s ||; ˌɪntrəˈdus/verb[T]
1 introduce sth (in/into sth) to bring in sth new, use sth, or take sth to a place for the first time 引进或引入新事物: The new law was introduced in 1991. 这项新法律是1991年制定的。 The company is introducing a new range of cars this summer. 这家公司今年夏天要推出一系列新型汽车。 Goats were first introduced to the island in the 17th century. 山羊是在17世纪引入该岛的。
2 introduce sb (to sb) to tell two or more people who have not met before what each others' names are 介绍: ‘Who's that girl over there?’ ‘Come with me and I'll introduce you to her.’ “那边那个女孩是谁？”“跟我来，我给你们介绍一下。”
3 introduce yourself (to sb) to tell sb you have met for the first time what your name is 自我介绍: He just walked over and introduced himself to me. 他径直走过来向我自我介绍一番。
4 introduce sb to sth to make sb begin to learn about sth or do sth for the first time 给某人介绍（某事物）: This pamphlet will introduce you to the basic aims of our society. 这本小册子介绍了我们协会的基本目标。
5 to be the first or main speaker on a radio or television programme telling the audience who is going to speak, perform, etc 主持（电台或电视节目）: May I introduce my first guest on the show tonight... 请让我介绍一下今晚节目的第一位嘉宾…
In Britain there are a number of different ways of introducing one person to another, depending on the occasion. In a formal introduction, we use a person's title followed by the surname. In an informal situation, or when introducing children, we use first names. In both formal and informal introductions we say ‘this is’, when referring to the people we are introducing, not ‘he/she is’ (informal 非正式) ‘John, meet Mary.’(informal 非正式) ‘Mrs Smith, this is my daughter, Jane.’(formal 正式) ‘May I introduce you. Dr Waters, this is Mr Jones. Mr Jones, Dr Waters.’ An informal response to an introduction is ‘Hello’ or ‘Nice to meet you.’ A formal response is ‘How do you do?’ The other person also replies: ‘How do you do?’ When people are introduced they often shake hands. 在英国，不同的场合有不同的介绍方式。在正式场合，用头衔加姓氏；在非正式场合或介绍小孩时，直接用名字。无论在正式场合还是非正式场合，作介绍时都用this is，而不用he／she is（非正式）：‘John, meet Mary.’“约翰，这是玛丽。”·（非正式）：‘Mrs Smith, this is my daughter, Jane.’“史密斯太太，这是小女简。”·（正式）：‘May I introduce you. Dr Waters, this is Mr Jones. Mr Jones, Dr Waters.’“我来介绍一下。沃特斯博士，这位是琼斯先生。琼斯先生，这位是沃特斯博士。”被介绍时，非正式的响应可以是Hello，或Nice to meet you。正式的响应是How do you do?对方也说How do you do?双方一般互相握手。
*introduction
/ˌɪntrəˈdʌkʃn ||; ˌɪntrəˈdʌkʃən/noun
1 [U] introduction of sth (into sth) the action of bringing in sth new; using sth or taking sth to a place for the first time 引进；首度使用: the introduction of computers into the classroom 开始在教室里使用计算机
2 [C] [usu.pl] the act of telling two or more people each others' names for the first time 介绍（使双方相识）: I think I'll get my husband to make/do the introductions -- he's better at remembering names! 还是让我先生来介绍，他记名字的本事比我大！
3 [C] the first part of a book, a piece of written work or a talk which gives a general idea of what is going to follow （书的）引言，导论；（讲话的）开场白
4 [C] an introduction (to sth) a book for people who are beginning to study a subject 入门书: ‘An Introduction to English Grammar’ 《英语语法入门》
5 [sing] an introduction to sth first experience of sth 初次经历: My first job -- in a factory -- was not a pleasant introduction to work. 我的第一份工作是在一家工厂里，这初次的经历可不怎么令人愉快。

introductory
/ˌɪntrəˈdʌktəri ||; ˌɪntrəˈdʌktərɪ/adj
1 happening or said at the beginning in order to give a general idea of what will follow 介绍性质的: an introductory speech/chapter/remark 引言；绪篇；开场白
2 intended as an introduction to a subject or activity 初次经历的，初阶的（某个科目或活动）: introductory courses 基础课程

introvert
/ˈɪntrəvɜ:t ||; ˈɪntrəˌvɝt/noun [C] a quiet, shy person who prefers to be alone than with other people 性格内向的人 [OPP] extrovert 反义词为extrovert ➔introverted adj

intrude
/ɪnˈtru:d ||; ɪnˈtrud/verb [I] intrude on/upon sb/sth to enter a place or situation without permission or when you are not wanted 闯入；不请自进；打扰: I'm sorry to intrude on your Sunday lunch but... 打扰你们的礼拜天午饭，真对不起，可是…

intruder
/ɪnˈtru:də(r) ||; ɪnˈtrudɚ/noun [C] a person who enters a place without permission and often secretly 闯入者；侵入者

intrusion
/ɪnˈtru:ʒn ||; ɪnˈtruʒən/noun
1 [C,U] (an) intrusion (on/upon/into sth) something that disturbs you or your life when you want to be private 侵入；闯入；打扰: This was another example of press intrusion into the affairs of the royals. 这是新闻界侵扰王室人员事务的又一例子。
2 [C] (in geology 地质学) a mass of hot liquid rock that has been forced up from below the earth's surface and cooled in between other layers of rock 侵入岩浆 ➔intrusive /ɪnˈtru:sɪv ||; ɪnˈtrusɪv/ adj

intuition
/ˌɪntjuˈɪʃn; US -tu- ||; ˌɪntυˈɪʃən/noun [C,U] the feeling or understanding that makes you believe or know that sth is true without being able to explain why 直觉: She knew, by intuition, about his illness, although he never mentioned it. 虽然他没有说，可是她凭直觉知道他患了病。 ➔intuitive /ɪnˈtju:ɪtɪv; US -tu:- ||; ɪnˈtuɪtɪv/ adj ➔intuitively adv Intuitively, she knew that he was lying. 她凭直觉知道他在撒谎。

Inuit
/ˈɪnuɪt ||; ˈɪnjuɪt/noun [C] (plural Inuit or Inuits) (a member of) the race of people from northern Canada and parts of Alaska, Greenland, and eastern Siberia 伊努伊特人（生活在加拿大北部、阿拉斯加部份地区、格陵兰及西伯利亚东部的一个民族） Inuit adj

inundate
/ˈɪnʌndeɪt ||; ˈɪnʌnˌdet/verb [T] (usually passive 通常用于被动语态)
1 inundate sb (with sth) to give or send sb so many things that he/she cannot deal with them all 给予，交予（某人太多事物，致使人家难以应付）: We were inundated with applications for the job. 这个职位的申请信件如雪片飞来，我们实在应付不过来。 [SYN] swamp 同义词为swamp
2 (formal 正式) to cover an area of land with water 淹没；泛滥: After the heavy rains the fields were inundated. 大雨之后农田都给水淹了。 [SYN]A less formal word is flood. 不大正式的场合用flood。

invade
/ɪnˈveɪd ||; ɪnˈved/verb
1 [I,T] to enter a country with an army in order to attack and take control of it 侵略；入侵；侵犯 · When did the Romans invade Britain? 罗马人是何时入侵英国的？
2 [T] to enter in large numbers, often where sb/sth is not wanted 大批进入，涌入（常指不受欢迎的）: The whole area has been invaded by tourists. 这地区到处都是成群结队的游客。 ☞noun invasion 名词为invasion ➔invader noun [C]

invalid¹
/ɪnˈvælɪd ||; ɪnˈvælɪd/adj
1 not legally or officially acceptable 没有法律效力的: I'm afraid your passport is invalid. 恐怕你的护照已经失效了。
2 not correct according to reason; not based on all the facts 站不住脚的；缺乏事实根据的: an invalid argument 站不住脚的论据
3 (computing计算机技术) (used about an instruction, etc) of a type that the computer cannot recognize （指指令等）计算机无法识别的，无效的: an invalid command 无效指令 [OPP] valid 反义词为valid
invalid²
/ˈɪnvəlɪd ||; ˈɪnvəlɪd/noun [C] a person who has been very ill for a long time and needs to be looked after （久病不愈、要人照顾的）病人

invalidate
/ɪnˈvælɪdeɪt ||; ɪnˈvæləˌdet/verb[T]
1 to show that an idea, a story, an argument, etc is wrong 表明（想法、说法、论点等）是错的: This new piece of evidence invalidates his version of events. 这件新证据表明他的说法是错的。
2 if you invalidate a document, contract, election, etc, you make it no longer legally or officially valid or acceptable 使（文件、合约、选举等）无效、作废 [OPP] validate 反义词为validate ➔invalidation /ɪnˌvælɪˈdeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌvæləˈdeʃən/ noun [U]

invaluable
/ɪnˈvæljuəbl ||; ɪnˈvæljυəbḷ/adj invaluable (to/for sb/sth) extremely useful 极其有用的；无价的: invaluable help/information/support 极其宝贵的帮助╱信息╱支持 Be careful. Invaluable is not the opposite of valuable. The opposite of valuable is valueless or worthless. 注意:invaluable不是valuable的反义词，valuable的反义词为valueless或worthless。

invariable
/ɪnˈveəriəbl ||; ɪnˈvɛrɪəbḷ/adj not changing 不变的；始终如一的

invariably
/ɪnˈveəriəbli ||; ɪnˈvɛrɪəblɪ/adv almost always 总是: She invariably arrives late. 她老是迟到。

*invasion
/ɪnˈveɪʒn ||; ɪnˈveʒən/noun
1 [C,U] the action of entering another country with an army in order to take control of it 侵略；入侵: the threat of invasion 被侵略的威胁
2 [C] the action of entering a place where you are not wanted and disturbing sb 侵扰；侵犯: Such questions are an invasion of privacy. 这样的问题侵犯了隐私。 ☞verb invade 动词为invade

*invent
/ɪnˈvent ||; ɪnˈvɛnt/verb[T]
1 to think of or make sth for the first time 发明；创造: When was the camera invented? 照相机是什么时候发明的？
2 to say or describe sth that is not true 造；虚构: I realized that he had invented the whole story. 我发觉整件事都是他编造出来的。 ➔inventor noun [C]

*invention
/ɪnˈvenʃn ||; ɪnˈvɛnʃən/noun
1 [C] a thing that has been made or designed by sb for the first time 发明物: The microwave oven is a very useful invention. 微波炉是一项十分有用的发明。
2 [U] the action or process of making or designing sth for the first time 发明；创造: Books had to be written by hand before the invention of printing. 印刷术发明之前，书本都是手抄的。
3 [C,U] telling a story or giving an excuse that is not true 造；虚构: It was obvious that his story about being robbed was (an) invention. 遭抢劫的事显然是他一手杜撰的。

inventive
/ɪnˈventɪv ||; ɪnˈvɛntɪv/adj having clever and original ideas 善于发明的；有创造才能的 ➔inventiveness noun [U]

inventory
/ˈɪnvəntri; US -tɔ:rɪ ||; ˈɪnvənˌtɔrɪ/noun [C] (plural inventories) a detailed list, for example of all the furniture in a house 清单: The landlord is coming to make an inventory of the contents of the flat. 房东要过来将套房里的东西列一张清单。

inverse¹
/ˌɪnˈvɜ:s ||; ɪnˈvɝs/adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) opposite in amount or position to sth else （数量或位置上与他物）相反的，倒置的: A person's wealth is often in inverse proportion to their happiness (= the more money a person has, the less happy he/she is). 一个人的财富往往跟其快乐程度成反比。 ➔inversely adv
inverse²
/ˈɪnvɜ:s ||; ɪnˈvɝs/ the inverse noun [sing] (technical术语) the exact opposite of sth 相反；颠倒

invert
/ɪnˈvɜ:t ||; ɪnˈvɝt/verb [T] (formal 正式) to put sth in the opposite order or position to the way it usually is 使倒置: What you see in a mirror is an inverted image of yourself. 你在镜子里看到的是自己左右倒置的影像。

invertebrate
/ɪnˈvɜ:tɪbrət ||; ɪnˈvɝtəbrɪt/noun [C] an animal without a solid line of bones(backbone)going along its body 无脊椎动物: slugs, worms and other small invertebrates 蛞蝓、蚯蚓等小无脊椎动物 [OPP] vertebrate 反义词为vertebrate

inˌverted ˈcommas
(Brit 英) =QUOTATION MARKS to put sth in inverted commas 加上引号

*invest
/ɪnˈvest ||; ɪnˈvɛst/verb [I,T] invest (sth) (in sth)
1 to put money into a bank, business, property, etc in the hope that you will make a profit 投资: Many firms have invested heavily in this project. 许多公司在这项工程投入了大量资金。 I've invested all my money in the company. 我把所有积蓄都投资于这家公司。
2 to spend money, time or energy on sth that you think is good or useful 投入，耗费，付出（金钱、时间、精力于某事）: I'm thinking of investing in a computer. 我在考虑买一台计算机。 You have to invest a lot of time if you really want to learn a language well. 如若真想掌握一种语言，你得花上很多工夫。 ➔investor noun [C]

*investigate
/ɪnˈvestɪgeɪt ||; ɪnˈvɛstəˌget/verb [I,T] to try to find out all the facts about sth 调查；研究: A murder was reported and the police were sent to investigate. 凶杀案发生后，警察被派去调查。 A group of experts are investigating the cause of the crash. 专家小组正在调查坠机原因。 ➔investigator noun [C]

*investigation
/ɪnˌvestɪˈgeɪʃn ||; ɪnˌvɛstəˈgeʃən/noun [C,U] (an) investigation (into sth) an official examination of the facts about a situation, crime, etc （官方）调查，审查，研究: The airlines are going to carry out an investigation into security procedures at airports. 航空公司将研究机场的保安程序。 The matter is still under investigation. 事情仍在调查阶段。

investigative
/ɪnˈvestɪgətɪv; US -geɪtɪv ||; ɪnˈvɛstəˌgetɪv/adj trying to find out all the facts about sb/sth 调查性质的: investigative journalism 调查新闻学

investment
/ɪnˈvestmənt ||; ɪnˈvɛstmənt/noun
1 [U] [C] (an) investment (in sth) the act of putting money in a bank, business, property, etc; the amount of money that you put in 投资；投资额: investment in local industry 投资于当地工业 The company will have to make an enormous investmentto computerize production. 若要使生产计算机化，这家公司非得投入大量资金。
2 [C] (informal 非正式) a thing that you have bought 买回来的东西: This coat has been a good investment -- I've worn it for three years. 这件外衣买得合算，我已穿了三年。

invigilate
/ɪnˈvɪdʒɪleɪt ||; ɪnˈvɪdʒəˌlet/verb [I,T] (Brit 英) to watch the people taking an exam to make sure that nobody is cheating 监考 ➔invigilator noun [C]

invigorate
/ɪnˈvɪgəreɪt ||; ɪnˈvɪgəˌret/verb [I,T] to make sb feel healthy, fresh and full of energy 使生气勃勃；使精力充沛: I felt invigorated after my run. 跑完步以后我觉得精力充沛。 ➔invigorating adj

invincible
/ɪnˈvɪnsəbl ||; ɪnˈvɪnsəbḷ/adj too strong or powerful to be defeated 不可战胜的；无敌的

invisible
/ɪnˈvɪzəbl ||; ɪnˈvɪzəbḷ/adj invisible (to sb/sth) that cannot be seen 看不见的: bacteria that are invisible to the naked eye 肉眼看不见的细菌 [OPP] visible 反义词为visible ➔invisibility /ɪnˌvɪzəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪnvɪzəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U] ➔invisibly /-bli/ adv

invitation
/ˌɪnvɪˈteɪʃn ||; ˌɪnvəˈteʃən/noun
1 [U] the act of inviting sb or being invited 邀请: Entry is by invitation only. 凭请柬入场。 a letter of invitation 邀请信
2 [C] an invitation to sb/sth (to sth/to do sth) a written or spoken request to go somewhere or do sth 邀请书；口头邀请: Did you get an invitation to the conference? 你接到会议邀请函了吗？ a wedding invitation 婚礼请帖
You may accept an invitation, or you may turn it down or decline it. 接受邀请可以说accept an invitation，拒绝就用turn it down或decline it。
*invite
/ɪnˈvaɪt ||; ɪnˈvaɪt/verb[T]
1 invite sb (to/for sth) to ask sb to come somewhere or to do sth 邀请: We invited all the family to the wedding. 我们邀请了所有家族成员出席婚礼。 Successful applicants will be invited for interview next week. 申请成功的人将被邀请参加下星期的面试。
2 to make sth unpleasant likely to happen 引起，招致（不好的事）: You're inviting trouble if you carry so much money around. 你身上带着那么多钱到处跑会招来麻烦的。
invite sb back
1 to ask sb to return with you to your home 邀请某人和自己一起回到家里: Shall we invite the others back for coffee after the meeting? 会议后我们邀请其他人到家里喝杯咖啡，好不好？
2 to ask sb to come to your home a second time, or after you have been a guest at his/her home 再请某人到家里；回请某人到家里
invite sb in to ask sb to come into your home 请某人到家里来 invite sb out to ask sb to go out somewhere with you 请某人一起外出去某地: We've been invited out to lunch by the neighbours. 邻居邀请我们上馆子吃午饭。 invite sb over/round(informal 非正式) to ask sb to come to your home 邀请某人到家里作客: I've invited Mohamed and his family round for lunch on Sunday. 我邀请了穆罕默德一家人礼拜天到家里吃午饭。 ☞ Ask can be used instead of invite in all senses. 注意：invite在各义项中皆可用ask代替。

inviting
/ɪnˈvaɪtɪŋ ||; ɪnˈvaɪtɪŋ/adj attractive and pleasant 吸引人的；令人神往的: The smell of cooking was very inviting. 烧菜的香味可真诱人。

in vitro
/ˌɪn ˈvi:trəʊ ||; ˌɪn ˈvitro/adj adv (technical术语) (used about a process or a reaction) taking place in a glass tube or dish, not inside a living body （指过程或反应）在试管中（的），在生物体外（的）: in vitro experiments 试管中的试验 the development of in vitro fertilization 体外受精的发展 an egg fertilized in vitro 体外受精卵

invoice
/ˈɪnvɔɪs ||; ˈɪnvɔɪs/noun [C] an official paper that lists goods or services that you have received and says how much you have to pay for them 发票

involuntary
/ɪnˈvɒləntri; US -terɪ ||; ɪnˈvɑlənˌtɛrɪ/adj done without wanting or meaning to 非自愿的；不由自主的: She gave an involuntary gasp of pain as the doctor inserted the needle. 医生给她打针的时候，她痛得禁不住倒抽了一口气。 [OPP] voluntary or deliberate 反义词为voluntary或deliberate ➔involuntarily /ɪnˈvɒləntrəli ||; ɪnˈvɑlənˌtɛrəlɪ/ adv

*involve
/ɪnˈvɒlv ||; ɪnˈvɑlv/verb[T]
1 (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to make sth necessary 需要: The job involves a lot of travelling. 这份工作需要经常出差。
2 (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) if a situation, an event or an activity involves sb/sth, he/she/it takes part in it 参与: The story involves a woman who went on holiday with her child. 这故事讲一个女人带着孩子去度假。 More than 100 people were involved in the project. 100多人参与这项工程。
Although this verb is not used in the continuous tenses, it is common to see the present participle (= -ing form) There was a serious accident involving a stolen car. 虽然这个动词不用于进行时，但它的现在分词还是常见﹕There was a serious accident involving a stolen car.发生了一起严重的事故，牵涉到一辆偷来的汽车。
3 involve sb/sth in (doing) sth to cause sb/sth to take part in or be concerned with sth 使…卷入；使…牵涉: Please don't involve me in your family arguments. 你们家里的争执别把我牵扯进去。 ➔involvement noun [C,U] The men deny any involvement in the robbery. 那几个男人否认参与这宗劫案。

involved
/ɪnˈvɒlvd ||; ɪnˈvɑlvd/adj
1 difficult to understand; complicated 复杂的: The book has a very involved plot. 这本书的情节非常复杂。
2 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) involved (in sth) closely connected with sth; taking an active part in sth 密切相关；积极参与: I'm very involved in local politics. 我积极投入本地政坛。
3 (not before a noun 不用于名词前) involved (with sb) having a sexual relationship with sb 跟某人有性关系: She is involved with an older man. 她搭上了一个年纪较大的男人。

inward
/ˈɪnwəd ||; ˈɪnwɚd/adv adj
1 (also inwards) towards the inside or centre 向内（的）；向着中心（的）: Stand in a circle facing inwards. 面朝里站成一个圈儿。
2 inside your mind, not shown to other people 内心（的）: my inward feelings 我内心的感觉 [OPP] outward 反义词为outward

inwardly
/ˈɪnwədli ||; ˈɪnwɚdlɪ/adv in your mind; secretly 心里；秘密地: He was inwardly relieved that they could not come. 他暗自庆幸他们来不了。

iodide
/ˈaɪədaɪd ||; ˈaɪəˌdaɪd/noun [C] a chemical compound consisting of iodine and another chemical element 碘化物

iodine
/ˈaɪədi:n; US -daɪn ||; ˈaɪəˌdaɪn/noun [U] (symbol I) a dark-coloured substance that is found in sea water. A purple liquid containing iodine is sometimes used to clean cuts in your skin. 碘

ion
/ˈaɪən ||; ˈaɪɒn/noun [C] (in chemistry 化学) an atom or a MOLECULE (= a group of atoms) that has gained or lost one or more of its parts (electrons) and so has a positive or negative electric charge 离子

ionic
/aɪˈɒnɪk ||; aɪˈɒnɪk/adj
1 of or related to ions 离子的；与离子有关的
2 (used about the way chemicals join together) using the electrical pull between positive and negative ions （用于化学物质连接的方式）利用正负离子之间的引力的: ionic bonds/compounds 离子键；离子化合物

ionize
/ˈaɪənaɪz ||; ˈaɪənˌaɪz/ (also -ise) verb [I,T] (used about atoms and molecules 指原子及分子) to gain a positive or negative electric charge by losing or gaining one part(an electron) 使电离；使离子化

ionosphere
/aɪˈɒnəsfɪə(r) ||; aɪˈɑnəˌsfɪr/noun [sing] the ionosphere the layer of the earth's atmosphere between about 80 and 1000 kilometres above the surface of the earth, that sends radio waves back around the earth 电离层（大气层的组成部份，离地球表面约80至1000公里，反射无线电波） ☞Compare stratosphere and troposphere. 与stratosphere及troposphere比较。

IOU
/ˌaɪ əʊ ˈju: ||; ˈaɪ ˌo ˈju/abbr I owe you; a piece of paper that you sign showing that you owe sb some money 借据；欠单

IPA
/ˌaɪ pi: ˈeɪ ||; ˈaɪ ˌpi ˈe/abbr the International Phonetic Alphabet 国际音标

IQ
/ˌaɪ ˈkju: ||; ˌaɪ ˈkju/abbr intelligence quotient; a measure of how intelligent sb is 智商（计算人智力的标准）: have a high/low IQ 智商高╱低 an IQ of 120 智商120

iridium
/ɪˈrɪdiəm ||; ɪˈrɪdɪəm/noun [U] (symbol Ir) a very hard yellow-white metal, used especially to mix with other metals to form another metal(an alloy) 铱

*iron¹
/ˈaɪən; US ˈaɪərn ||; ˈaɪɚn/noun
1 [U] (symbol Fe) a hard strong metal that is used for making steel and is found in small quantities in food and in blood 铁: an iron bar 铁棒 iron ore 铁矿 The doctor gave me iron tablets. 医生给我开了些含铁质的药片。 (figurative 比喻) The general has an iron(= very strong)will. 这位将军有顽强的意志。 ☞Look at pig iron. 参看pig iron。
2 [C] an electrical instrument with a flat bottom that is heated and used to smooth clothes after you have washed and dried them 熨斗: a steam iron 蒸汽熨斗
*iron²
/ˈaɪən; US ˈaɪərn ||; ˈaɪɚn/verb [I,T] to use an iron to make clothes, etc smooth 熨平（衣服等）: Could you iron this dress for me? 这条连衣裙可以给我熨一下吗？ Do the ironing is often used instead of iron I usually do the ironing on Sunday. 熨衣服一般叫do the ironing，不叫iron：I usually do the ironing on Sunday.我通常在礼拜天熨衣服。 iron sth out to get rid of any problems or difficulties that are affecting sth 消除，解决（问题或困难）

ironic
/aɪˈrɒnɪk ||; aɪˈrɑnɪk/ (also ironical /aɪˈrɒnɪkl ||; aɪˈrɑnɪkḷ/) adj
1 meaning the opposite of what you say 说反话的；讽刺的: Jeff sometimes offends people with his ironic sense of humour. 杰夫喜欢冷嘲热讽，有时候得罪人。 ☞ Look at sarcastic. 参看sarcastic。
2 (used about a situation) strange or amusing because it is unusual or unexpected （指情况）出乎意料的，令人啼笑皆非的: It is ironic that the busiest people are often the most willing to help. 最乐意提供协助的往往是那些最忙碌的人，这真令人意想不到。 ➔ironically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

ironing
/ˈaɪənɪŋ ||; ˈaɪɚnɪŋ/noun [U] clothes, etc that need ironing or that have just been ironed 待熨或熨好的衣服等: a large pile of ironing 一大堆待熨的衣服 ☞Look at the note at iron. 参看iron的注释。

ˈironing board
noun [C] a special table that is used for putting clothes on when we are making them smooth with an iron 熨衣板 ☞picture at iron 见iron插图

irony
/ˈaɪrəni ||; ˈaɪrənɪ/noun (plural ironies)
1 [C,U] an unusual or unexpected part of a situation, etc that seems strange or amusing 出乎意料的情况；令人啼笑皆非的事: The irony was that he was killed in a car accident soon after the end of the war. 战争结束后不久他便死于交通事故，真是造化弄人。
2 [U] a way of speaking that shows you are joking or that you mean the opposite of what you say 反话: ‘The English are such good cooks’, he said with heavy irony. 他故意挖苦说：“英国人真是烹饪能手。”

irradiate
/ɪˈreɪdieɪt ||; ɪˈredɪˌet/verb [T] to treat food with powerful(radioactive)rays in order to be able to keep it for a long time 辐照处理（对食物进行辐照以便长久保存）: Irradiated food lasts longer, but some people think it is not safe. 受过辐照处理的食物保存时间较长，但有人认为吃了对身体有害。

irrational
/ɪˈræʃənl ||; ɪˈræʃənḷ/adj not based on reason or clear thought 荒谬的；不合逻辑的: an irrational fear of spiders 对蜘蛛莫名的恐惧 ➔irrationality /ɪˌræʃəˈnæləti ||; ɪˌræʃəˈnælətɪ/ noun [U] ➔irrationally /-nəli ||; -nəlɪ/ adv

irreconcilable
/ɪˌrekənˈsaɪləbl ||; ɪˈrɛkənˌsaɪləbḷ/adj (formal 正式) (used about people or their ideas and beliefs) so different that they cannot be made to agree （指人、观念或信仰）势不两立的，不可调和的 ➔irreconcilably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

*irregular
/ɪˈregjələ(r) ||; ɪˈrɛgjəlɚ/adj
1 not having a shape or pattern that we recognize or can predict 不规则的；无规律的: an irregular shape 不规则的形状
2 happening at times that you cannot predict 不定期的: His visits became more and more irregular. 他的探视越来越不定期了。
3 not allowed according to the rules or social customs 不合规矩的；不合常规的: It is highly irregular for a doctor to give information about patients without their permission. 医生未经病人同意把他们的资料公开是不合规矩的。
4 (grammar语法) not following the usual rules of grammar 不规则变化的: irregular verbs 不规则动词 ‘Caught’ is an irregular past tense form. caught是不规则变化的过去时形式。 [OPP] for senses 1, 2 and 4regular 第1、2及4义的反义词皆为regular
➔irregularity /ɪˌregjəˈlærəti ||; ˌɪrɛgjəˈlærətɪ/ noun [C,U] (plural irregularities) ➔irregularly adv

irrelevancy
/ɪˈreləvənsi ||; ɪˈrɛləvənsɪ/noun [C] (plural irrelevancies) something that is not important because it is not connected with sth else 不相关的事物；无关紧要的东西

irrelevant
/ɪˈreləvənt ||; ɪˈrɛləvənt/adj not connected with sth or important to it 不相关的；无关紧要的: That's completely irrelevant to the subject under discussion. 那个跟讨论的主题完全拉不上关系。 [OPP] relevant 反义词为relevant ➔irrelevance noun [U] [C] ➔irrelevantly adv

irreparable
/ɪˈrepərəbl ||; ɪˈrɛpərəbḷ/adj that cannot be repaired 不能修复的；不可弥补的: Irreparable damage has been done to the forests of Eastern Europe. 东欧的森林遭受了无可弥补的破坏。 ➔irreparably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irreplaceable
/ˌɪrɪˈpleɪsəbl ||; ˌɪrɪˈplesəbḷ/adj (used about sth very valuable or special) that cannot be replaced （指贵重或特别的对象）不可替代的 [OPP] replaceable 反义词为replaceable

irrepressible
/ˌɪrɪˈpresəbl ||; ˌɪrɪˈprɛsəbḷ/adj full of life and energy 充满活力和精力的；压抑不住的: young people full of irrepressible good humour 处处流露出好心情的年轻人 ➔irrepressibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irresistible
/ˌɪrɪˈzɪstəbl ||; ˌɪrɪˈzɪstəbḷ/adj
1 so strong that it cannot be stopped or prevented 无法抗拒的；不能压制的: an irresistible urge to laugh 忍不住想笑
2 irresistible (to sb) very attractive 诱惑人的；令人无法抗拒的: He seems to think he's irresistible to women. 他似乎认为自己在女人面前很有魅力。 ☞verb resist 动词为resist ➔irresistibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irrespective of
/ˌɪrɪˈspektɪv əv ||; ˌɪrɪˈspɛktɪv əv/prep not affected by 不受…的影响；不论；不管: Anybody can take part in the competition, irrespective of age. 不论老少，谁都可以参加比赛。

irresponsible
/ˌɪrɪˈspɒnsəbl ||; ˌɪrɪˈspɑnsəbḷ/adj not thinking about the effect your actions will have; not sensible 不负责任的；不理智的: It is irresponsible to let small children go out alone. 让小孩子单独出门是不负责任的行为。 [OPP] responsible 反义词为responsible ➔irresponsibility /ˌɪrɪˌspɒnsəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪrɪˌspɑnsəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U] ➔irresponsibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irreverent
/ɪˈrevərənt ||; ɪˈrɛvərənt/adj not feeling or showing respect 不敬的；无礼的: This comedy takes an irreverent look at the world of politics. 这部喜剧毫不客气地探讨政界的情况。 ➔irreverence noun [U] ➔irreverently adv

irreversible
/ˌɪrɪˈvɜ:səbl ||; ˌɪrɪˈvɝsəbḷ/adj that cannot be stopped or changed 无法逆转的；不能改变的: The disease can do irreversible damage to the body. 这种病会给身体造成不可挽回的伤害。 ➔irreversibly /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irritable
/ˈɪrɪtəbl ||; ˈɪrətəbḷ/adj becoming angry easily 易怒的；暴躁的: to be/feel/get irritable 觉得╱变得烦躁 ➔irritability /ˌɪrɪtəˈbɪləti ||; ˌɪrətəˈbɪlətɪ/ noun [U] ➔irritably /-əbli ||; -əblɪ/ adv

irritant
/ˈɪrɪtənt ||; ˈɪrətənt/noun [C] a substance that makes part of your body painful or sore 刺激物 irritant adj

irritate
/ˈɪrɪteɪt ||; ˈɪrəˌtet/verb[T]
1 to make sb angry; to annoy 激怒；使烦躁: It really irritates me the way he keeps repeating himself. 他说来说去都是那些话，我真是听烦了。
2 to cause a part of the body to be painful or sore 使（身体某部份）疼痛；刺激: I don't use soap because it irritates my skin. 我不用肥皂，因为肥皂刺激我的皮肤。 ➔irritation /ˌɪrɪˈteɪʃn ||; ˌɪrəˈteʃən/ noun [C,U]

isolate
/ˈaɪsəleɪt ||; ˈaɪsḷˌet/verb [T] isolate sb/sth (from sb/sth) to put or keep sb/sth separate from other people or things 使隔离；使孤立；使脱离: Some farms were isolated by the heavy snowfalls. 有些农场被大雪所困，与外界隔绝。 We need to isolate all the animals with the disease so that the others don't catch it. 我们要把染病的动物隔离，以免其他动物受到传染。

isolated
/ˈaɪsəleɪtɪd ||; ˈaɪsḷˌetɪd/adj
1 isolated (from sb/sth) alone or apart from other people or things 隔离的；单独的: an isolated village deep in the countryside 乡间深处一个与世隔绝的村庄 I was kept isolated from the other patients. 我被安排跟其他病人隔离。
2 not connected with others; happening once 孤立的；只发生一次的: Is this an isolated case or part of a general pattern? 这是个别事例还是普遍现象？

isolation
/ˌaɪsəˈleɪʃn ||; ˌaɪsḷˈeʃən/noun [U]: isolation (from sb/sth) the state of being separate and alone; the act of separating sb/sth 孤立；隔离: He lived in complete isolationfrom the outside world. 他过着与世隔绝的生活。 In isolation each problem does not seem bad, but together they are quite daunting. 单独来看，每个问题似乎并不严重，但加在一起就相当吓人了。 ☞Compare loneliness and solitude. 与loneliness及solitude比较。

/aɪˈsɒsəli:z ||; aɪˈsɑsḷˌiz/adj (mathematics数学) (used about a triangle 指三角形) having two of its three sides the same length 等腰的 ☞picture at triangle 见triangle插图

/ˈaɪsəθɜ:m ||; ˈaɪsəˌθɝm/noun [C] (technical术语) a line on a weather map that joins places that have the same temperature at a particular time 等温线；恒温线

isotope
/ˈaɪsətəʊp ||; ˈaɪsəˌtop/noun [C] (in chemistry 化学) one of two or more forms of a chemical element that have different physical characteristics but the same chemical characteristics 同位素（两个或以上化学特性相同，但物理特性不同的化学元素） Isotopes of the same element have the same number of protons in the nucleus, but a different number of neutrons. 同一元素的同位素(isotope)原子核中含等量的质子(proton)，但不等量的中子(neutron)。

ISP
/ˌaɪ es ˈpi: ||; ˌaɪ ɛs ˈpi/abbr Internet service provider; a company that provides you with an Internet connection and services such as email, etc 因特网服务提供商

*issue¹
/ˈɪʃu:;ˈɪsju: ||; ˈɪʃυ; ˈɪʃjυ/noun
1 [C] a problem or subject for discussion 问题；论题；议题: I want to raise the issue of overtime pay at the meeting. 我想在会上提出加班费的问题。 The government cannot avoid the issue of homelessness any longer. 政府不能再回避有些人无家可归的问题。
2 [C] one in a series of things that are published or produced （期刊等的）一期: Do you have last week's issue of this magazine? 你有没有这杂志上个礼拜的那一期？
3 [U] the act of publishing or giving sth to people 发行；给予: the issue of blankets to the refugees 向难民发放毛毯
make an issue (out) of sth to give too much importance to a small problem 小题大做: OK, we disagree on this but let's not make an issue of it. 好吧，我们在这一点上有分歧，可是不要小题大做。
issue²
/ˈɪʃu:;ˈɪsju: ||; ˈɪʃυ; ˈɪʃjυ/verb
1 [T] to print and supply sth 发行: to issue a magazine/newsletter 发行杂志╱简讯
2 [T] to give or say sth to sb officially 正式发给；发表: The new employees were issued with uniforms. 新员工都发给了制服。 to issue a visa 发给签证 The police will issue a statement later today. 今天晚些时候警方将发表一项声明。
3 [I] (formal 正式) to come or go out 传出；发出: An angry voice issued from the loudspeaker. 扩音器里传来一个怒气冲冲的声音。

isthmus
/ˈɪsməs ||; ˈɪsməs/noun [C] (in geography 地理学) a narrow piece of land, with water on each side, that joins two larger pieces of land 地峡

IT
/ˌaɪ ˈti: ||; ˌaɪ ˈti/abbr (computing计算机技术) Information Technology 信息技术；信息科技

*it
/ɪt ||; ɪt/pronoun
1 (used as the subject or object of a verb, or after a preposition) the animal or thing mentioned earlier （用作动词的主语、宾语，或放在介词后面）它: Look at that car. It's going much too fast. 瞧那辆汽车，它开得太快了。 The children went up to the dog and patted it. 小孩走到那只狗的身旁，用手轻拍它。 It can also refer to a baby whose sex you do not know Is it a boy or a girl? 如果不知道婴儿的性别，也可以用it：Is it a boy or a girl?是男娃娃还是女娃娃？
2 used for identifying a person （用于指出某人身分）: It's your Mum on the phone. 是你妈妈来电话。 ‘Who's that?’ ‘It's the postman.’ “是谁？”“是邮递员。” It's me! 是我！ It's him! 是他！
3 used in the position of the subject or object of a verb when the real subject or object is at the end of the sentence （用作动词的主语或宾语，而真正的主语或宾语在句末）: It's hard for them to talk about their problems. 要他们谈自身的问题并不容易。 I think it doesn't really matter what time we arrive. 依我看，我们在什么时候到达并不重要。
4 used in the position of the subject of a verb when you are talking about time, the date, distance, the weather, etc （用作动词的主语，表示时间、日期、距离或天气等）: It's nearly half past eight. 快到八点半了。 It's Tuesday today. 今天是星期二。 It's about 100 kilometres from London. 离伦敦约100公里。 It was very cold at the weekend. 上周末很冷。 It's raining. 下着雨呢。
5 used when you are talking about a situation （指某情况）: It gets very crowded here in the summer. 这儿一到夏天就人山人海。 I'll come at 7 o'clock if it's convenient. 方便的话，我7点钟来。 It's a pity they can't come to the party. 真遗憾，他们来不了这个聚会。
6 used for emphasizing a part of a sentence （用于强调句子的某一部份）: It was Jerry who said it, not me. 这话是杰里说的，不是我说的。 It's your health I'm worried about, not the cost. 我担心的是你的健康，不是费用。
that/this is it
1 that/this is the answer 对了: That's it! You've solved the puzzle! 对了！这个谜语你猜对了！
2 that/this is the end 到此为止: That's it, I've had enough! I'm going home! 好了，我受够了！我要回家了！

/ɪˈtælɪks ||; ɪˈtælɪks/noun [pl] a type of writing or printing in which the letters do not stand straight up 斜体字: All the example sentences in the dictionary are printed in italics. 本词典的所有例句都以斜体印刷。 italic adj

*item
/ˈaɪtəm ||; ˈaɪtəm/noun[C]
1 one single thing on a list or in a collection 项；项目；条目: Some items arrived too late to be included in the catalogue. 有些项目来得太晚，来不及纳入目录。 What is the first item on the agenda? 第一项议程是什么？
2 one single article or object 一件物品: Can I pay for each item separately? 我可不可以一项一项分开来付钱？ an item of clothing 一件衣物
3 a single piece of news 一条消息: There was an interesting item about Spain in yesterday's news. 昨天的新闻有一条关于西班牙的趣闻。

/ˈɪtl ||; ˈɪtḷ/ short forIT WILL

it's
/ɪts ||; ɪts/ short forIT IS; IT HAS Be careful. It's is a short way of saying it is or it has. Its means ‘belonging to it’ The bird has broken its wing. 注意：it's为it is及it has的缩写形式，its表示“它的”﹕The bird has broken its wing.小鸟的翅膀折断了。

*its
/ɪts ||; ɪts/det of or belonging to a thing 它的: The club held its Annual General Meeting last night. 俱乐部昨晚举行年度大会。 ☞Look at the note at it's. 参看it's的注释。

*itself
/ɪtˈself ||; ɪtˈsɛlf/pronoun
1 used when the animal or thing that does an action is also affected by it （表示动物或事物受自己行为影响）它自己: The cat was washing itself. 猫儿在清洁自己。 The company has got itself into financial difficulties. 这家公司陷入财务困境。
2 used to emphasize sth （用于强调）它本身: The building itself is beautiful, but it's in a very ugly part of town. 这大楼本身相当漂亮，可是所在的城区却很难看。
(all) by itself
1 without being controlled by a person; automatically 自动: The central heating comes on by itself before we get up. 我们起床之前，中央暖气已经自动启动了。
2 alone 单独；独自: The house stood all by itself on the hillside. 这座房子孤零零地座落在山腰上。 ☞ Look at the note at alone. 参看alone的注释。
